## Processed Chapters

### Chapter 1: First Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 1-6
- Source PDF pages: 7, 8, 9
- Printed page numbers: 11, 12, 13
- Key entities: Narayana, Valmiki, Lava, Kusha, Dasharatha, Brahma, Narada, Rama
- Places: Ayodhya, Tamasa, Ganga, Yamuna, Kosala, Sarayu

**Summary:** This chapter introduces the Ramayana, starting with creation by Narayana, the story of Valmiki's inspiration, the composition of the Ramayana, and the qualifications of Lava and Kusha to sing it. It also describes the glory of Ayodhya under King Dasharatha's rule.

#### Q1

**Question:** At the beginning of the kalpa, when Lord Narayana intended to start creation, whom did he first create by his mere will?

**Options:**
- 1. Vaivasvata Manu
- 2. Four-faced Brahma
- 3. Marichi
- 4. Narada Maharshi

**Correct answer:** Four-faced Brahma

**Key entities:** Narayana, Brahma

#### Q2

**Question:** When Valmiki Maharshi saw a Nishada killing one of a pair of Krauncha birds in the forest, on the bank of which river had he gone to bathe at that time?

**Options:**
- 1. Ganga River
- 2. Yamuna River
- 3. Narmada River
- 4. Tamasa River

**Correct answer:** Tamasa River

**Key entities:** Valmiki, Tamasa

#### Q3

**Question:** After having his doubts resolved by Narada Maharshi, with the grace of Lord Brahma, through whom did Valmiki Maharshi first propagate the Ramayana he wrote in the world?

**Answer:** Lava and Kusha

**Key entities:** Narada, Brahma, Valmiki, Lava, Kusha

#### Q4

**Question:** What was the qualification of Lava and Kusha to sing the Ramayana in Ayodhya?

**Answer:** Valmiki Maharshi taught the Ramayana, composed with all his penance, to his disciples Lava and Kusha. Having thoroughly studied the Sama Veda and possessing good musical knowledge, they sang the Ramayana beautifully with the sage's approval, adding music to the words and deep meanings. Thus, having learned all the nuances of singing from Valmiki, Lava and Kusha sang the Ramayana in various hermitages during sacrificial ceremonies, giving joy to the listeners. Later, while they were singing the Ramayana in the streets of Ayodhya, Lord Rama heard them and, during his Ashvamedha sacrifice, summoned them and had them sing the Ramayana before him.

**Key entities:** Lava, Kusha, Ayodhya, Valmiki, Rama

#### Q5

**Question:** During the reign of King Dasharatha, what was the splendor of the Kosala kingdom's capital, Ayodhya?

**Answer:** The Kosala kingdom, situated on the banks of the Sarayu River, abounded in wealth, grains, and all riches. The city of Ayodhya, built by the Prajapati Vaivasvata Manu, was the capital. During the reign of King Dasharatha, Ayodhya was impregnable to enemies, surrounded by high ramparts, deep moats outside the walls, and wide royal roads on all four sides of the fort, with shops on both sides, making it beautiful to behold. The city was filled with scholars, warriors, those who maintained the sacred fire, people endowed with virtues like self-control and tranquility, experts in Vedic studies, and truth-speakers. King Dasharatha was well-versed in the meanings of the Vedas, honored the brave and learned with wealth and grains, and kept them under his control. He was also a knower of future events. The people of Ayodhya were devoted to performing their respective duties. Thus, King Dasharatha, endowed with a fourfold army, righteously ruled the prosperous Kosala empire.

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Kosala, Ayodhya, Sarayu

### Chapter 2: Second Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 7-12
- Source PDF pages: 9, 10, 11
- Printed page numbers: 13, 14, 15
- Key entities: Dasharatha, Rishyashringa, Romapada, Vasishta, Sumantra, Vishvamitra, Jabali, Shanta
- Places: Ayodhya, Kosala

**Summary:** King Dasharatha, childless, seeks advice on performing a sacrifice for progeny. He invites sage Rishyashringa to Ayodhya with the help of King Romapada of Anga. Preparations for the Ashvamedha sacrifice begin under the guidance of Rishyashringa and sage Vashishta.

#### Q1

**Question:** How many ministers did King Dasharatha, who ruled the Kosala kingdom, have?

**Options:**
- 1. Seven
- 2. Ten
- 3. Eight
- 4. Nine

**Correct answer:** Eight

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Kosala

#### Q2

**Question:** Who advised Dasharatha to first invite and bring Rishyashringa for the sacrifice he intended to perform for obtaining sons due to lack of progeny?

**Options:**
- 1. Sumantra
- 2. Vashishta
- 3. Vishvamitra
- 4. Jabali

**Correct answer:** Sumantra

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Rishyashringa, Sumantra

#### Q3

**Question:** When King Dasharatha went with all his people to invite sage Rishyashringa to Ayodhya, where was sage Rishyashringa at that time?

**Answer:** In Anga kingdom

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Rishyashringa, Ayodhya

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Rishyashringa's arrival in Ayodhya take place?

**Answer:** King Dasharatha, along with all his queens and royal retinue, set out and visited King Romapada of Anga, receiving special honors. Then he met sage Rishyashringa. After staying in Anga for a week, Dasharatha told Romapada: 'O king, send your daughter Shanta and your son-in-law Rishyashringa to my city. A great task is to be performed there. I am inviting this couple to participate in it.' Romapada accepted Dasharatha's invitation and told Rishyashringa: 'O sage, accept King Dasharatha's invitation and go to Ayodhya with your wife Shanta, accompanying Dasharatha.' Rishyashringa agreed and, with his wife, set out with Dasharatha and reached Ayodhya. Dasharatha reverently worshipped Rishyashringa who came to his palace. Shanta and Rishyashringa stayed happily in Ayodhya for some time.

**Key entities:** Rishyashringa, Ayodhya, Dasharatha, Romapada, Shanta

#### Q5

**Question:** What arrangements did King Dasharatha make for the sacrifice he had undertaken?

**Answer:** At the beginning of the spring season, King Dasharatha intended to start the Ashvamedha sacrifice. First, he bowed to sage Rishyashringa and requested him to be the chief priest for the sacrifice meant for the prosperity of his dynasty. Rishyashringa accepted the king's request and told him to prepare the sacrificial materials. Then Dasharatha, pleased, summoned his intimate minister Sumantra and said, 'Go quickly and bring Vashishta and other preceptors and priests.' According to the king's order, Sumantra went quickly and brought them all. King Dasharatha duly worshipped the arrived preceptors and priests and requested sage Vashishta, 'O revered one, desiring the elevation of our dynasty, please ensure that the sacrificial task I have undertaken proceeds without obstacles.' Then all of them said to the king, 'Let it be as per your command!' and agreed to perform their respective duties in the conduct of the sacrifice along with sage Rishyashringa.

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Rishyashringa, Sumantra, Vasishta

### Chapter 3: Third Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 13-18
- Source PDF pages: 11, 12, 13
- Printed page numbers: 15, 16, 17
- Key entities: Dasharatha, Vishnu, Kausalya, Kaikeyi, Sumitra, Rama, Bharata, Lakshmana, Shatrughna, Vasishta, Narayana, Ravana, Brahma
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** King Dasharatha performs the Ashwamedha yajna and then the Putrakameshti yajna to obtain sons. The gods, pleased with the offerings, decide to incarnate as Vanaras and bears to assist Vishnu, who will be born as Dasharatha's sons. In due time, Kausalya, Kaikeyi, and Sumitra give birth to Rama, Bharata, Lakshmana, and Shatrughna. The sage Vashishta names them. The princes grow up, excelling in learning and archery. One day, sage Vishwamitra visits Dasharatha's court.

#### Q1

**Question:** On which tithi, determined by the Ritvijs, did Dasharatha release the sacrificial horse after performing all the yajna rites?

**Options:**
- 1. Chaitra Shuddha Navami
- 2. Chaitra Shuddha Purnima
- 3. Chaitra Shuddha Dashami
- 4. Chaitra Shuddha Ekadashi

**Correct answer:** Chaitra Shuddha Purnima

**Key entities:** Dasharatha

#### Q2

**Question:** After the sacrificial horse returned and Dasharatha completed the Ashwamedha yajna according to scripture, which yajna did he perform for the sake of obtaining sons?

**Options:**
- 1. Vishwajit Yajna
- 2. Vajapeya Yajna
- 3. Putrakameshti Yajna
- 4. Ishti Yajna

**Correct answer:** Putrakameshti Yajna

**Key entities:** Dasharatha

#### Q3

**Question:** In what form did the divine being appear at the yajna vedika and deliver the fruit of the yajna to Dasharatha?

**Answer:** In the form of Payasa (a sweet porridge)

**Key entities:** Dasharatha

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the gods, satisfied with the offerings given by Dasharatha, decide in accordance with future developments?

**Answer:** All the gods who had gathered at the yajna thought about the terrible atrocities of the demons and sought refuge in Narayana. At the request of all the gods, Narayana decided to incarnate on earth to destroy Ravana and other demons and protect the devotees. Brahma commanded all the gods to be born with their respective aspects to assist him. Thus, thousands of Vanaras, bears, and monkeys were born with divine aspects. Mahavishnu decided to be born as four sons to Dasharatha. After the yajna concluded, Dasharatha happily lived with his three pregnant queens, and a year passed.

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Narayana, Ravana, Brahma

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Dasharatha's joy over his sons unfold?

**Answer:** Among the three pregnant queens, the senior queen Kausalya gave birth to a male child at the beginning of spring, on Chaitra Shuddha Navami, in the fourth quarter of the Punarvasu nakshatra, under the zodiac sign of Cancer. Then on Chaitra Shuddha Dashami, Queen Kaikeyi gave birth to a male child. Later that same day, Sumitra gave birth to twin male children. Eleven days after the sons were born, Dasharatha performed the Jatakarma and naming ceremonies, gave generous gifts to the deserving, and rejoiced. Sage Vashishta came and named the eldest Rama, Kaikeyi's son Bharata, and Sumitra's sons Lakshmana and Shatrughna. Dasharatha, who had been without children for a long time, spent his time in great joy with his four sons. Among them, his love for the eldest Rama was greater than his own life. He had the four princes study the Vedas and scriptures under a guru. They became proficient in archery and were devoted to the welfare of the people. Rama, the great scion of the Raghu dynasty, possessed invincible valor. From childhood, Lakshmana was devoted to his elder brother Rama. Dasharatha was filled with supreme joy with his four sons, who were endowed with auspicious marks. Rama's childhood passed joyfully with his brothers, and they all became youths. One day, while Dasharatha was holding court, sage Vishwamitra arrived. Dasharatha welcomed the sage and worshipped him appropriately.

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Kausalya, Kaikeyi, Sumitra, Vasishta, Rama, Bharata, Lakshmana, Shatrughna

### Chapter 4: Fourth Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 19-24
- Source PDF pages: 13, 14, 15
- Printed page numbers: 17, 18, 19
- Key entities: Dasharatha, Rama, Vasishta, Lakshmana, Shiva, Tataka, Maricha, Shatrughna, Bharata, Sumantra, Jabali, Kausalya, Indra
- Places: Sarayu, Ganga

**Summary:** Visvamitra asks King Dasaratha to send Rama to protect his sacrifice. Dasaratha initially hesitates but agrees on the advice of Vasistha. Rama and Lakshmana accompany Visvamitra, who teaches them the Bala and Atibala mantras. They travel to the confluence of Sarayu and Ganga, where Visvamitra narrates the story of the place, including Shiva's destruction of Manmatha. They then cross the Ganga and enter a forest, where Visvamitra tells the story of the demoness Tataka and her son Maricha, who have devastated the Malada and Karusha kingdoms.

#### Q1

**Question:** Whom did Visvamitra ask King Dasaratha to send with him for the protection of the sacrifice he had undertaken?

**Options:**
- 1. Shatrughna
- 2. Lakshmana
- 3. Bharata
- 4. Rama

**Correct answer:** Rama

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Following Visvamitra's request, Dasaratha expressed his inability to send his eldest son Rama. On whose advice did he agree?

**Options:**
- 1. Sumantra
- 2. Vasistha
- 3. Jabali
- 4. Kausalya

**Correct answer:** Vasistha

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Rama, Vasishta

#### Q3

**Question:** When Rama and Lakshmana, following Visvamitra, were stopped by the sage at a place south of the Sarayu river, what were the names of the vidyas (knowledge) he taught them?

**Answer:** Bala and Atibala

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Sarayu

#### Q4

**Question:** Rama and Lakshmana rested on the banks of the Sarayu. Waking up at dawn, they traveled some distance and reached a place. How did Visvamitra answer their doubt when they asked about it?

**Answer:** Rama and Lakshmana, traveling with their guru, saw the holy confluence of the Sarayu and Ganga. There, sages had been performing penance for thousands of years. The princes asked Visvamitra, 'O great sage! Whose is this holy hermitage? Who are the great men living here? Tell us its ancient history.' Then the sage said, 'O Rama! In ancient times, Lord Shiva performed penance here. Once, Manmatha (Kamadeva) tried to disturb Shiva's penance. Shiva looked angrily, and Manmatha was burnt to ashes in that fiery gaze. Since then, Manmatha became bodiless and was called Ananga. Because Kama (desire) abandoned his body (anga), this region became Angadesha. All the ascetics here are devoted to Shiva. O princes! Let us spend this night at this holy confluence of Ganga and Sarayu. Tomorrow we can cross the Ganga.' Thus they all rested there.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Sarayu, Ganga, Shiva

#### Q5

**Question:** After crossing the Ganga, Rama and Lakshmana traveled some distance and saw a terrible forest. When they asked Visvamitra about its history, how did the sage explain?

**Answer:** Visvamitra said to Rama, 'My son! In ancient times, this place consisted of two kingdoms called Malada and Karusha. They were prosperous with wealth and grain. After some time, a yakshini named Tataka, who had the strength of a thousand elephants from birth, roamed here assuming any form she wished. She was the wife of the powerful Sunda. She had a son named Maricha, who was as strong as Indra. The wicked Tataka constantly destroyed the two kingdoms of Malada and Karusha, making them devoid of human habitation. Since then, this area became a desolate forest. O Rama! Do not fear; you will be safe. Now we must cross this Tataka forest.' Saying this, Visvamitra walked ahead, and Rama and Lakshmana followed.

**Key entities:** Ganga, Rama, Lakshmana, Tataka, Maricha, Indra

### Chapter 5: Fifth Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 25-30
- Source PDF pages: 15, 16, 17
- Printed page numbers: 19, 20, 21
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Tataka, Maricha, Subahu, Agastya, Vali, Indra
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** Rama and Lakshmana accompany Vishwamitra to protect his yajna. Rama kills the demoness Tataka, receives celestial weapons from Vishwamitra, and later kills the demons Maricha and Subahu during the yajna. Vishwamitra explains the history of Siddhashrama.

#### Q1

**Question:** Which great sage cursed the yakshini Tataka, saying 'Because of various reasons you have come to devour me, you shall become a terrible demoness living on human flesh'?

**Options:**
- 1. Agastya
- 2. Vishwamitra
- 3. Vasishtha
- 4. Jamadagni

**Correct answer:** Agastya

**Key entities:** Tataka, Agastya

#### Q2

**Question:** Following the command of Sage Vishwamitra, at what time did Rama slay Tataka?

**Options:**
- 1. As midday approached
- 2. As the first twilight approached
- 3. As the last twilight approached
- 4. At night

**Correct answer:** As the last twilight approached

**Key entities:** Rama, Tataka

#### Q3

**Question:** Vishwamitra, greatly pleased with the slaying of Tataka, graciously gave Rama various celestial weapons along with their mantras of invocation and dismissal. Later, who taught all those weapons to Lakshmana?

**Answer:** 

**Key entities:** Tataka, Rama, Lakshmana

#### Q4

**Question:** When Rama asked about the history of Siddhashrama, how did Vishwamitra explain it to him?

**Answer:** Vishwamitra, upon being asked by Rama, explained about Siddhashrama: 'Rama! Lord Mahavishnu performed penance here for ages. The great ascetic Kashyapa attained perfection here. It was here that Mahavishnu, born as Vamana to Aditi and Kashyapa, begged three steps of land from King Bali. Then, becoming Trivikrama, the all-pervading Supreme Self, by his power sent Bali to the netherworld and gave heaven to Indra. This place is sanctified by the touch of the great Vamana's feet. Hence it is called Siddhashrama. That is why I have taken refuge here. My son Rama! Demons who create obstacles come to this hermitage. It is here that you must slay those wicked ones.' As soon as Sage Vishwamitra entered the hermitage, the sages residing in Siddhashrama welcomed and honored Vishwamitra, Rama, and Lakshmana.

**Key entities:** Rama, Vali, Indra, Lakshmana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Rama and Lakshmana protect the yajna conducted by Vishwamitra?

**Answer:** Rama and Lakshmana said to Vishwamitra, who was initiated into the yajna, 'O Brahmarshi! When will the demons who create obstacles to the yajna come? We will remain vigilant to stop them.' Hearing this, the sages there rejoiced and told them, 'From today, for six days, Sage Vishwamitra will observe a vow of silence. O princes! You must remain alert and protect the yajna for these six days.' Then Rama and Lakshmana, bearing bows and arrows, guarded the yajna for five days. On the sixth day, as the yajna was proceeding properly with Vedic mantras, a terrible sound was heard from the sky. The fearsome demons Maricha and Subahu, along with their followers, came there using their illusions and scattered blood and flesh on the sacrificial altar. Then Rama of the Raghu dynasty, using the human weapon called 'Shiteshu', struck Maricha so that he fell into the ocean. Then, using the Agneya weapon, he killed Subahu. After Rama also killed some other demons who were obstacles to the yajna, all the blood and flesh scattered on the altar, being illusions of the demons, vanished from sight. After the yajna was completed without hindrance, Vishwamitra congratulated and blessed Rama and Lakshmana. Thus Rama protected the yajna.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Maricha, Subahu

### Chapter 6: Sixth Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 31-36
- Source PDF pages: 17, 18, 19, 20
- Printed page numbers: 21, 22, 23, 24
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Kusha, Parvati, Vishvamitra, Brahma, Menaka, Shiva
- Places: Mithila, Ganga

**Summary:** After the completion of the sacrifice, following Vishwamitra's suggestion, Rama and Lakshmana set out for Sita's swayamvara in Mithila. They travel north, stopping at the Shona River. Rama asks Vishwamitra about the region, leading Vishwamitra to narrate his lineage, including the story of Kusha, Kushanabha, and his own birth. Later, at the Ganges, Vishwamitra recounts the stories of Ganga and Parvati, and the descent of the Ganges due to Bhagiratha.

#### Q1

**Question:** After the completion of the sacrifice, following Vishwamitra's suggestion, Rama and Lakshmana set out for Sita's swayamvara in Mithila. In which direction did they travel from Siddhashrama?

**Options:**
- 1. East
- 2. South
- 3. West
- 4. North

**Correct answer:** North

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Mithila

#### Q2

**Question:** All those traveling with Vishwamitra reached the banks of the Shona River by evening and rested there. Then Rama bowed to Vishwamitra and asked, 'O Guru! Under whose rule is this place where we are now?' Whose rule did Vishwamitra say the place was under?

**Options:**
- 1. Kusha
- 2. Kushanabha
- 3. Vasu
- 4. Adhurtarajas

**Correct answer:** Vasu

**Key entities:** Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** While answering Rama's question, Vishwamitra, in the course of telling the story of his ancestor Kushanabha's daughters, revealed who the progenitor of his lineage was?

**Answer:** Kaushika

**Key entities:** Rama, Vishvamitra

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Sage Vishwamitra describe the history of his lineage to Rama on the banks of the Shona River?

**Answer:** O Rama! Brahma's mind-born son is Kusha. His son Kushanabha had a hundred daughters, whom he married to Bhagadatta, the king of Kampilya, and sent them to their in-laws' house. Later, the king, to compensate for the lack of sons, performed the Putrakameshti sacrifice. After some time, Kushanabha, through his wife Ghritachi, obtained a son named Gadhi. This Gadhi was highly righteous. The righteous king Gadhi is my father. Because I was born in the Kusha lineage, I am also called Kaushika. O Rama! Satyavati is my elder sister. She was married to the sage Richika. Since my sister was also born in the Kusha lineage, she is also called Kaushiki. Because she was a great pativrata, she followed her husband and went to heaven with her physical body. Later, as the supremely generous Kaushiki, she flows as a great river on this earth. Out of my love for my elder sister, I reside on the banks of the Kaushiki River. O Rama! For the purpose of performing a sacrifice, I came here from that region. By your valor in Siddhashrama, I have become fulfilled and am returning. In telling you about the special features of this region, I have also told you about my lineage. Thus the sage concluded.

**Key entities:** Rama, Brahma, Kusha, Vishvamitra

#### Q5

**Question:** Where and how did Vishwamitra describe the special features of Ganga and Parvati to Sri Rama?

**Answer:** Following Vishwamitra, Rama and others traveled some distance and reached the banks of the holy Ganges by midday. After completing their baths in the holy Ganges and offering libations to the ancestors, Rama asked about the story of the Ganges. Vishwamitra said: O Rama! Menaka and Himavan had two daughters. The elder daughter is Ganga Devi, and the second daughter is Parvati Devi. Once, the gods, for their own purpose, asked Himavan to hand over Ganga to them. The righteous Himavan, for the welfare of the world, handed over Ganga, who flows everywhere, to them. The second daughter, Parvati Devi, while still a maiden, performed severe penance, desiring to obtain Shankara as her husband through her vow. Himavan, according to his daughter's wish, gave her in marriage to Parama Shiva. Born as a daughter to Himavan and reaching the heavens, this holy Ganga is this Ganges river. Pleased with Vishwamitra's narration of the Ganga story, Rama asked: O Sage! How did this Ganges river come to be called Tripathaga? Then Kaushika told the story of the birth of Kumaraswami and also explained how Ganga descended from heaven to earth due to Bhagiratha. Thus Vishwamitra fully narrated the story of the Ganges as asked by Rama.

**Key entities:** Ganga, Parvati, Rama, Menaka, Shiva, Vishvamitra

### Chapter 7: Seventh Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 37-42
- Source PDF pages: 20, 21, 22
- Printed page numbers: 24, 25, 26
- Key entities: Indra, Brahma, Narayana, Shiva
- Places: Ganga, Himalaya

**Summary:** This chapter covers the story of King Sagara's horse sacrifice, the theft of the horse by Indra, the search by Sagara's 60,000 sons, their destruction by Kapila's anger, and the eventual retrieval of the horse by Anshuman. It also includes the efforts of Anshuman, Dilipa, and Bhagiratha to bring the Ganges to earth to purify the ashes of Sagara's sons.

#### Q1

**Question:** At the request of all the gods, whom did Lord Brahma appoint as their commander?

**Options:**
- 1. Vighneshwara
- 2. Kumaraswami
- 3. Nandishwara
- 4. Vishvaksena

**Correct answer:** Kumaraswami

**Key entities:** Brahma

#### Q2

**Question:** Because he had no children, Emperor Sagara went to the Himalayas with his two wives and performed penance for whom?

**Options:**
- 1. Parashiva
- 2. Lord Brahma
- 3. Bhrigu Maharshi
- 4. Narayana

**Correct answer:** Bhrigu Maharshi

**Key entities:** Himalaya

#### Q3

**Question:** During the Ashwamedha sacrifice, who stole the horse released by Emperor Sagara?

**Answer:** Indra

**Key entities:** Indra

#### Q4

**Question:** After the sacrificial horse was stolen, what effort did Sagara make to search for the horse?

**Answer:** Following the words of the priests who said that without the sacrificial horse the sacrifice would not be completed and calamity would occur, Sagara summoned his sixty thousand sons and said, 'Dear sons! Because I am in the vow of the sacrifice, I cannot come. Therefore, go and search for the sacrificial horse. Search everywhere on earth; if not found, dig the earth and go to the netherworld and search. May you be blessed.' Thus he sent them. They all set out and searched everywhere on earth, but they did not find any trace of the horse. Then, each dividing one yojana, they dug the earth and reached the netherworld. There, seeing the sacrificial horse near the hermitage of Kapila Maharshi, they thought that the sage himself had stolen the horse and insulted Kapila. Angered by their rude words and behavior, Kapila Maharshi roared. By Kapila's roar, Sagara's sons were burnt to ashes. Thus Sagara's effort failed.

**Key entities:** None listed

#### Q5

**Question:** Who brought back Sagara's sacrificial horse and in what manner, completing the sacrifice? What became of Sagara's sons who lay as heaps of ashes?

**Answer:** King Sagara, worried that his sons had not returned for a long time, summoned his grandson Anshuman and said, 'Dear son! Your uncles went in search of the sacrificial horse and have not returned. You go and search for your uncles and the sacrificial horse and bring them back to complete the sacrifice.' Immediately, Anshuman obeyed his grandfather's command and followed the path his uncles had taken by digging the earth to the netherworld. There, in the hermitage of Kapila Maharshi, he saw all his relatives lying as heaps of ashes. Following the suggestion of Garutman, he took the sacrificial horse and completed the sacrifice. Then Anshuman informed his grandfather Sagara that his uncles had been reduced to ashes by Kapila's anger, and to grant them the attainment of the world of ancestors, the sacred celestial Ganga had to be brought to earth. Thereafter, Sagara, thinking about the attainment of the higher worlds for his sons, passed away. Subsequently, Anshuman and Dilipa successively tried to bring Ganga to earth for the salvation of their ancestors, but their efforts failed. Finally, Dilipa's son Bhagiratha prayed to Lord Brahma, Ganga, and Shiva. Pleased with his penance, Brahma bore Ganga and released her onto the earth. Ganga followed Bhagiratha and moistened the ashes of the king's ancestors, granting them the worlds of ancestors. Thus, due to Bhagiratha, his ancestors attained the higher worlds.

**Key entities:** Ganga, Brahma, Shiva

### Chapter 8: Eighth Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 43-49
- Source PDF pages: 22, 23, 24
- Printed page numbers: 26, 27, 28
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Gautama, Ahalya, Shiva, Indra, Dasharatha
- Places: Ganga, Kailasa, Mithila, Himalaya

**Summary:** This chapter covers the journey of Vishwamitra, Rama, and Lakshmana. They cross the Ganga, visit Vishala city, and proceed to Gautama's hermitage. The story of Ahalya's curse and liberation is narrated. The chapter also includes the tale of Diti's pregnancy and the Maruts.

#### Q1

**Question:** Where did Lord Shiva release the Ganga from his matted locks after hearing Bhagiratha's plea?

**Options:**
- 1. Kanchana Ganga
- 2. Kailasa Mountain
- 3. Bindu Sarovara
- 4. Kedarnath

**Correct answer:** Bindu Sarovara

**Key entities:** Shiva, Ganga

#### Q2

**Question:** After crossing the Ganga, Vishwamitra and others traveled north and reached a city. At Rama's request, Vishwamitra described that city. What is its name?

**Options:**
- 1. Kashi
- 2. Avanti
- 3. Dwaraka
- 4. Vishala

**Correct answer:** Vishala

**Key entities:** Ganga, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** To obtain a son capable of killing Indra, Diti conceived with her husband Kashyapa Prajapati's permission. Knowing this, Indra entered her womb and cut the fetus into seven pieces. Later, those body parts became deities by Indra's grace. What are they called in the world?

**Answer:** Sapta Maruts

**Key entities:** Indra

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Vishwamitra describe Gautama's hermitage to Rama when asked?

**Answer:** While traveling from Vishala towards Mithila, Vishwamitra and his group saw an ancient hermitage. Rama asked Vishwamitra, 'O great one! Whose is this ancient hermitage?' Vishwamitra replied, 'O best of men! This is the hermitage of the great sage Gautama. It once shone with divine splendor and was worshipped by the gods. Once, Gautama performed penance here for many years with his wife Ahalya. When Gautama was away, Indra came disguised as Gautama and enjoyed conjugal bliss with Ahalya. Knowing this, Gautama cursed Indra to be without testicles. He told Ahalya, 'You shall perform penance here for some years, unseen by anyone. Later, Rama, son of King Dasharatha, will come to this hermitage. As soon as he sets foot here, you will become pure. Then all your greed and delusion will vanish, and you will be purified and join me.' Saying this, Gautama went to the Himalayas to perform penance.' Thus Vishwamitra told Rama about Gautama's hermitage.

**Key entities:** Gautama, Rama, Mithila, Ahalya, Indra, Dasharatha, Himalaya

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Ahalya's liberation from the curse occur?

**Answer:** After describing Gautama's hermitage, Vishwamitra told Rama, 'O prince! You bring about Ahalya's liberation from the curse.' Then Rama, following Vishwamitra's command, entered Gautama's hermitage with Lakshmana and Vishwamitra. There, Rama saw Ahalya, who was radiant due to severe austerities like subsisting on air. Due to Gautama's curse, she was invisible to all until she saw Rama. Upon seeing Rama, she was freed from the curse and became visible to everyone. Then Ahalya bowed to Rama and Lakshmana and offered them arghya and other honors. Then Gautama himself appeared and, along with Ahalya, worshipped Rama and was pleased. Thereafter, Gautama continued his ascetic life in his hermitage with Ahalya. Then Rama, with Lakshmana, set out for Mithila with Vishwamitra.

**Key entities:** Ahalya, Gautama, Rama, Lakshmana, Mithila

### Chapter 9: Ninth Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 50-56
- Source PDF pages: 24, 25, 26
- Printed page numbers: 28, 29, 30
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Janaka, Ahalya, Gautama, Shatananda, Sumantra, Jabali, Shiva
- Places: Mithila

**Summary:** Rama and Lakshmana, accompanying Vishwamitra, arrive in Mithila and receive hospitality from King Janaka. They meet the son of Ahalya and Gautama. The chapter recounts Vishwamitra's past conflict with Vasishtha over the divine cow Shabala, leading to Vishwamitra's loss of his sons and army, his subsequent penance to obtain divine weapons, and his failed attack on Vasishtha's hermitage, after which he renounces Kshatriya pride and turns to intense asceticism.

#### Q1

**Question:** Rama and Lakshmana, who reached Mithila with Vishwamitra, accepted the hospitality of King Janaka and there they met the son of Ahalya and Gautama. What is his name?

**Options:**
- 1. Sudhamanu
- 2. Shatananda
- 3. Sumantra
- 4. Jabali

**Correct answer:** Shatananda

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Mithila, Janaka, Ahalya, Gautama, Shatananda

#### Q2

**Question:** In Mithila, who told Sri Rama about the past history of Vishwamitra?

**Options:**
- 1. Shatananda
- 2. Janaka
- 3. Kushadhwaja
- 4. Sudhamanu

**Correct answer:** Shatananda

**Key entities:** Mithila, Rama, Shatananda

#### Q3

**Question:** King Vishwamitra came to Vasishtha's hermitage with his retinue, accepted the hospitality given by the great sage, was pleased, and asked Vasishtha for the cow that was the cause of such hospitality. What is the name of that cow?

**Answer:** Shabala

**Key entities:** None listed

#### Q4

**Question:** When Vasishtha refused the cow, what did Vishwamitra do? What happened subsequently?

**Answer:** Vishwamitra, seeing that Vasishtha had arranged food for him and his retinue by mere will, was astonished and asked for the wish-fulfilling cow named Shabala, offering a hundred thousand cows in exchange. Vasishtha did not agree, so Vishwamitra tried to take the cow by force. With Vasishtha's permission, Shabala created thousands of armies from her bellow. While Vishwamitra watched, his entire army was destroyed by Shabala's forces. Vishwamitra mounted his chariot and used various weapons to scatter Shabala's armies. Then the wish-fulfilling cow created immensely powerful armies from her body parts, which destroyed Vishwamitra's army. Seeing this, Vishwamitra's hundred sons attacked Vasishtha, but the sage reduced them to ashes with a roar. Thus Vishwamitra's attempt failed.

**Key entities:** None listed

#### Q5

**Question:** After being defeated by Vasishtha, what did Vishwamitra do next?

**Answer:** Vishwamitra, with his sons and all his forces destroyed, became powerless like a snake with its fangs removed. Overcome with despair, he went to his kingdom, handed over the kingdom to his one son who followed Kshatriya dharma, and went to perform penance. He performed severe penance in the Himalayan region, meditating on Shiva. Pleased with his austerity, Shiva appeared and asked him to wish for anything. Vishwamitra then asked for the secrets of the Upanishads and the mastery of all weapons possessed by gods, demons, sages, Gandharvas, Yakshas, and Rakshasas. Receiving that boon from Shiva, he became arrogant and went to Vasishtha's hermitage to take revenge. There he used his weapon power to destroy the hermitage. Seeing this, the sages and Vasishtha's disciples fled in all directions. Then Vasishtha, angry, said, 'O fool! You have destroyed the hermitage that was flourishing with flowers and fruit trees for a long time. What is your Kshatriya strength before my Brahmin strength?' and stood holding his staff. Vishwamitra, enraged, released all the weapons under his control one by one. But all of Vishwamitra's weapons became powerless in the shadow of Vasishtha's staff. Seeing this, Vishwamitra exclaimed, 'Fie! Is Kshatriya strength any strength? Brahminical splendor is the true strength.' He renounced his Kshatriya anger, controlled his mind and senses, and went to lead a life of intense penance.

**Key entities:** Shiva

### Chapter 10: Tenth Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 57-62
- Source PDF pages: 26, 27, 28
- Printed page numbers: 30, 31, 32
- Key entities: Vasishta, Trishanku, Brahma, Indra, Ambarisha, Agni
- Places: Ayodhya

**Summary:** This chapter narrates the story of Vishwamitra's penance, his conflict with Vasishta, and his assistance to King Trishanku and Shunashepa. Vishwamitra, after being called a Rajarshi by Brahma, helps Trishanku ascend to heaven with his body, and later saves Shunashepa from being sacrificed.

#### Q1

**Question:** Disturbed due to his enmity with Vasishta, Vishwamitra went south with a firm resolve and performed severe penance for Brahma. When the Grandfather (Brahma) appeared, what rishi did he recognize Vishwamitra as?

**Options:**
- 1. Brahmarshi
- 2. Rajarshi
- 3. Devarshi
- 4. Maharshi

**Correct answer:** Rajarshi

**Key entities:** Vasishta, Brahma

#### Q2

**Question:** When King Trishanku, the lord of Ayodhya, requested a sacrifice to ascend to heaven with his physical body, how did the angry sons of Vasishta curse him?

**Options:**
- 1. Become a Chandala
- 2. Become an animal
- 3. Become a stone
- 4. Be deprived of your kingdom

**Correct answer:** Become a Chandala

**Key entities:** Trishanku, Ayodhya, Vasishta

#### Q3

**Question:** Whom did Trishanku, who received the curse from the guru's sons, approach?

**Answer:** Vishwamitra

**Key entities:** Trishanku

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Vishwamitra welcome Trishanku who sought his refuge?

**Answer:** Trishanku, rejected by Vasishta and his sons, sought refuge with Vishwamitra. Vishwamitra, despite Trishanku being rejected by his enemy, welcomed him and decided to perform the sacrifice as per his wish. He called his sons and ordered them to gather the necessary materials. Then he sent his disciples to invite all rishis, their disciples, priests, and Vedic scholars. Everyone came as per Vishwamitra's command. Vishwamitra said that they should all perform the sacrifice and send Trishanku to heaven with his body. They agreed and performed the sacrifice according to the scriptures. As a result, Trishanku went to heaven with his body. There, Indra, due to the curse of the guru, said Trishanku was unworthy of heaven and threw him headlong from heaven. Knowing this, Vishwamitra, with his power, stopped Trishanku in the sky, created another heaven, and declared that this heaven would be Trishanku's abode and that all gods should agree. All gods agreed. Vishwamitra placed Trishanku in the heaven he created and completed the sacrifice with his patronage.

**Key entities:** Trishanku, Vasishta, Indra

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Vishwamitra save Shunashepa, who was going as a sacrificial animal for King Ambarisha?

**Answer:** Once, King Ambarisha of Ayodhya started a sacrifice. Indra stole the sacrificial animal. The priest told the king that due to his negligence the animal was stolen, and if it could not be brought back, he could offer cows as substitute and obtain a human as a sacrificial animal. As part of that effort, Ambarisha visited Rishi Ruchika and gave him a hundred thousand cows, obtaining his second son Shunashepa as a sacrificial animal. On the way, Shunashepa sought refuge with his maternal uncle Vishwamitra. By the power of the mantra given by the sage, at the conclusion of the sacrifice, Shunashepa worshipped Agni and praised Indra and Upendra. Then Indra, pleased, granted long life to Shunashepa and the fruit of the sacrifice to Ambarisha. Thus, by Vishwamitra's instruction, Shunashepa was saved from danger.

**Key entities:** Ambarisha, Ayodhya, Indra, Agni

### Chapter 11: Eleventh Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 63-67
- Source PDF pages: 28, 29, 30, 31
- Printed page numbers: 32, 33, 34, 35
- Key entities: Shiva, Sita, Rama, Menaka, Shatananda, Brahma, Vasishta, Janaka, Lakshmana, Dasharatha
- Places: Ayodhya, Mithila

**Summary:** This chapter continues the story of Vishwamitra's penance and his attainment of Brahmarshi status. It also describes the history of Shiva's bow, Sita's birth, and the breaking of the bow by Rama during Sita's swayamvara.

#### Q1

**Question:** Who was the incomparably beautiful apsara who disrupted Vishwamitra's penance at Pushkara Tirtha?

**Options:**
- 1. Punjakasthala
- 2. Urvashi
- 3. Menaka
- 4. Tilottama

**Correct answer:** Menaka

**Key entities:** Menaka

#### Q2

**Question:** While describing Vishwamitra's story to Rama, Shatananda said that Brahma declared Vishwamitra a Brahmarshi. In which direction was Vishwamitra performing penance when that declaration occurred?

**Options:**
- 1. South
- 2. West
- 3. North
- 4. East

**Correct answer:** East

**Key entities:** Rama, Shatananda, Brahma

#### Q3

**Question:** After Brahma granted him Brahmarshi status, Vishwamitra said that he would cease his penance if someone called him 'Brahmarshi'.

**Answer:** Vashishta

**Key entities:** Brahma, Vasishta

#### Q4

**Question:** How did King Janaka explain the history of Shiva's bow and the announcement of Sita's swayamvara to Vishwamitra?

**Answer:** Vishwamitra told King Janaka: 'O king! Rama and Lakshmana, the princes of Ayodhya, wish to see the bow of Shiva that is in your house. Please show it.' Then Janaka bowed to the sage and humbly said: 'O Brahmarshi! This bow of Shiva was given by Lord Shiva to the gods after they propitiated him when he was angry and destroying Daksha's sacrifice. The gods entrusted it to Devarata, the sixth king of our Nimi dynasty. Since then, this bow has been worshipped in our house. O revered sage! Once, while plowing the earth for a sacrifice, a girl emerged from the furrow. I named her Sita and raised her. When she came of age, I announced that valor would be the bride-price and only a valiant man could marry my daughter. Many princes came and displayed their prowess, but none could even string the bow. O Brahmarshi! With your permission, I will show this powerful bow to Rama and Lakshmana. I will give my daughter to whoever strings it.' Thus Janaka explained to Vishwamitra.

**Key entities:** Janaka, Shiva, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Ayodhya

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the breaking of Shiva's bow occur during Sita's swayamvara?

**Answer:** By King Janaka's order, his ministers had the chest containing Shiva's bow brought to the assembly hall by strong soldiers. Then the king said to Vishwamitra: 'O guru! I have had the bow of Shiva brought here. The princes with you may see it.' Then Vishwamitra said: 'Rama, my son, look at this bow.' Rama approached the chest, looked at the bow, and said: 'O guru! I will touch this great bow, lift it, and string it.' Janaka and Vishwamitra agreed. Then, as thousands of onlookers watched, Rama followed the sage's command, grasped the middle of the bow, effortlessly lifted it, and stood it upright. Then that best of men strung the bow and drew it to his ear. Immediately the bow broke with a loud crack. At the sound of the bow breaking, bells jingled. Sita's body thrilled with wonder and excitement. Then King Janaka said: 'O sage! I have seen with my own eyes the valor of Rama, son of Dasaratha. I did not imagine such a heroic deed. My daughter Sita, obtaining Rama as her husband, will bring glory to both families.' Then, with the permission of Vishwamitra and Rama, Janaka sent his ministers to Ayodhya to inform King Dasaratha of the details of Sita's swayamvara and invite him to Mithila. Thus the news of the breaking of Shiva's bow spread among the citizens of Mithila and Ayodhya, and everyone rejoiced.

**Key entities:** Shiva, Sita, Janaka, Rama, Dasharatha, Ayodhya, Mithila

### Chapter 12: Twelfth Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 68-72
- Source PDF pages: 31, 32, 33
- Printed page numbers: 35, 36, 37
- Key entities: Janaka, Dasharatha, Bharata, Brahma, Rama
- Places: Ayodhya

**Summary:** King Janaka sends ministers and messengers to Ayodhya to invite King Dasaratha for the wedding. They arrive in three days. Janaka instructs Shatānanda to invite his brother Kuśadhvaja from Sāṅkāśya. At the wedding pavilion, after everyone is seated, Dasaratha requests Vasiṣṭha to recite the Ikshvaku lineage. Janaka then recites the Videha lineage. Later, Viśvāmitra proposes that Bharata and Śatrughna marry Kuśadhvaja's daughters, and Janaka agrees that all four princes marry on the same day.

#### Q1

**Question:** Carrying King Janaka's message, the ministers and messengers traveled day and night and reached Ayodhya in how many days?

**Options:**
- 1. Two days
- 2. Three days
- 3. Four days
- 4. Five days

**Correct answer:** Three days

**Key entities:** Janaka, Ayodhya

#### Q2

**Question:** Janaka called Shatānanda and ordered him to make arrangements to invite his brother, who ruled Sāṅkāśya, along with his family for the auspicious wedding. What is the name of that brother of King Janaka?

**Options:**
- 1. Mahāroma
- 2. Devarāta
- 3. Hrasvaroma
- 4. Kuśadhvaja

**Correct answer:** Kuśadhvaja

**Key entities:** Janaka

#### Q3

**Question:** After everyone was comfortably seated at the wedding pavilion, through whom did King Dasaratha have his lineage recited?

**Answer:** Through Vasiṣṭha

**Key entities:** Dasharatha

#### Q4

**Question:** How were the lineages of Ikshvaku and Videha kings described?

**Answer:** After both sides' wedding parties arrived and were seated at the wedding pavilion, at Dasaratha's request, Vasiṣṭha described the Ikshvaku lineage: Brahma's mind-born son Marīci, his son Kaśyapa, Kaśyapa's son Vaivasvata Manu, and Manu's son Ikshvaku, the first king of Ayodhya. Ikshvaku's son Kukṣi, and then the lineage continued with Triśaṅku, Māndhātā, Bharata, Sagara, Bhagīratha, Kakutstha, Raghu, Ambarīṣa, Nahuṣa, and Yayāti. Yayāti's son Nābhāga, Nābhāga's son Aja, Aja's son Daśaratha, and Daśaratha's four sons: Rāma, Bharata, Lakṣmaṇa, and Śatrughna. Then King Janaka said: 'O great sage, our lineage is also renowned. As the bride's father should also recount his lineage, listen to ours. The famous Nimi is the founder of our dynasty. His son Mithi, the builder of Mithilā and the first Janaka, hence our dynasty is called Janaka. Then our lineage prospered with many famous kings like Devarāta, Bṛhadratha, Haryaśva, Kīrtirāta, Mahāroma, and Svarṇaroma. My father Hrasvaroma handed over the kingdom to me and retired to the forest.' Thus he described his lineage.

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Brahma, Ayodhya, Bharata, Rama, Janaka

#### Q5

**Question:** How were the marriages of Lakṣmaṇa, Bharata, and Śatrughna decided?

**Answer:** After King Dasaratha arrived at Mithilā with his family and retinue at Janaka's invitation, while everyone was happily together, Sage Vasiṣṭha said to King Janaka: 'O king, it would be excellent if you give your daughters Sītā and Ūrmilā in marriage to Rāma and Lakṣmaṇa, who are born in the Ikshvaku dynasty.' Janaka bowed and agreed. After the lineages were recited, Viśvāmitra said to Janaka: 'O king, both the Ikshvaku and Videha dynasties are incomparably glorious. These marital alliances between the two families are appropriate in every way. I wish to say something: it would be good if you give your brother Kuśadhvaja's two daughters in marriage to Bharata and Śatrughna. All of Dasaratha's sons are handsome and youthful, so this marriage alliance will be beneficial for both families.' Hearing Viśvāmitra's words spoken with Vasiṣṭha's consent, King Janaka humbly folded his hands and said: 'O great sages, may your words, spoken for our welfare, come true. So be it. Let these four valiant princes marry these princesses on the same day.' Thus he gave his consent.

**Key entities:** Bharata, Dasharatha, Janaka

### Chapter 13: Thirteenth Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 73-77
- Source PDF pages: 33, 34, 35, 36
- Printed page numbers: 37, 38, 39, 40
- Key entities: Rama, Sita, Parashurama, Dasharatha, Janaka, Shatananda, Urmila, Mandavi, Shrutakirti, Kushadhvaja, Shiva, Narayana, Vishnu
- Places: Ayodhya

**Summary:** The chapter describes the wedding ceremonies of Rama and his brothers with Sita and her sisters, the departure of Vishwamitra, the encounter with Parashurama, and the safe return to Ayodhya.

#### Q1

**Question:** King Dasharatha came to the wedding pavilion with his sons and all the sages. Then Janaka, bringing his daughters adorned with all ornaments, came to the wedding altar and requested whom to perform all the wedding rites along with all the sages?

**Options:**
- 1. Vishwamitra
- 2. Shatananda
- 3. Vasishtha
- 4. Vamadeva

**Correct answer:** Vasishtha

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Janaka

#### Q2

**Question:** After the wedding of Sita and Rama was completed, the next day, where did Maharishi Vishwamitra go after blessing all the brides and grooms?

**Options:**
- 1. To the Himalayan regions
- 2. To the Vindhya mountain
- 3. To the Gandhara country
- 4. To Mahendragiri

**Correct answer:** Himalayan regions

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** When King Dasharatha set out for Ayodhya with his four sons, four daughters-in-law, and his retinue, which great sage obstructed their journey?

**Answer:** Parashurama

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Ayodhya, Parashurama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the weddings of Sita, Urmila, Mandavi, and Shrutakirti take place?

**Answer:** The wedding pavilion was decorated with fragrant flowers and mango festoons. All necessary materials for the wedding rites were brought to the altar. With the cooperation of all sages, Maharishi Vasishtha undertook to conduct the wedding ceremony, performing it auspiciously, according to scriptures, and with mantras. King Janaka completed the giving away of Sita and Urmila, and had his brother Kushadhvaja perform the giving away of Mandavi and Shrutakirti. Then, approving Janaka's words, the four brothers, with Vasishtha's consent, took their brides' hands and circumambulated the fire, the altar, King Janaka, and all the sages, bowing to them. Then, following the scriptures and Kalpa Sutras, Maharishi Vasishtha continued the wedding ceremony. For the wedding of the Raghu dynasty that took place in this manner, the gods in the sky showered flowers. Seeing that auspicious celebration, the virtuous men and women told each other that their births were fulfilled. Thus, those radiant newlyweds, holding each other's little fingers and with the knots of their garments tied together, circumambulated the fire three times and completed the wedding ceremony. Then the four couples went to their respective lodgings.

**Key entities:** Sita, Urmila, Mandavi, Shrutakirti, Janaka, Kushadhvaja

#### Q5

**Question:** How was the danger that came in the form of Parashurama to Sri Rama, who was returning to Ayodhya after completing the wedding festivities, averted?

**Answer:** Dasharatha, who set out for Ayodhya with his four sons and daughters-in-law, bid farewell to Janaka and others and traveled some distance. Then, Parashurama, carrying an axe on one shoulder and the Vaishnava bow in one hand, came towards them. Vasishtha and others bowed to him and had Rama worship him. Then Parashurama said, 'O Rama! I heard that you broke the Shiva bow. I have brought another divine bow. This Vaishnava bow was placed by Narayana with our grandfather Richika. Take this bow, string it, and demonstrate your strength. Seeing your capability, I will fight a duel with you.' Hearing Parashurama's words, Dasharatha was frightened and prayed with folded hands. Then Rama said, 'O Bhargava! Breaking the Shiva bow was done according to Kshatriya dharma by merely stringing it. The breaking of the bow was only divine will. But you spoke considering me incapable. I do not accept that. Now see my prowess.' Saying this, Rama took the Vaishnava bow from Parashurama's hand and strung an arrow. Since the arrow once shot should not go waste, he struck the meritorious worlds that Parashurama had earned through severe penance. Then Parashurama, helpless, realizing that Rama was none other than Maha Vishnu, went to Mahendragiri with the speed of mind. Thereafter, Dasharatha and all others happily reached Ayodhya.

**Key entities:** Parashurama, Rama, Ayodhya, Dasharatha, Janaka, Shiva, Narayana, Vishnu

### Chapter 14: Fourteenth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 1-6
- Source PDF pages: 36, 37, 38
- Printed page numbers: 40, 41, 42
- Key entities: Dasharatha, Rama, Bharata, Vasishta, Sita, Yudhajit, Kushadhvaja, Shatananda, Jabali, Sumantra, Narayana
- Places: Ayodhya

**Summary:** King Dasharatha decides to crown Rama as prince regent. He seeks the assembly's consent, while Bharata is away at his maternal uncle's house. Dasharatha entrusts the coronation arrangements to Sage Vashishta. Rama is summoned and told of the auspicious asterism Pushya for the ceremony. Sita and Rama undertake a fast, performing rituals and sleeping on darbha grass. The citizens of Ayodhya celebrate the news with great joy, decorating the city and praising the king.

#### Q1

**Question:** When King Dasharatha intended to crown Sri Rama as prince regent and sought the consent of all in his assembly, Bharata was at his maternal uncle's house. What is the name of Bharata's maternal uncle?

**Options:**
- 1. Siradhvaja
- 2. Kushadhvaja
- 3. Yudhajit
- 4. Shatananda

**Correct answer:** Yudhajit

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Rama, Bharata, Yudhajit

#### Q2

**Question:** To whom did Dasharatha entrust the responsibility of conducting Sri Rama's coronation?

**Options:**
- 1. Vishwamitra
- 2. Vashishta
- 3. Jabali
- 4. Jabali

**Correct answer:** Vashishta

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Rama, Vasishta

#### Q3

**Question:** King Dasharatha, having summoned Sri Rama through Sumantra, said, 'My son! Tomorrow, on an auspicious asterism, you shall be crowned.' What is the name of that auspicious asterism?

**Answer:** Pushya

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Rama, Sumantra

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the fast undertaken by Sita and Rama proceed during the coronation?

**Answer:** Dasharatha told Vashishta, 'O great sage! I have instructed that Rama should undertake a fast. You also go and tell Sita to undertake the fast along with Rama.' Accordingly, Vashishta went to Rama's inner apartments and gave the fast initiation with mantras to Sita and Rama. Then Rama's palace was filled with joyous men and women. After Vashishta left, Sri Rama completed his bath and other rituals, and with a steady mind, along with his wife Sita, worshipped Lord Narayana. Then, carrying a vessel containing offerings, he circumambulated the fire and, facing Lord Mahavishnu, performed a homa according to the scriptures into the blazing fire. He then partook of the remaining offerings. Meditating on the supreme deity Mahavishnu, they both silently and with self-control lay down on a well-spread bed of darbha grass in that palace. Thus the fast of Sita and Rama continued.

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Dasharatha, Vasishta, Narayana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the citizens of Ayodhya celebrate upon hearing the news of Sri Rama's coronation?

**Answer:** Hearing the auspicious news of Sri Rama's coronation, the townspeople and countryfolk were overjoyed. They cleaned all the city streets, sprinkled water, and drew colorful designs. They decorated the city with door arches and flower garlands, making it splendid. As the auspicious time for the coronation approached, the men and women in the city chatted in their courtyards and were delighted. Everywhere, people enjoyed the fine performances of actors and actresses, the graceful dance poses of dancers, and the sweet songs of singers. In honor of the great coronation festival, all citizens scattered colorful flowers on the royal roads. They made all the roads fragrant with incense and perfumed ointments. The people, adorned with splendor, praised King Dasharatha. They extolled the king as the enhancer of the Ikshvaku dynasty, recognizing his old age and his decision to crown Sri Rama as a great thing. They said, 'Sri Rama, who knows the good and bad of all people, is going to be our lord. He alone will be our eternal protector. This fortune that has befallen us is the result of divine grace.' Thus all the people expressed their joy to one another.

**Key entities:** Ayodhya, Rama, Dasharatha

### Chapter 15: Fifteenth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 7-12
- Source PDF pages: 38, 39, 40
- Printed page numbers: 42, 43, 44
- Key entities: Kaikeyi, Rama, Mandara, Dasharatha, Bharata, Kausalya, Maricha, Subahu
- Places: Dandaka Forest

**Summary:** Queen Kaikeyi learns of Rama's impending coronation from her maid Manthara. She reminds King Dasharatha of two boons he had promised her during a battle with Shambarasura, and demands that Bharata be crowned instead of Rama, and that Rama be exiled to the forest for fourteen years. Dasharatha is devastated and pleads with Kaikeyi to relent, but she remains firm.

#### Q1

**Question:** Who first told Kaikeyi, one of Dasharatha's wives, the news of Rama's coronation?

**Options:**
- 1. Dasharatha
- 2. Maid Manthara
- 3. Vamadeva
- 4. Kausalya

**Correct answer:** Maid Manthara

**Key entities:** Kaikeyi, Dasharatha, Rama, Mandara

#### Q2

**Question:** During a war with whom did Dasharatha previously give Kaikeyi two boons as a pledge?

**Options:**
- 1. Shambarasura
- 2. Maricha
- 3. Subahu
- 4. Sunda

**Correct answer:** Shambarasura

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Kaikeyi

#### Q3

**Question:** When King Dasharatha entered Kaikeyi's inner palace to tell her the auspicious news of the coronation, where was Kaikeyi?

**Answer:** In the anger room (kopagriha), lying on the bare floor

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Kaikeyi

#### Q4

**Question:** In what manner and what kind of boons did Kaikeyi ask from King Dasharatha?

**Answer:** Kaikeyi, lying on the bare floor in the anger room, was approached by Dasharatha who asked her what she wanted. She demanded that he first swear an oath. Then she reminded him of the two boons he had given her during the war with Shambarasura. She asked that Bharata be crowned with the preparations made for Rama, and that Rama wear bark garments, mat his hair, and go to Dandaka forest for fourteen years of exile.

**Key entities:** Kaikeyi, Dasharatha, Bharata, Rama, Dandaka Forest

#### Q5

**Question:** After hearing the boons demanded by Kaikeyi, how did King Dasharatha lament?

**Answer:** Dasharatha became stunned and after a while regained consciousness, lamenting whether it was a dream or delusion. He then looked at Kaikeyi as if to burn her with his gaze, asking what wrong Rama or he had done to her. He said he could not live without Rama even for a moment, and begged her to give up the idea of sending Rama to the forest. He offered to give her the entire earth, but she remained unmoved. He then fell down in despair.

**Key entities:** Kaikeyi, Dasharatha, Rama

### Chapter 16: Sixteenth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 13-18
- Source PDF pages: 40, 41, 42
- Printed page numbers: 44, 45, 46
- Key entities: Dasharatha, Kaikeyi, Rama, Bharata, Sumantra, Jabali
- Places: Ayodhya

**Summary:** King Dasharatha, bound by his promise to Kaikeyi, is grief-stricken and collapses. At dawn, he sends for Rama. Rama arrives at Kaikeyi's palace and learns from her that he must go into exile for fourteen years so that Bharata can be crowned.

#### Q1

**Question:** Seeing Kaikeyi who would not relent, King Dasharatha, overwhelmed with grief that his son would be separated from him, fell down where?

**Options:**
- 1. On a proper seat
- 2. In Kaikeyi's lap
- 3. On a swan-down bed
- 4. On the bare ground

**Correct answer:** On the bare ground

**Key entities:** Kaikeyi, Dasharatha

#### Q2

**Question:** Pressed by Kaikeyi, King Dasharatha, bound by the noose of dharma, as dawn broke, whom did he send to summon Rama to him?

**Options:**
- 1. Sumantra
- 2. Vasishtha
- 3. The chamberlain
- 4. Jabali

**Correct answer:** Sumantra

**Key entities:** Kaikeyi, Dasharatha, Rama, Sumantra

#### Q3

**Question:** Upon his father's summons from Kaikeyi's chamber, Rama immediately set out on which vehicle?

**Answer:** Chariot

**Key entities:** Kaikeyi, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Sage Vasishtha, who was responsible for conducting the coronation, come to the city of Ayodhya? What did the sage do in the city?

**Answer:** As the sun rose and the auspicious moment for the coronation approached, Sage Vasishtha, accompanied by his disciples, gathered the coronation materials and set out from the hermitage to the city of Ayodhya. By the time he arrived, the city was beautifully decorated. The people, eager to see Rama's coronation, crowded the streets. The air was fragrant with sandalwood and aloe incense. Then Vasishtha, surrounded by his disciples, proceeded towards the inner palace. Sumantra came to meet him. Vasishtha told Sumantra, 'Inform the king that I am here.' He also showed Sumantra all the materials he had brought for the auspicious coronation ceremony. Sumantra was pleased and, following Vasishtha's command, entered the king's chamber, proclaiming victory to the king. Not knowing the king's condition, Sumantra greeted him as usual with 'Good morning.' He said, 'Vasishtha and others have arrived. You should complete your bath and other rituals and prepare for the coronation ceremony.' Thus, Sumantra, having come as per Vasishtha's order, stood near the king.

**Key entities:** Ayodhya, Rama, Sumantra

#### Q5

**Question:** When Rama saw his father in Kaikeyi's chamber, what news did he hear from Queen Kaikeyi?

**Answer:** Rama saw King Dasharatha sitting on a golden couch with a withered face, looking dejected, and Kaikeyi beside him. Rama bowed to his father's feet. Then, as the distressed Dasharatha uttered 'Father! Rama!', his eyes filled with tears, his throat choked, and he could not see. Seeing this, Rama was bewildered. Rama then bowed to Kaikeyi and asked, 'Mother! Why does our father appear angry like this? Have I committed any offense?' Kaikeyi replied, 'Rama! You are most dear to the king. I cannot bring myself to speak unpleasant words to you. He has given me a promise. That task can only be accomplished by you. If you promise me that you will surely fulfill it regardless of good or bad, then I will explain it fully. The king himself is unable to tell you.' Hearing Kaikeyi's words, Rama said, 'Mother! If it is the king's command, I am ready even to jump into fire. To uphold my father's word, I am ready even to drink deadly poison.' Having bound Rama by his promise, Kaikeyi said, 'Rama! I have now asked for the boons your father promised me long ago. The first is to crown Bharata, and the second is that you go to the forest today and spend fourteen years there. Your father gave me these two boons as a promise. You must uphold your father's truth.' Hearing his stepmother's words, Rama stood without any agitation.

**Key entities:** Rama, Kaikeyi, Dasharatha, Bharata

### Chapter 17: Seventeenth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 19-24
- Source PDF pages: 42, 43, 44, 45
- Printed page numbers: 46, 47, 48, 49
- Key entities: Rama, Kaikeyi, Kausalya, Lakshmana, Dasharatha, Sumantra, Mandara, Bharata
- Places: Ayodhya

**Summary:** Rama, determined to go to the forest, takes leave from Kaikeyi and then goes to his mother Kausalya. Lakshmana angrily protests against the exile, but Rama pacifies him by emphasizing obedience to parents. Kausalya laments and wants to accompany Rama, but Rama consoles her, urging her to serve King Dasharatha and wait for his return.

#### Q1

**Question:** Ready to renounce the kingdom and go to the forest, Sri Rama told Queen Kaikeyi from whom he would take leave?

**Options:**
- 1. Vasishtha
- 2. Queen Kausalya
- 3. Sumantra
- 4. Lakshmana

**Correct answer:** Queen Kausalya

**Key entities:** Rama, Kaikeyi, Kausalya

#### Q2

**Question:** When Lakshmana expressed his disagreement about Rama's exile, whom did Rama primarily cite as the cause for the kingdom slipping away and his exile?

**Options:**
- 1. Destiny
- 2. Father
- 3. Kaikeyi
- 4. Manthara

**Correct answer:** Destiny

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** Before Rama came to Queen Kausalya's palace to inform her about his exile, did Kausalya already know the details of the news?

**Answer:** No

**Key entities:** Rama, Kausalya

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Lakshmana think about the exile? How did Rama pacify his younger brother?

**Answer:** Rama said that his renouncing the coronation and going to the forest was due to fate alone. Hearing this, Lakshmana was torn between joy at his brother's adherence to dharma and sorrow at his leaving the kingdom. Then, like a wounded great serpent, Lakshmana angrily said, 'Brother! Kaikeyi and Dasharatha are both selfish. They will only harm you. They are enemies in the form of parents. You should not even mentally agree to their wishes. Brother! This is not done by them deliberately. It is not right for you to think it is merely divine. Now it will be known which is greater: divine power or human prowess. Even if all the guardians of the directions and the thirty-three crore gods come, they cannot stop Rama's coronation today. Whoever opposes me, strong as I am, will inevitably sink into endless sorrow from the force of my manliness. Even destiny cannot save him. O Lord! I am your servant. Command me what I should do to make this earth under your control.' Hearing Lakshmana's words, Rama said, 'Brother! Obey the command of parents with purity of thought, word, and deed. Consider them as me. This is the path of the virtuous.' Thus Sri Rama pacified his younger brother.

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Rama, Kaikeyi, Dasharatha

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Queen Kausalya express her anguish before Sri Rama? How did Rama pacify and convince her?

**Answer:** Knowing Rama's firm resolve to obey his father's command, Queen Kausalya shed continuous tears and with a choked voice said, 'My son! Rama! I cannot live without you before my eyes. If you are determined to go to the forest as per your father's command, take me with you. I will get used to forest life near you and live peacefully.' Seeing his mother lamenting, Rama said, 'Mother! For a woman, her husband is God. The great king now rules over you and me. Bharata is also righteous. He, being devoted to dharma, will always be obedient to you and follow you. This is my firm belief. After I leave Ayodhya, you must take care of the king so that he does not suffer from grief for his son. Do not let him be depressed by this unbearable sorrow; be vigilant and serve him. Spend your time in serving your husband and wait patiently until I return after completing my exile.' Hearing Rama's humble words, Kausalya wept profusely and said, 'My son! I do not have the strength to turn you from your firm resolve to go to the forest. Whatever fate decrees will happen. Son! Go carefully!' Then Kausalya gazed at Rama with unwavering attention and lovingly blessed him, wishing him all auspiciousness.

**Key entities:** Kausalya, Rama, Bharata, Ayodhya

### Chapter 18: Eighteenth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 25-30
- Source PDF pages: 45, 46, 47
- Printed page numbers: 49, 50, 51
- Key entities: Rama, Kausalya, Sita, Sumitra, Tataka, Bharata, Urmila, Shrutakirti, Janaka
- Places: Dandaka Forest, Ayodhya

**Summary:** Rama, after receiving blessings from his mother Kausalya, goes to Sita's palace. He informs Sita of his exile to the Dandaka forest due to his father's promise. Despite Rama's attempts to persuade her to stay in Ayodhya, Sita insists on accompanying him, citing her duty as a wife. Rama eventually agrees.

#### Q1

**Question:** After receiving blessings from his mother Kausalya, to whose presence did Rama go?

**Options:**
- 1. To the presence of Vasishtha
- 2. To the presence of Sumitra Devi
- 3. To the presence of Vamadeva
- 4. To the presence of Sita Devi

**Correct answer:** To the presence of Sita Devi

**Key entities:** Kausalya, Rama, Sita

#### Q2

**Question:** Lord Rama told Sita Devi, 'O Devi! I am strictly following my father's promise and going to which forests?'

**Options:**
- 1. To the Tataka forest region
- 2. To the penance forest
- 3. To the Dandaka forest
- 4. To the Ashoka forest region

**Correct answer:** To the Dandaka forest

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Dandaka Forest

#### Q3

**Question:** Rama tried many ways to persuade Sita Devi to stay in Ayodhya and not accompany him to the forest. Finally, if he refused to take her to the forests, unable to bear separation from Rama, what did she say she would sacrifice?

**Answer:** Her life

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Ayodhya

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Rama try to prevent Sita Devi from accompanying him to the forest?

**Answer:** After receiving blessings from mother Kausalya, Rama came on foot to Sita Devi's chamber. Seeing her husband worried, Sita said, 'Lord! Your face has lost its cheerfulness and become pale. I have never seen such a state before.' To his wife who spoke these distressed words, Rama said, 'Janaki, our venerable father is about to send me to the forests. Therefore, obeying the king's command, I must go to the Dandaka forests. You stay in Ayodhya and serve my parents with humility and affection. Have love for me, be patient with a firm mind. Perform worship as usual, observe vows and fasts. From the time Bharata becomes crown prince, he will be the supreme authority. In his rule, you should behave like an ordinary relative. Do not expect more respect than Urmila and Shrutakirti. Behave amicably among others. For the sake of fulfilling my father's word, I am going to the forests today. You stay in Ayodhya, do not displease anyone, and follow my words.' Thus Rama explained the nuances of dharma to Sita. Rama's words, though spoken, pained Sita, who was naturally gentle. Then she said, 'O noble husband! What is this? You are speaking meaningless words. Never before have such words come from your mouth. O great hero! A wife is half of her husband. Therefore, she is entitled to half the fruit of her husband's actions. The command given by the king to you applies to me as well, does it not? Hence, I too must undergo exile along with you.' Thus Sita expressed her firm opinion to Rama.

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Kausalya, Dandaka Forest, Ayodhya, Bharata, Urmila, Shrutakirti

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Sita Devi reason about dharma to persuade Rama to agree to take her to the forest?

**Answer:** To Janaki, who was ready to accompany him to the forest, Rama said, 'Sita! Do not make hasty, sorrowful thoughts. Listen to my words. In the forest there are thorns and stones, no paths to walk, no food at times. You, who have enjoyed royal luxuries unknown to the sun, cannot bear the hardships of that forest. The forest is always an abode of sorrow.' Hearing Rama's words, Sita realized that Rama did not wish to take her to the forest and wept for a long time. Shedding tears, she said, 'Lord! For any wife, living apart from her husband is unbearable. You are my visible god. In this world and the next, I desire your companionship. As proclaimed by renowned brahmins, after being given in marriage by parents with the pouring of water, I must follow you not only in this world but also in the next. Following the authority of the Vedas, my father Janaka gave me to you with the pouring of water, did he not? I am virtuous, devoted to serving my husband. I am a partner in your joys and sorrows. O noble husband! During exile, I consider both hardship and happiness equally. Therefore, take me with you. If you do not agree, I will give up my life.' Hearing Sita's words, Rama said, 'O Sita! Whatever it may be, you are determined to come with me to the forest. Therefore, follow me and fulfill your duty as a devoted wife.' Thus he agreed.

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Janaka

### Chapter 19: Nineteenth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 31-36
- Source PDF pages: 47, 48, 49, 50
- Printed page numbers: 51, 52, 53, 54
- Key entities: Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Dasharatha, Kaikeyi, Vasishta, Sumitra, Sumantra, Bharata
- Places: Dandaka Forest, Kosala

**Summary:** Rama, accompanied by Sita and Lakshmana, prepares for exile. He distributes his wealth to the deserving, visits his father Dasharatha, and consoles him. Kaikeyi's cruelty reaches its peak when she objects to Rama being given any comforts for his exile.

#### Q1

**Question:** Realizing that Sita and Rama were ready for exile, Lakshmana convinced his elder brother that he too would follow him to the forests. Thus, Rama, accompanied by Sita and Lakshmana, going to the forests, what did he do with all the wealth he had?

**Options:**
- 1. He entrusted it to the treasury
- 2. He entrusted it to Vasishta
- 3. He donated it to the deserving
- 4. He entrusted it to his mother and left

**Correct answer:** He donated it to the deserving

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Lakshmana

#### Q2

**Question:** Rama, accompanied by Sita and Lakshmana, going to the forests, first came to see whom?

**Options:**
- 1. Dasharatha
- 2. Vasishta
- 3. Kaikeyi
- 4. Sumitra Devi

**Correct answer:** Dasharatha

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Dasharatha

#### Q3

**Question:** Through whom did Rama inform his father that he had come to see him?

**Answer:** Sumantra

**Key entities:** Rama, Sumantra

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Rama console his grieving father and take leave from him?

**Answer:** Dasharatha was immersed in an ocean of grief upon seeing Rama who came to see him. Then Rama, joining his palms, said: 'O King! You are the lord of us all. Bless me with your cool hands and send me to the Dandaka forests for exile. Lakshmana and Sita wish to follow me to the forests. Though I tried to dissuade them in many ways, they do not listen. Therefore, permit them also to come with me. Do not grieve at all for us.' Saying thus, Rama waited for the king's permission. Seeing Rama, Dasharatha said: 'O Rama of the Raghu dynasty! I was deceived because of the boons given to Kaikeyi. Disregarding my words, you yourself take up the sovereignty of Kosala.' To Dasharatha, Rama replied: 'Father! It is not dharma for me to break your word. Therefore, I will go to the forests. After spending fourteen years there, I will return and serve you.' To his son who spoke thus, Dasharatha said: 'My son! O delight of the Raghus! By upholding my word, you are going to the forests leaving all our people to establish me in truth. This is impossible for anyone but you. My son! I cannot turn you from your resolve. But at least stay here until this night ends. I will spend this one day happily seeing you. You may go tomorrow.' Then Rama said: 'Father! Even if I spend this night here, will I not get these royal pleasures tomorrow? Therefore, setting aside desires, I wish to go to the forests now. Bless me and send me.' Then Dasharatha said: 'My son! I know well that you are devoted to dharma and truthful. Very well, go now. May you attain happiness in this world and the next!' Thus blessing him, he sent him off.

**Key entities:** Rama, Dasharatha, Dandaka Forest, Lakshmana, Sita, Kaikeyi, Kosala

#### Q5

**Question:** What can be described as the culmination of Kaikeyi's wickedness?

**Answer:** Dasharatha, greatly distressed by his vow, told Sumantra: 'O great minister! Equip the fourfold army and send them with Rama. Send dancers and wrestlers to provide entertainment and delight behind the army. Send various kinds of gold, jewels, ornaments, and clothes sufficient for fourteen years. Send important weapons, carts laden with food, and forest-dwellers to show the way in the forest as companions for Rama. Sri Rama, hunting wild animals in the forests and drinking honey available there, will not think of royal pleasures. Here Bharata can rule.' Hearing Dasharatha's words, Kaikeyi became afraid and worried. Standing before the king, she said: 'Bharata does not want a kingdom devoid of enjoyments and wealth, a deserted kingdom.' Saying this, with reddened eyes and abandoning shame, Kaikeyi spoke. Looking at Kaikeyi, Dasharatha rebuked her: 'Fie! O wicked woman! Do not show me your face.' Even after being rebuked in front of so many, Kaikeyi was not affected as if an ant had bitten her. Such an act of Kaikeyi can be described as the culmination of her wickedness.

**Key entities:** Kaikeyi, Dasharatha, Sumantra, Rama, Bharata

### Chapter 20: Twentieth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 37-42
- Source PDF pages: 50, 51, 52
- Printed page numbers: 54, 55, 56
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Dasharatha, Kaikeyi, Kausalya, Sumantra, Jabali, Bharata
- Places: Kosala

**Summary:** Rama, Lakshmana, and Sita prepare to leave for the forest. King Dasharatha orders a chariot. The citizens grieve Rama's departure. Dasharatha laments and blames Kaikeyi. Kausalya tries to console him.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Rama said to Dasharatha, 'Father, I have given up all comforts. Fruits and roots in the forest are my food. If anyone brings me bark garments, I am ready to wear them,' who provided bark garments to Rama and Lakshmana?

**Options:**
- 1. Queen Kaikeyi
- 2. A servant
- 3. Dasharatha
- 4. Sumantra

**Correct answer:** Queen Kaikeyi

**Key entities:** Rama, Dasharatha, Lakshmana, Kaikeyi

#### Q2

**Question:** Whom did Dasharatha order to prepare the chariot to take Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana to the forest?

**Options:**
- 1. The commander
- 2. Sumantra
- 3. Jabali
- 4. The chamberlain

**Correct answer:** Sumantra

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Sumantra

#### Q3

**Question:** Who said to the grief-stricken Dasharatha, who was watching the direction Rama went, 'O great king! Let us wish that our loved ones return to us. We cannot follow them far, can we?'

**Answer:** The ministers

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did all the citizens of the city become distressed for Sri Rama?

**Answer:** After the noble Rama left the palace, the cries of the palace women became intense. Rama, who never harmed anyone, was the protector of all. That lord never got angry with anyone, and he respected us with love and affection like his own mother Kausalya. Now where has that lord gone? The king, having lost his senses, sent him to the forest and separated him from us. Thus they wept loudly and wailed. The king, who was already suffering from separation from his son, became even more depressed upon hearing the terrible cries in the palace. The entire city was overcome with the pain of separation from Rama, and all the daily activities of the citizens came to a halt. All of Rama's friends lost their senses and took to their beds due to grief. In this way, all the citizens of the city became distressed.

**Key entities:** Rama, Kausalya

#### Q5

**Question:** After Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana went to the forest, how did Dasharatha lament?

**Answer:** Dasharatha kept looking in the direction of Rama's chariot until the dust raised by the chariot wheels was visible. When even that dust disappeared, the king fell to the ground in agony. Then Kausalya immediately grabbed his right shoulder to lift him up. Kaikeyi came and grabbed his left shoulder. Then Dasharatha turned to Kaikeyi and raged, 'Kaikeyi, do not touch me. Do not show me your face. O wicked woman! I married you with fire as witness. Because of your excessive evil deed, from today I abandon you. If Bharata becomes the ruler of this vast Kosala kingdom through adharma and rejoices, may the offerings he gives after my death not reach me!' Thus the king spoke in grief. Then Kausalya lifted the dust-covered king and went with him to her home. Dasharatha lamented thinking of his son who was dressed as an ascetic. The king looked like the sun eclipsed by Rahu. The grief-stricken king was withering away. Kausalya, herself grief-stricken, said to the king lying on the bed, 'Kaikeyi, with her crooked mind, sent Rama to the forest. Even if she gives the kingdom to Bharata, I accept it. But even if my son stays here and serves Bharata as a slave, I accept that. That is better than forest exile! Then my child would be here before my eyes!' Thus Kausalya and Dasharatha lamented thinking of Rama.

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Dasharatha, Kausalya, Kaikeyi, Bharata, Kosala

### Chapter 21: Twenty-first Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 43-48
- Source PDF pages: 52, 53, 54
- Printed page numbers: 56, 57, 58
- Key entities: Kausalya, Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Sumitra, Sumantra, Dasharatha, Kaikeyi
- Places: Ayodhya, Tamasa

**Summary:** Kausalya laments for Rama, and the citizens of Ayodhya follow Rama's chariot. Rama, Lakshmana, and Sita travel to the Tamasa river, where they spend the night. Rama decides to leave secretly to prevent the citizens from following further. The citizens wake up to find Rama gone and return to Ayodhya, grieving.

#### Q1
