**Question:** Who consoled Kausalya, who was grieving and emaciated with sorrow for her son, constantly thinking of Sri Rama, with comforting words?

**Options:**
- 1. Vasishtha
- 2. Sumantra
- 3. Sumitra
- 4. Dasaratha

**Correct answer:** Sumitra

**Key entities:** Kausalya, Rama, Sumitra

#### Q2

**Question:** Who followed Sri Rama's chariot without leaving him?

**Options:**
- 1. Commanders
- 2. Ministers
- 3. Vasishtha and others
- 4. Brahmins and citizens

**Correct answer:** Brahmins and citizens

**Key entities:** Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** Desiring to go to the forest, Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana traveled until evening, stopped at a place, and rested that night on the bank of which river?

**Answer:** Tamasa river

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Tamasa

#### Q4

**Question:** How far did the citizens of Ayodhya who followed Sri Rama's chariot go? What happened afterwards?

**Answer:** Despite Rama's protests, the citizens followed him. They traveled with the brahmins and people for some distance and reached the banks of the Tamasa river by evening. Then Rama said to Lakshmana, 'Today we will spend the first night of our exile here.' After drinking the waters of the Tamasa, Rama lay down on a bed of leaves arranged by Sumantra and Lakshmana, with Sita. Lakshmana and Sumantra remained awake that night. All the citizens, exhausted from the journey, fell into a deep sleep. Seeing them sleeping, Rama said to Lakshmana, 'Brother, look at these citizens sleeping under the trees. Out of affection for us, they have left their wives and children and followed us here. They are determined to take us back to Ayodhya, even at the cost of their lives. Therefore, before they wake up, let us board the chariot and quickly go by a path that no one can detect. Then they will have no chance to follow us and will return to Ayodhya. As princes, it is our duty to remove the people's grief.' Accordingly, Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana boarded the chariot, and Sumantra drove it across the river by another ford. Then the citizens who were sleeping under the trees woke up and, not seeing Sri Rama, were stunned with grief. They looked everywhere but could not find him. They lamented, yearning for the sight of Sita and Rama. Finally, they returned to Ayodhya by the same path they had come.

**Key entities:** Ayodhya, Rama, Tamasa, Lakshmana, Sumantra, Sita

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the citizens who returned to Ayodhya lament when they met their families?

**Answer:** The citizens who had followed Sri Rama to the forests and returned reached their homes and met their wives and children. Yet they could not overcome their grief. Even when friends came to greet them, no signs of joy appeared on their faces. The women in the houses did not engage in cooking. The women said to their husbands, 'In the present circumstances, this city is not fit for good people to live in. Everyone here is anxious about Sri Rama. If we stay here, we will have no peace. This kingdom is under Kaikeyi's control. Hence, adharma will prevail here. Living in such a place is futile. What is the use of wealth or children in a kingdom without protection? Kaikeyi, who made the king a puppet and did such a thing to Sri Rama, will not spare anyone. As long as Kaikeyi lives, we cannot live happily under her rule. Because of her, the entire kingdom will be destroyed. King Dasaratha, stricken with grief for his son, will not live long. On the day he is gone, our fortunes will be ruined. Therefore, let us go to a place where Kaikeyi's name is not heard.' Thus the citizens of Ayodhya lamented, and the sun set. The city of Ayodhya appeared like a dried-up ocean.

**Key entities:** Ayodhya, Rama, Kaikeyi, Dasharatha

### Chapter 22: Twenty-Second Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 49-54
- Source PDF pages: 54, 55, 56, 57
- Printed page numbers: 58, 59, 60, 61
- Key entities: Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Guha, Trishanku, Sumantra, Kaikeyi, Bharata, Kausalya, Sumitra
- Places: Tamasa, Ganga, Prayaga, Chitrakuta, Godavari, Kosala, Yamuna, Ayodhya, Dandaka Forest

**Summary:** Rama, Sita, and Lakshmana cross the Tamasa river and travel south, reaching the Ganges. They meet Guha, king of Shringaberapura, and later cross the Ganges to reach Prayaga, where they visit the hermitage of Sage Bharadvaja. After resting, they proceed to Chitrakuta.

#### Q1

**Question:** After crossing the Tamasa river and traveling south, which sacred river bank did Rama, along with Sita and Lakshmana, reach by that evening?

**Options:**
- 1. Godavari
- 2. Krishna
- 3. Ganges
- 4. Sindhu

**Correct answer:** Ganges

**Key entities:** Tamasa, Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Ganga

#### Q2

**Question:** After crossing the vast borders of Kosala, Rama reached the region of Shringaberapura and wished to rest there. Who was the ruler of that region?

**Options:**
- 1. Guha
- 2. Trishanku
- 3. Kushanabha
- 4. Vishala

**Correct answer:** Guha

**Key entities:** Kosala, Rama, Guha

#### Q3

**Question:** After sending Sumantra back with the chariot, Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana crossed the Ganges and reached Prayaga, the confluence of the Ganges and Yamuna. Whose hermitage did they visit there?

**Answer:** Bharadvaja Maharshi

**Key entities:** Sumantra, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Ganga, Prayaga, Yamuna

#### Q4

**Question:** After crossing the Ganges and the populated regions, the noble Rama entered the forests and rested at a place. What topics did he discuss with Lakshmana?

**Answer:** Rama performed the evening worship and then spoke to Lakshmana: 'Brother, this is the first night after leaving the populated areas. Let us somehow spend this night here.' They lay down on the beds of grass they had prepared. Rama said, 'Lakshmana, the king must be suffering greatly at this time. Kaikeyi, however, is rejoicing that her wish has been fulfilled. There is no one to comfort our father now; he is old and separated from us. Seeing this unexpected calamity, I wonder: Did Kaikeyi come to Ayodhya only to send me to the forest, to deliver the king to death, and to make her son Bharata king? Having gained power, she may become arrogant and forget right and wrong, and might trouble mother Kausalya and mother Sumitra for my sake. Therefore, Lakshmana, you should leave at dawn and go to Ayodhya to set things right. I will go to the Dandaka forest with Sita.' Thus Rama lamented in many ways. Then Lakshmana consoled his brother in various ways: 'Brother, if you grieve like this, it pains both Sita and me. I cannot live without you. I need no one but you. Even heaven without you I would despise.' After saying this, Sita and Rama lay down on the grass bed prepared by Lakshmana under the shade of a banyan tree. Thus they spent that night.

**Key entities:** Ganga, Rama, Lakshmana, Kaikeyi, Ayodhya, Bharata, Kausalya, Sumitra, Dandaka Forest, Sita

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana reach Bharadvaja's hermitage? How did the meeting with the sage proceed?

**Answer:** Rama, along with Sita and Lakshmana, journeyed to see Prayaga, the confluence of the Ganges and Yamuna. As they traveled, Rama said to Lakshmana, 'Brother, I have heard that the hermitage of Sage Bharadvaja is near Prayaga.' Thus speaking, they reached the hermitage of Sage Bharadvaja by evening. There, Rama met the sage and told him about themselves. Then Sage Bharadvaja performed hospitality for them, providing various fruits found in the forest, food items, and sweet drinks. He affectionately arranged for their stay. Then the sage said, 'O Rama, I have been waiting for a long time for the fortune of your sight. Today, with your arrival, it has been fulfilled. You may stay comfortably in this holy place at the confluence of the Ganges and Yamuna.' Then Rama replied, 'O sage, if I stay here, the people of Kosala will frequently come here. Therefore, it is not good for us to stay here. Please tell us of a hermitage area that is not accessible to people, where we can stay comfortably.' The sage then said, 'Rama, about ten kroshas from here, there is a place called Chitrakuta, which is suitable for you to reside.' Rama and his party then traveled along the path shown by the sage.

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Prayaga, Ganga, Yamuna, Kosala, Chitrakuta

### Chapter 23: Twenty-third Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 55-60
- Source PDF pages: 57, 58, 59
- Printed page numbers: 61, 62, 63
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Sumantra, Dasharatha, Kausalya, Valmiki, Atri, Vishvamitra, Guha, Bharata
- Places: Chitrakuta, Ayodhya, Yamuna, Ganga, Godavari, Sarayu, Dandaka Forest

**Summary:** Rama, Lakshmana, and Sita travel towards Chitrakuta. Sage Bharadvaja guides them, mentioning a river to cross. They meet a sage near Chitrakuta and build a hermitage. Sumantra returns to Ayodhya and delivers Rama's message to King Dasharatha, who grieves deeply. Sumantra tries to console Dasharatha and Kausalya.

#### Q1

**Question:** As Rama and his companions were traveling towards Chitrakuta, Sage Bharadvaja accompanied them for some distance and guided them, saying, 'If you cross a certain river, you will reach the Chitrakuta mountain region.' What is the name of that river?

**Options:**
- 1. Ganga
- 2. Yamuna
- 3. Godavari
- 4. Sarayu

**Correct answer:** Yamuna

**Key entities:** Rama, Chitrakuta, Yamuna

#### Q2

**Question:** Rama and his companions reached the Chitrakuta mountain region and visited a sage who lived nearby, telling him that they intended to build an ashrama in that area. Who was that sage?

**Options:**
- 1. Sage Atri
- 2. Sage Bharadvaja
- 3. Sage Valmiki
- 4. Sage Vishvamitra

**Correct answer:** Sage Valmiki

**Key entities:** Rama, Chitrakuta, Valmiki

#### Q3

**Question:** In the Chitrakuta mountain region, at the spot designated by Rama, Lakshmana built a leaf hut. Then Rama performed a ritual and Rama and Sita entered the hut. What is that ritual called?

**Answer:** Vastu Puja

**Key entities:** Chitrakuta, Rama, Lakshmana, Sita

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Sumantra, upon reaching Ayodhya, convey Rama's message to Dasharatha?

**Answer:** Rama, along with Sita and Lakshmana, crossed the Ganga and reached the other shore. Sumantra watched them as long as they were visible, then took leave of Guha and returned to Ayodhya. He entered the royal palace, met the king, and bowed to him. Then the king said to Sumantra, 'My children, who have never known heat, are suffering many hardships in the forest. Where do they sleep? What are their food and activities? Describe all these. By hearing Rama's story, I will be somewhat freed from grief.' Hearing this, Sumantra, with tears and a choked voice, said, 'O king! Rama, with joined palms, bowed his head to you and said, "Sumantra! Convey my prostrations to the feet of our father, who is a knower of the self and a great soul. Tell all the mothers in the inner apartments that I have bowed to them and asked about their welfare. Especially convey my salutations to our mother Kausalya. Inform them that we are all well and are practicing dharma with devotion. Convey our welfare to Bharata. Tell him from me to treat all mothers with equal regard." After Rama said many such things, Lakshmana said, "Sumantra! What offense did Rama, a prince, commit to be sent to the forest? Whatever happens, whether brother or father, Rama is everything to me." O king! Sita, without speaking a word to me, was motionless, grieving, crying, and repeatedly looking at the chariot and at me.' Thus Sumantra delivered Rama's message.

**Key entities:** Sumantra, Ayodhya, Rama, Dasharatha, Sita, Lakshmana, Ganga, Guha, Kausalya, Bharata

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Sumantra console Dasharatha and Queen Kausalya, who were lamenting with grief for their son?

**Answer:** After hearing Rama's message through Sumantra, Dasharatha said, 'O Sumantra! I now wish to see Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana. But due to my sin, that is not possible.' Lamenting thus, he lost consciousness. Then Kausalya, trembling and weak, fell to the ground. After some time, she said, 'Sumantra! Without Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana, I cannot live even for a moment. Therefore, take me to the place where they are.' Hearing Kausalya's pitiful words, Sumantra grieved for a long time. Then Sumantra said, 'Mother! Rama of the Raghu dynasty is staying peacefully in the Dandaka forest without any worry. So do not worry about what will happen to Rama. Give up the grief caused by separation from him. Lakshmana, who is self-controlled and knows dharma, is constantly serving Rama in the forest. Sita is always receiving love and affection from her husband. Mother Kausalya! Do not worry at all about Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana.' Thus Sumantra tried to console Dasharatha and Kausalya with appropriate words, but they, weakened by grief at separation from their son, continued to lament, crying 'Rama! Rama!' and suffering.

**Key entities:** Sumantra, Dasharatha, Kausalya, Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Dandaka Forest

### Chapter 24: Twenty-Fourth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 61-66
- Source PDF pages: 59, 60, 61, 62
- Printed page numbers: 63, 64, 65, 66
- Key entities: Kausalya, Rama, Dasharatha, Sumitra, Vasishta, Kaikeyi
- Places: Ayodhya

**Summary:** Kausalya, unable to bear separation from Rama, speaks harshly to Dasaratha. Seeing her husband's distress, she repents. Dasaratha consoles her and recounts a curse from his youth that he would die of grief for his son. As night deepens, Dasaratha, calling out to Kausalya and Sumitra, passes away, remembering Rama. The queens and palace women lament loudly. Vasistha and ministers decide to preserve the king's body in an oil-filled trough until his sons return. The city of Ayodhya falls into grief and darkness.

#### Q1

**Question:** Unable to bear separation from Sri Rama, Kausalya spoke harshly to Dasaratha. Seeing her husband's distress, how did she behave?

**Options:**
- 1. She repented
- 2. She became irritated
- 3. She was astonished
- 4. She justified herself

**Correct answer:** She repented

**Key entities:** Rama, Kausalya, Dasharatha

#### Q2

**Question:** Dasaratha, consoling Kausalya, told her in detail about a curse that befell him as a result of an incident in his youth. What did he say the curse was?

**Options:**
- 1. You will be deprived of your kingdom
- 2. You will be deprived of heaven
- 3. You will die of grief for your son
- 4. You will be deprived of righteousness

**Correct answer:** You will die of grief for your son

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Kausalya

#### Q3

**Question:** When King Dasaratha, late at night past midnight, said 'Alas, Kausalya! Sumitra! My senses are failing moment by moment,' as he left this world, whom did he remember while giving up his life?

**Answer:** Sri Rama

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Kausalya, Sumitra, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the queens and the women of the inner palace lament upon the death of King Dasaratha?

**Answer:** By sunrise, all the attendants came eagerly to serve the king. Since Dasaratha had not come out of the bedchamber, they suspected something and looked inside, realizing that the king's heartbeat had stopped. Kausalya and Sumitra, immersed in grief until late night, were in deep sleep and did not realize. Upon learning that the king had died, the women of the inner palace raised their voices and wept piteously. Awakened by their cries, Kausalya and Sumitra quickly woke up. Seeing the king, they cried 'Alas! Lord of our lives!' and fell to the ground. Overwhelmed with grief, Kausalya rolled on the ground, her body covered with dust and lustreless. Then Kaikeyi and all of Dasaratha's wives, overcome with sorrow, wept and fell unconscious. With the wailing of all the queens including Kausalya, the entire palace trembled again with cries. With the king's death, the palace was filled with fear, agitation, and distressed attendants. Thus the queens and attendants lamented at the death of King Dasaratha.

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Kausalya, Sumitra, Kaikeyi

#### Q5

**Question:** How was King Dasaratha's mortal body preserved? Then how did the people of Ayodhya and the queens grieve?

**Answer:** Kausalya, placing the head of the lifeless King Dasaratha on her lap, lamented in various ways. She said, 'What use is life without the king? I will also perform self-immolation with the king.' She wept falling on her husband's body. Then the maids took her away. Then Vasistha, consulting with all the ministers, not wishing to perform the cremation rites without the sons nearby, preserved the king's mortal body in a trough filled with oil. Afterwards, they managed all state affairs. Seeing the king's body placed in the oil trough, the women of the inner palace and all the servants wept profusely. They cried, 'Alas! O great king! You who were grieving for Sri Rama, have now left us and gone to heaven. We have all become orphans. How can we live before Kaikeyi?' All the queens grieved thus, rolling on the ground. With the king's death, neither the palace women nor the city people cleaned their homes and courtyards, so the city became lustreless. They all abstained from food that day and became feeble. Then the sun set. All the residents of Ayodhya lost their peace of mind.

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Ayodhya, Kausalya, Vasishta, Rama, Kaikeyi

### Chapter 25: Twenty-fifth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 67-72
- Source PDF pages: 62, 63, 64
- Printed page numbers: 66, 67, 68
- Key entities: Markandeya, Bharata, Shatrughna, Kaikeyi, Kausalya, Yudhajit, Dasharatha, Rama, Lakshmana
- Places: Ayodhya, Kosala

**Summary:** The sages, led by Markandeya, entrust the responsibility of ruling the kingdom to Vasishtha. Vasishtha sends messengers to bring Bharata and Shatrughna back to Ayodhya. The messengers travel to Girivrajapura, the capital of Kekaya, where Bharata and Shatrughna are staying with their maternal grandfather. Bharata, upon receiving the message, sets out with a fourfold army and reaches Ayodhya in eight days. Entering the city, he learns of his father's death from his mother Kaikeyi and is overcome with grief.

#### Q1

**Question:** The sages led by Markandeya, saying that a kingdom without a king should not exist, entrusted the responsibility of thinking about this to whom?

**Options:**
- 1. Kausalya Devi
- 2. Vamadeva
- 3. The commander-in-chief
- 4. Vasishtha

**Correct answer:** Vasishtha

**Key entities:** Markandeya

#### Q2

**Question:** When sending messengers to bring Bharata and Shatrughna to Ayodhya, what did Vasishtha describe as the name of the city where Bharata's maternal uncle resides?

**Options:**
- 1. Vishala Nagara
- 2. Hastinapura
- 3. Girivrajapura
- 4. Dwaraka

**Correct answer:** Girivrajapura

**Key entities:** Bharata, Shatrughna, Ayodhya

#### Q3

**Question:** Having received the messengers' message, Bharata, accompanied by Shatrughna and a fourfold army, traveled without delay and reached Ayodhya in how many days?

**Answer:** Eight days

**Key entities:** Bharata, Shatrughna, Ayodhya

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the messengers sent by Vasishtha's order reach the Kekaya kingdom? In what manner did Bharata's journey towards Ayodhya proceed?

**Answer:** The messengers sent by Vasishtha's order traveled for several days and reached Girivrajapura, the capital city of the Kekaya king. There, they met Bharata and Shatrughna, who were spending time comfortably in the royal palace of Yudhajit. Then Bharata asked the messengers, 'Is our father, King Dasharatha, well? Are the great souls Rama and Lakshmana, and our three mothers, all well? Has no calamity befallen our mother Kaikeyi? Did she send any message?' The messengers replied, 'O best of men! All are well. Depart immediately.' Hearing the messengers' words, Bharata said, 'Alright, the messengers are urging me to travel to Ayodhya. With your permission, I will proceed to Ayodhya.' Thus, he requested his maternal grandfather and, obtaining permission from him and all others there, Bharata set out for Ayodhya with a fourfold army. Crossing mountains, forests, rivers, cities, and villages, he traveled for seven days and on the eighth day at sunrise entered the Kosala kingdom and saw Ayodhya. In this manner, Bharata's journey to Ayodhya proceeded.

**Key entities:** Bharata, Ayodhya, Shatrughna, Yudhajit, Dasharatha, Rama, Lakshmana, Kaikeyi, Kosala

#### Q5

**Question:** After entering the city of Ayodhya, how did Bharata learn the news of his father's death?

**Answer:** Entering Ayodhya, Bharata did not see his father in the royal palace, so he went to his mother Kaikeyi's chamber. Seeing Bharata, who had been at his grandfather's house until now, Kaikeyi rose from her seat with unbounded joy. Immediately, Bharata bowed at his mother's feet. Then Kaikeyi said, 'My son! Bharata! You have come from your grandfather's house, haven't you? Are your grandfather and maternal uncle all well there?' and asked about the welfare of everyone there. Then Bharata said, 'Mother! To see father, I went to his palace. He was not there. Is he in the palace of my elder mother Kausalya?' To Bharata's question, his mother replied, 'My son! Your father, the great soul, the treasure of virtuous men, has attained the supreme goal attained by all beings.' Hearing his mother's words about his father's death, he was overcome with terrible grief for his father and lamented with pitiful words, 'Oh father! Have you left me?' and fell to the ground, rolling. Then Kaikeyi lifted her son and consoled him. Bharata sobbed for a long time with overwhelming grief. Later, composing himself, he asked, 'Mother! What was the disease that caused the death of our noble father?' Then his mother told him the entire story and said, 'O son! Abandon your sorrow and grief, and with courage, rule this Kosala kingdom free of thorns.' Hearing her words, Bharata became stunned.

**Key entities:** Ayodhya, Bharata, Kaikeyi, Kausalya, Kosala

### Chapter 26: Twenty-Sixth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 73-78
- Source PDF pages: 64, 65, 66, 67
- Printed page numbers: 68, 69, 70, 71
- Key entities: Bharata, Kaikeyi, Rama, Dasharatha, Kausalya, Vasishta, Mandara, Sumantra
- Places: Sarayu

**Summary:** Bharata learns from Kaikeyi that his mother's actions caused Rama's exile and Dasaratha's death. He rebukes her and then, with Satrughna, goes to Kausalya. Vasistha advises Bharata to perform the funeral rites for Dasaratha. The funeral is conducted with full rituals. Later, Satrughna seizes Manthara, but Bharata stops him from harming her, citing Rama's disapproval of violence against women.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Bharata learned that his mother was the main cause of Rama's exile and his father's death, he rebuked her in many ways and said, 'Listen to what I am going to do about this wicked deed of yours.' What did Bharata tell his mother?

**Options:**
- 1. You rule this kingdom yourself
- 2. I will crown Satrughna
- 3. I will make Rama the king
- 4. I will hand over this kingdom to Vasistha

**Correct answer:** I will make Rama the king

**Key entities:** Bharata, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Learning of Bharata's arrival, Sumantra and other ministers came to Kaikeyi's palace. Bharata had already lost consciousness and did not regain it for a long time. Then, with whom did Bharata set out together with Satrughna?

**Options:**
- 1. To Vasistha
- 2. To Queen Kausalya
- 3. To the assembly of citizens and countrymen
- 4. To the chief servant

**Correct answer:** To Queen Kausalya

**Key entities:** Bharata, Sumantra, Kaikeyi, Kausalya

#### Q3

**Question:** While Bharata was overcome with grief, who told him, 'O prince, this is not the time for grief. The king's funeral rites must be performed so that he may attain the highest realms'?

**Answer:** Vasistha

**Key entities:** Bharata, Vasishta

#### Q4

**Question:** How were the funeral and post-funeral rites of King Dasaratha performed?

**Answer:** Following Vasistha's advice, Bharata composed himself to perform his father's funeral rites. Dasaratha's body was taken down from the oil vat. Seeing their lifeless father, Bharata and Satrughna wept for a long time. Then Vasistha told the princes to perform the funeral rites without distraction. As per the guru's words, Bharata urged the priests, chaplains, and teachers. Attendants placed the king's bier on a palanquin and took it to the cremation ground. There, on the pyre, they placed aloe, sandalwood, resin sticks, pine, padmaka, and deodar wood, and sprinkled various fragrant substances. Then, as the priests chanted Vedic hymns, Bharata lit the fire. Queen Kausalya and other royal wives came to the cremation ground with attendants. After the cremation was complete, they bathed in the Sarayu river and offered libations. For ten days, Bharata slept on the ground, suppressing his grief and performing the rites. On the eleventh day, he purified himself and performed the purificatory rites. On the twelfth day, he completed the sapindikarana and other shraddha rites, and gave abundant food donations for the king's attainment of the highest realms. They also donated gold ornaments, thousands of cows, and various goods and vehicles. Thus, Bharata and Satrughna completed King Dasaratha's funeral rites.

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Vasishta, Bharata, Kausalya, Sarayu

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Satrughna attempt to punish Manthara?

**Answer:** After completing all the post-funeral rites, while Bharata was thinking of going to Rama, Satrughna was also there. At that time, Manthara, adorned with ornaments and delighted, was standing at the eastern gate. Seeing her, some gatekeepers seized her and brought her to Satrughna, saying, 'O prince, this Manthara is the root cause of all these calamities. Do as you wish with this sinful woman.' Then Satrughna, learning everything, said to the attendants, 'She must suffer the consequences of her wickedness towards us,' and grabbed her tightly. The hunchback screamed in fear. Satrughna dragged her and threw her to the ground. Hearing Manthara's cries of mortal fear, Kaikeyi came to rescue her. Satrughna defied her, and Kaikeyi, frightened, sought refuge with Bharata. Then Bharata, seeing his mother and the enraged Satrughna, said, 'I ought to kill her, but I refrained because our brother Rama would not look upon the face of a matricide. Similarly, if we kill this hunchback, our brother would not even glance at us, calling us women-killers. So release her.' Following Bharata's words, Satrughna let Manthara go. Kaikeyi took the terrified Manthara to her palace.

**Key entities:** Mandara, Bharata, Rama, Kaikeyi

### Chapter 27: Twenty-seventh Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 79-84
- Source PDF pages: 67, 68, 69
- Printed page numbers: 71, 72, 73
- Key entities: Dasharatha, Bharata, Rama, Guha, Kausalya, Sumantra, Kaikeyi, Valmiki, Lakshmana, Sumitra
- Places: Ganga, Ayodhya

**Summary:** After King Dasharatha's funeral, Bharata is urged to become king but decides to bring Rama back. He sets out with a large entourage including queens and citizens, reaches the Ganges near Shringaberapura, and meets Guha, the Nishada king. Guha initially suspects Bharata's intentions but learns the truth and welcomes him. Bharata performs water offerings for his father and they camp for the night.

#### Q1

**Question:** On the morning of the fourteenth day after performing King Dasharatha's funeral rites, who said to Bharata, 'O prince! At present, you alone are fit to be king by law'?

**Options:**
- 1. Vasishtha
- 2. Kausalya
- 3. Citizens
- 4. Ministers

**Correct answer:** Ministers

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Bharata

#### Q2

**Question:** At whose call did Sumantra and the other ministers convene a full assembly?

**Options:**
- 1. Kausalya
- 2. Kaikeyi
- 3. Vasishtha
- 4. Bharata

**Correct answer:** Vasishtha

**Key entities:** Sumantra

#### Q3

**Question:** In the full assembly after King Dasharatha's funeral, who decided and said that Rama alone is fit to be king and that we should go with the fourfold army and invite him back?

**Answer:** Valmiki Maharshi

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Rama, Valmiki

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Bharata's journey with his retinue proceed up to the Ganges River in search of Rama?

**Answer:** Eager to see Rama and Lakshmana, Bharata set out with Kausalya, Sumitra, and Kaikeyi in suitable vehicles. Along with the fourfold army, the citizens of Ayodhya of all professions followed Bharata. Thus the entire city of Ayodhya moved. The soldiers joyfully traveled far on horses, elephants, and chariots and reached the banks of the Ganges near Shringaberapura. That city is the residence of Guha, Rama's friend. Seeing the Ganges with its sacred waters and noticing his army somewhat tired, Bharata told the ministers, 'As you wish, halt our army here. Tomorrow we will cross the Ganges. I will offer water oblations to our father with Ganges water.' Bharata did accordingly. By Bharata's command, Sumantra and others stopped the army and stationed them in various places. Then Bharata, thinking of a way to bring the great Rama back, spent that night there.

**Key entities:** Bharata, Ganga, Rama, Lakshmana, Kausalya, Sumitra, Kaikeyi, Ayodhya, Guha, Sumantra

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Guha, upon seeing Bharata encamped on the Ganges bank, receive and honor him?

**Answer:** Guha, the king of the Nishadas, seeing Bharata's army and the Kovidara flag flying on the chariots, thought, 'This is the army of the Ikshvaku kings. It seems Bharata has set out to permanently seize the kingdom and eliminate Rama.' He considered, 'If Bharata intends to bring joy to Rama, we will safely cross the Ganges with this army.' He instructed his men and took some food items and went personally to Bharata. There he first met Sumantra and learned the truth, becoming happy. Then Guha bowed to Bharata and said, 'O lord! If we had known of your arrival earlier, we would have welcomed and honored you. We are all your servants. We wish to offer you the fruits, roots, meat, and various forest grains we have gathered and honor you.' Bharata replied, 'Brother! You are a great friend of my elder brother Rama. Your wish is good. Your devotion, sincerity, and kind words have satisfied me. Just get us across the Ganges.' Then Guha said, 'O prince! I know all these forest paths. I and my people will ferry you across the Ganges and accompany you. Be at ease, accept our hospitality today with your army, and tomorrow we can cross the Ganges.' Bharata agreed, and everyone rested there that night.

**Key entities:** Guha, Bharata, Ganga, Rama, Sumantra

### Chapter 28: Twenty-Eighth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 85-90
- Source PDF pages: 69, 70, 71, 72
- Printed page numbers: 73, 74, 75, 76
- Key entities: Bharata, Guha, Rama, Atri, Valmiki, Gautama, Shatrughna, Kausalya, Dasharatha, Sita, Lakshmana
- Places: Ganga, Chitrakuta

**Summary:** Bharata and his army cross the Ganga with Guha's help and reach the hermitage of Sage Bharadvaja. Bharata seeks guidance to find Rama, and the sage advises him to rest and visit Rama at Chitrakuta the next day.

#### Q1

**Question:** During the intimate conversation between Bharata and Guha, which sage's hermitage did Bharata ask Guha to guide them to?

**Options:**
- 1. Sage Atri
- 2. Sage Bharadvaja
- 3. Sage Valmiki
- 4. Sage Gautama

**Correct answer:** Sage Bharadvaja

**Key entities:** Bharata, Guha

#### Q2

**Question:** Guha, while telling about Sri Rama, said, 'O prince! Your elder brother Sri Rama slept that night right under this tree, on a bed of grass.' What is the name of that tree?

**Options:**
- 1. Gara tree
- 2. Banyan tree
- 3. Ragi tree
- 4. Medi tree

**Correct answer:** Gara tree

**Key entities:** Guha, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** With what means did Guha transport Bharata's fourfold army across the Ganga?

**Answer:** Boats

**Key entities:** Guha, Bharata, Ganga

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Bharata, along with his retinue, cross the Ganga and reach Sage Bharadvaja's hermitage?

**Answer:** Bharata and Shatrughna slept at the very spot where Rama had slept on the Ganga bank. Waking before sunrise, they boarded five hundred boats arranged by Guha, carrying the preceptors including Vashishtha, the royal women including Kausalya, soldiers, relatives, friends, and all supplies. Some people shouted loudly about their belongings and boarded the boats hastily. Many boats were crowded with women, some were filled with horses, and others with carts and oxen. Gradually, some boats went to the opposite shore and returned. Then, elephants were loaded onto some boats. Some crossed by boat, others by swimming. The army, purified by the river waters, reached near Bharadvaja's hermitage after some time. Bharata left his army at a distance and went on foot with Vashishtha and other priests to the sage. The hermitage of Sage Bharadvaja looked charming with its leaf huts.

**Key entities:** Bharata, Ganga, Shatrughna, Rama, Guha, Kausalya

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Bharata and others see Sage Bharadvaja and speak with him?

**Answer:** Seeing Sage Bharadvaja from a distance, Bharata stopped all those following him and walked ahead with his priest Vashishtha in front. The great ascetic, seeing Vashishtha, rose from his seat and came forward. Then Bharata and Vashishtha introduced their gotra names and bowed. Sage Bharadvaja then offered arghya and padya to Bharata and Vashishtha and worshipped them. He asked about their welfare and recognized Bharata as Dasharatha's son. Then he asked Bharata, 'Your elder brother Sri Rama has been sent to the forest, hasn't he? What is the reason for your coming here?' Bharata, shedding tears, explained everything. Then Sage Bharadvaja said, 'O best of men! Your goal and your resolve are all good. I know the truth of your intention. May it become firm in you! May your fame spread throughout the earth! The righteous Rama, along with Sita and Lakshmana, is living in the regions of Chitrakuta mountain. Therefore, O Bharata! You may go to your elder brother Sri Rama tomorrow. Today, stay here with your ministers and retinue. This is my wish.' Then Bharata said, 'O lord of sages! I bow to your command,' and decided to stay at the hermitage for that night.

**Key entities:** Bharata, Dasharatha, Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Chitrakuta

### Chapter 29: Twenty-ninth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 91-96
- Source PDF pages: 72, 73, 74
- Printed page numbers: 76, 77, 78
- Key entities: Bharata, Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Brahma, Kubera
- Places: Chitrakuta, Ayodhya

**Summary:** Bharata, eager to see Rama, approaches sage Bharadvaja who tells him that Chitrakuta is three and a half yojanas away. Meanwhile, Rama, Sita, and Lakshmana enjoy the natural beauty of Chitrakuta and the Mandakini river. Lakshmana spots Bharata's approaching army and suspects hostile intent, but Rama remains calm.

#### Q1

**Question:** Having decided to offer hospitality to Bharata and his entire retinue, sage Bharadvaja entered the fire-sanctuary, performed achamana, and whom did he first invite?

**Options:**
- 1. Vishvakarma
- 2. Brahma
- 3. Parashakti
- 4. Annapurna Devi

**Correct answer:** Vishvakarma

**Key entities:** Bharata

#### Q2

**Question:** Taking leave from sage Bharadvaja, with a desire to see Rama, Bharata approached the sage and asked, 'O great one! Where is my elder brother? How far is that place from here?' What distance did sage Bharadvaja say Chitrakuta, where Rama was, was from there?

**Options:**
- 1. Five yojanas
- 2. Four and a half yojanas
- 3. Three and a half yojanas
- 4. Two yojanas

**Correct answer:** Three and a half yojanas

**Key entities:** Rama, Bharata, Chitrakuta

#### Q3

**Question:** With a desire to see Rama, Bharata along with his army, following the clues given by sage Bharadvaja, was walking on the slopes of Chitrakuta mountain when some servants came and showed a sign to Bharata, saying Rama might be there. What could that sign be?

**Answer:** Smoke

**Key entities:** Rama, Bharata, Chitrakuta

#### Q4

**Question:** When Bharata went to the Chitrakuta region with all his people, how were Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana situated?

**Answer:** Rama, accompanied by Sita and Lakshmana, had begun his forest exile about a month ago. Gradually, Rama, enjoying the natural beauties of Chitrakuta, showed the wonderful mountain splendors to Sita and began to delight in them. Then Rama said to his wife, 'O beautiful one! Although kingship is far from me, and friends who wish me well are not near, my mind, absorbed in enjoying the delightful scenes of these Chitrakuta mountains, is not troubled by those matters. Sita! By performing forest exile, I have repaid my father's debt by ruling that land. At the same time, I have done good to my brother Bharata. I have obtained these two results. By happily spending these fourteen years following the rules of forest exile, our family's fame and prestige will increase further.' Thus describing the splendors of the region to Sita, he once went with Sita to the banks of the Mandakini river. Showing her that river with its sacred waters, he said, 'Sita! This bank of the Mandakini river, with its sandbanks, swans sporting there, cranes, and lotuses blooming in the water, is very delightful. The trees on both sides of the river, laden with fruits and flowers, make this place resemble Kubera's Saugandhika lake.' Speaking thus, with Sita as his companion, Rama roamed about the Chitrakuta mountain regions and the banks of the Mandakini river.

**Key entities:** Bharata, Chitrakuta, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Kubera

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Rama and Lakshmana recognize the arrival of Bharata and others?

**Answer:** While Rama was sitting on a level ground in the leaf-hut area, the sounds of Bharata's approaching army and the dust raised by their feet suddenly became visible. Meanwhile, the elephants and wild animals in the forest, frightened by the tumultuous sounds of the great army, fled from their herds. Then Rama, hearing the sounds caused by the movement of the army, looked at Lakshmana and said, 'O Saumitri! It seems some prince is coming this way, look.' As soon as his elder brother spoke, Lakshmana climbed a nearby tall tree and looked in all directions. He saw a great army towards the north. Observing the army with its four divisions and the flags flying on the chariots, he said, 'Brother! Bharata is coming here with his army. You take up your bow and arrows and be ready. He, having been crowned in Ayodhya, is coming here to kill you in order to remove you as an obstacle to his rule. O elder brother! We have endured many insults so far. I have been controlling the fire of anger within me. Now his death at my hands is certain. I do not consider killing Bharata a sin.' Thus Lakshmana was agitated with anger. At that time, Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana were in that state.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Bharata, Ayodhya, Sita

### Chapter 30: Thirtieth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 97-102
- Source PDF pages: 74, 75, 76, 77
- Printed page numbers: 78, 79, 80, 81
- Key entities: Bharata, Lakshmana, Rama, Shatrughna, Dasharatha, Sita, Sumantra, Indra, Brahma
- Places: Chitrakuta, Ayodhya

**Summary:** Bharata arrives at Chitrakuta with his army. Lakshmana, seeing the army, suspects Bharata's intentions and urges Rama to prepare for battle. Rama rebukes Lakshmana, stating he would not desire any position unrighteously. Bharata, leaving his army, approaches Rama's hermitage on foot. He climbs a tree to spot Rama's dwelling. Upon meeting, Bharata and Shatrughna prostrate at Rama's feet. Rama, clad in bark garments and deer skin, questions Bharata about their father. Bharata informs Rama of King Dasharatha's death. Rama, overwhelmed with grief, performs the funeral rites with Sita, Lakshmana, and Sumantra at the Mandakini River.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Lakshmana said, 'Bharata is coming with his army. We should be ready with weapons in hand,' what position did Rama say he would not desire unrighteously?

**Options:**
- 1. Even the position of a king
- 2. Even the position of Indra
- 3. Even the position of a Lokapala
- 4. Even the position of Brahma

**Correct answer:** Even the position of Indra

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Bharata, Rama, Indra

#### Q2

**Question:** When Bharata came to the Chitrakuta region, he halted all his armies at one place, proceeded on foot, and climbed a tree to look for Rama's whereabouts. What is the name of that tree?

**Options:**
- 1. Maddi tree
- 2. Deodar tree
- 3. Chandrag tree
- 4. Nara epi tree

**Correct answer:** Maddi tree

**Key entities:** Bharata, Chitrakuta, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** When Bharata and Shatrughna saw Rama in the leaf hut and prostrated at his feet, Rama was wearing bark garments. What was he wearing as an upper garment?

**Answer:** Deer skin

**Key entities:** Bharata, Shatrughna, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the meeting of Rama and Bharata take place?

**Answer:** Bharata, wearing bark cloth, with matted hair, prostrated on the ground. Rama lifted him, embraced him, seated him beside him, and asked, 'My son! Bharata! Where is our father? Why have you come here instead of serving him?' Then Rama asked about the welfare of the gurus and mothers. Afterwards, he spoke to Bharata about many royal duties. Hearing Rama's words, Bharata said, 'Brother! Serving you is my supreme duty. If I am separated from that, what use are other royal duties? Elder brother! No matter how many sons a king has, the eldest son is worthy of the throne. This is the eternal tradition in our dynasty. You, being the eldest son, should come to Ayodhya with me and be crowned. Our father, King Dasharatha, died when I was in the Kekaya kingdom, as soon as you left for the forest. Unable to bear your departure to the forest, the king ascended to heaven. I and Shatrughna performed the funeral rites for father. You were dear as life to our father. He gave up his life thinking of you. The elders say that if a beloved son offers sesame and water oblations, the ancestors attain eternal worlds.' Thus Rama and Bharata spoke about their father's death.

**Key entities:** Rama, Bharata, Ayodhya, Dasharatha, Shatrughna

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Rama offer the rice-ball and water oblations to his father?

**Answer:** Hearing the sorrowful news of his father's death from Bharata, Rama became motionless. On hearing that heart-rending news, Rama lost consciousness and fell to the ground. Then Sita, Lakshmana, Bharata, and Shatrughna performed soothing ministrations. Gradually regaining consciousness, he wept and lamented piteously. Rama said, 'Sita, your father-in-law, who cherished you with great affection, has gone to heaven. Lakshmana! We have become fatherless.' As Rama spoke, the four brothers shed continuous tears. Then Bharata said, 'Brother! Perform the water oblations for our father.' Then Rama consoled the weeping Janaki and said, 'Lakshmana! Bring the paste of garcinia seeds, a cloth, and an upper garment. Let us go to offer oblations to our father.' Taking Sita, followed by Lakshmana and Sumantra, they went to the Mandakini River, bathed in the holy waters, and offered oblations saying, 'Father! May these waters bring you satisfaction!' Then Rama offered sesame and water oblations and performed the rice-ball offering. Afterwards, Rama returned to the leaf hut. Hearing the sounds of lamentation from the leaf hut area, the soldiers realized that Bharata had met Rama, and they all came in that direction and saw Rama. Rama welcomed all who came to him.

**Key entities:** Rama, Bharata, Sita, Lakshmana, Shatrughna, Sumantra

### Chapter 31: Thirty-first Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 103-108
- Source PDF pages: 77, 78, 79
- Printed page numbers: 81, 82, 83
- Key entities: Bharata, Rama, Jabali, Kausalya, Guha, Indra, Kubera, Brahma, Kaikeyi, Dasharatha, Sita, Lakshmana
- Places: Ayodhya, Kosala

**Summary:** Bharata, accompanied by Sage Vasishtha, arrives at Rama's hermitage and pleads with Rama to return to Ayodhya and accept the throne. Rama refuses, citing his duty to uphold his father's promise. Bharata threatens to fast unto death. Sage Jabali presents a materialistic argument to convince Rama, but Rama remains steadfast. The chapter includes Rama's discourse on dharma and his explanation of the events leading to his exile.

#### Q1

**Question:** Who came to the leaf hut with Sage Vasishtha, and later, upon seeing the rice balls placed by Sri Rama for the ancestral rite near the Mandakini river, grieved excessively?

**Options:**
- 1. Jabali
- 2. Guha
- 3. Bharata
- 4. Queen Kausalya

**Correct answer:** Queen Kausalya

**Key entities:** Rama, Kausalya

#### Q2

**Question:** When Bharata prayed to his elder brother Sri Rama to return to Ayodhya and accept the kingdom, Rama told Bharata that upholding the father's word is our dharma. To whom did Rama compare their father?

**Options:**
- 1. Indra
- 2. Kubera
- 3. Brahma
- 4. Ishvara

**Correct answer:** Indra

**Key entities:** Bharata, Rama, Ayodhya, Indra

#### Q3

**Question:** Despite Bharata's earnest entreaties, Rama declared he would adhere only to his father's command. Referring to a king who, in ancient times, performed a sacrifice at Gaya Kshetra for the manes and declared that a son who uplifts his parents from the hell called Punnamanaraka is a true son, which king did Rama mention to Bharata?

**Answer:** Gaya

**Key entities:** Bharata, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** With what reasoning did Rama explain to Bharata that making their father truthful is their duty?

**Answer:** Bharata prayerfully requested Sri Rama to return to Ayodhya and be crowned. Then Sri Rama said, 'Brother Bharata! You were born to Kaikeyi from the king of kings, Dasaratha. Your words are appropriate to your stature. Brother! Long ago, when our father married your mother, he promised your grandfather that the son born to Kaikeyi would receive the kingdom. Later, during the war between gods and demons, pleased with your mother's service, the king promised her two boons. Accordingly, your mother made the king swear and asked for two boons: that you be crowned and that I be sent to the forest. The king agreed. What fault is there in your mother? The king commanded me. I came to the forest with Sita and Lakshmana. You too should respect father's word and be crowned immediately. Follow my words and free the king from his debt to Kaikeyi. Do not cause him to attain hell.' Thus Sri Rama in many ways instructed Bharata that it is proper for him to bear the burden of the kingdom.

**Key entities:** Rama, Bharata, Ayodhya, Kaikeyi, Dasharatha, Sita, Lakshmana

#### Q5

**Question:** What kind of argument did Jabali, one of Dasaratha's ministers, present to convince Sri Rama?

**Answer:** While the righteous Sri Rama was thus consoling Bharata, Jabali, one of Dasaratha's ministers, came forward and said, 'O Rama! What you said is fine. But you are wise and mentally strong. Do not let such futile thoughts enter your mind like an ignorant person. In this world, who is related to whom? All human relationships are momentary. Therefore, good people should not develop attachment to those bonds. O best of men! This forest life is very difficult. It is not proper for someone like you to abandon the wealth inherited from your father and choose such a difficult path. O wise one! Do not think that a father's word is inviolable. Enjoy the immediate benefit of the kingdom that is before you. Do not believe in unseen otherworldly benefits. O Rama! The pleasures of this world are real. There is no afterlife. Follow the authority of those who say this. Accept this Kosala kingdom as Bharata is entreating.' Thus Jabali presented his atheistic argument to Sri Rama.

**Key entities:** Jabali, Dasharatha, Rama, Bharata, Kosala

### Chapter 32: Thirty-second Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 109-114
- Source PDF pages: 79, 80, 81, 82
- Printed page numbers: 83, 84, 85, 86
- Key entities: Jabali, Rama, Vasishta, Bharata, Kausalya, Guha, Shatrughna, Lakshmana, Sumantra, Dasharatha, Kaikeyi
- Places: Ayodhya, Chitrakuta, Yamuna, Ganga

**Summary:** Jabali's atheistic arguments are refuted by Rama, who upholds truth. Vasistha also advises Rama to return to Ayodhya. Bharata threatens a hunger strike, and Rama gives his sandals to Bharata. Bharata returns to Ayodhya with the sandals, lamenting the city's desolate state.

#### Q1

**Question:** Who pacified Rama by saying that Jabali is not an atheist, but spoke thus only to persuade him to return to Ayodhya, while Rama was condemning Jabali's atheism and emphasizing the importance of truth?

**Options:**
- 1. Vasistha
- 2. Kausalya
- 3. Bharadvaja Maharshi
- 4. Guha

**Correct answer:** Vasistha

**Key entities:** Rama, Jabali, Ayodhya, Vasishta

#### Q2

**Question:** When Rama did not agree to return to Ayodhya despite Vasistha's advice, Bharata said he would spread darbha grass before Rama and sit on it fasting. Whom did he ask to bring the darbha grass?

**Options:**
- 1. Shatrughna
- 2. Jabali
- 3. Lakshmana
- 4. Sumantra

**Correct answer:** Shatrughna

**Key entities:** Rama, Ayodhya, Vasishta, Bharata, Shatrughna

#### Q3

**Question:** Upon Bharata's request, Rama gave his sandals. Bharata then said, 'Brother, until you complete your fourteen-year exile and return to take up the burden of the kingdom, I will rule by these sandals.' He bowed to the sandals, received them, placed them on the howdah of an elephant, and took them. What was the name of that elephant?

**Answer:** Shatrunjaya

**Key entities:** Bharata, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Bharata return to the city of Ayodhya?

**Answer:** Bharata took the sandals from the elephant howdah, placed them on his head, and with Shatrughna, his mothers, gurus, ministers, citizens, and the entire army, took leave of Rama and set out for Ayodhya. He reached the hermitage of Bharadvaja Maharshi near Chitrakuta, bowed to the sage, narrated all that happened in the presence of Rama at Chitrakuta, took leave, and proceeded towards Ayodhya. The great army with four divisions, along with palanquins, carts, and other vehicles, followed Bharata. They traveled some distance, crossed the Yamuna river, then saw the holy Ganga. With the help of Guha, they crossed the Ganga and reached Shringaberipura. There they bade farewell to Guha and set out from Shringaberipura. After traveling some distance, Bharata saw Ayodhya. Seeing the city bereft of his father and brothers, he said to the charioteer Sumantra, 'Sumantra! This Ayodhya is desolate and has lost its charm. There is no joy among the people here.' Thus Bharata entered Ayodhya.

**Key entities:** Bharata, Ayodhya, Shatrughna, Rama, Chitrakuta, Yamuna, Ganga, Guha, Sumantra

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Bharata suffer upon seeing the miserable condition of Ayodhya?

**Answer:** When Bharata entered Ayodhya, the city was devoid of splendor. Due to the death of King Dasaratha and Rama's exile to the forest, Ayodhya was grief-stricken, dejected, lustreless, and bereft of beauty. Like the sky when clouds cover the moon and stars, Ayodhya had become pale. Ayodhya was shattered by the force of Kaikeyi's boons. As Bharata rode in his chariot through the royal streets, he said to Sumantra, 'Previously, when I walked through the streets of Ayodhya, the sounds of veenas, flutes, mridangams, and cymbals were heard. The city was fragrant with sandalwood, aloe, musk, and flowers. Now none of that exists. The shouts of palanquin bearers, the neighing of horses, the trumpeting of elephants, and the rattle of chariot wheels used to be heard, but now they are absent. All the beauty and grandeur of this Ayodhya have gone to the forests with my brother Rama. There is nothing we can do but wait for the day Rama returns from the forest.' Speaking thus in many ways, Bharata entered the royal palace. Seeing the inner apartments empty, Bharata shed tears.

**Key entities:** Bharata, Ayodhya, Dasharatha, Rama, Kaikeyi, Sumantra

### Chapter 33: Thirty-third Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 115-119
- Source PDF pages: 82, 83, 84, 85
- Printed page numbers: 86, 87, 88, 89
- Key entities: Bharata, Rama, Khara, Atri, Sita, Lakshmana, Maricha, Ravana, Subahu, Kausalya, Janaka, Shiva, Dasharatha
- Places: Chitrakuta, Dandaka Forest, Ayodhya, Mithila

**Summary:** Bharata decides to stay in Nandigrama during Rama's exile. Rama learns from sages about the demon Khara troubling Chitrakuta. Rama leaves Chitrakuta and reaches the hermitage of Sage Atri. Sita narrates her marriage story to Anasuya. Rama, Sita, and Lakshmana leave Atri's hermitage and enter the Dandaka forest.

#### Q1

**Question:** Bharata, placing all his mothers in the inner apartments, sorrow-stricken, told his guru Vasishtha, 'O revered teacher! I cannot stay in Ayodhya without Rama. Therefore, I will go to a village near here and stay there for these fourteen years.' What is the name of that village?

**Options:**
- 1. Shringaberipura
- 2. Nandigrama
- 3. Vaishali
- 4. Karusha

**Correct answer:** Nandigrama

**Key entities:** Bharata, Ayodhya, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Rama lived for some time in the Chitrakuta region. One day, Rama noticed that the hermitage dwellers in that area were planning to leave the region. He asked a great sage among them the reason. The sage replied, 'The torment of demons has increased in this area. One of them is very powerful. Rama! You too come with us, go far away, and build hermitages.' What is the name of that powerful demon?

**Options:**
- 1. Maricha
- 2. Ravana
- 3. Subahu
- 4. Khara

**Correct answer:** Khara

**Key entities:** Rama, Chitrakuta, Khara

#### Q3

**Question:** After all the sages left those hermitage sites, Rama thought in various ways. He remembered that Bharata, Kausalya, and all his people had met him here. Haunted by those memories, he decided to leave that place. Traveling some distance, he reached the hermitage of a great sage. Whose hermitage was that?

**Answer:** Atri

**Key entities:** Rama, Bharata, Kausalya, Atri

#### Q4

**Question:** To whom and in what manner did Sita narrate her marriage story?

**Answer:** From the Chitrakuta mountain region, Rama along with Sita and Lakshmana reached the hermitage of Sage Atri. After bowing to the sage and introducing himself, the sage welcomed Rama like his own son. Then Sage Atri introduced Sita to his wife Anasuya. Anasuya greatly welcomed and honored Sita. In the course of conversation, Anasuya taught Sita many duties of a devoted wife. At Anasuya's request, Sita narrated her marriage story: 'O mother! King Janaka, the lord of Mithila, is my father. While plowing the earth for a sacrifice to obtain children, I emerged from a furrow in a casket. King Janaka took me in his arms and raised me with great affection, saying 'She is my daughter.' When I came of age, my father proclaimed a swayamvara: 'I will give my daughter to him who strings the bow of Shiva that has been in our lineage since the time of Devarata.' Princes from various countries came but could not string it and returned. Then Rama, the elder of Rama and Lakshmana who came with Sage Vishwamitra, strung the bow and won me. Then my father invited King Dasharatha, my father-in-law, and celebrated my marriage with Rama with great pomp.' Thus Sita narrated her marriage story to Anasuya.

**Key entities:** Sita, Chitrakuta, Rama, Lakshmana, Atri, Janaka, Mithila, Shiva, Dasharatha

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Rama leave the hermitage of Sage Atri and enter the Dandaka forest?

**Answer:** Hearing Sita's marriage story, Anasuya rejoiced and said, 'O Sita! Now adorn yourself with these divine garments and ornaments I have given you. I wish to see you thus adorned and be pleased.' Sita wore those garments, ornaments, and garlands and bowed to Anasuya. Then Sita went before Rama. Seeing Sita adorned with the gifts given by Anasuya out of love, Rama was greatly pleased. Rama and Lakshmana rejoiced that Sita had received honors not given to any human. Then Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana accepted the hospitality offered by the ascetics, spent the night there, and rose at dawn. Taking leave of the ascetics, they asked for the path to Dandaka forest. Following the path they indicated, Rama, the subduer of enemies, along with Sita and Lakshmana, entered the dense Dandaka forest like the sun in a cloud bank.

**Key entities:** Rama, Atri, Dandaka Forest, Sita, Lakshmana

### Chapter 34: Thirty-fourth Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 1-6
- Source PDF pages: 85, 86, 87
- Printed page numbers: 89, 90, 91
- Key entities: Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Viradha, Indra, Brahma, Kabandha, Maricha, Dushana, Atri
- Places: Dandaka Forest, Kailasa

**Summary:** Rama, Sita, and Lakshmana enter the Dandaka forest, visit hermitages, encounter the demon Viradha, and then proceed to Sage Sharabhanga's ashrama where the sage immolates himself after Rama's arrival. Rama then reassures the sages and heads to Sage Sutikshna's ashrama.

#### Q1

**Question:** Rama entered the Dandaka forest, which is impossible for ordinary people to tread. There he saw many hermitages. The chanting of the Vedas during sacrificial rituals resounded throughout the place. With which realm is it compared?

**Options:**
- 1. Indra's realm
- 2. Brahma's realm
- 3. Vaikuntha
- 4. Kailasa

**Correct answer:** Indra's realm

**Key entities:** Rama, Dandaka Forest, Indra

#### Q2

**Question:** After receiving hospitality from the sages, Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana spent the night in the hermitage and at sunrise took leave and proceeded. After going some distance, they saw a demon. What was his name?

**Options:**
- 1. Kabandha
- 2. Maricha
- 3. Viradha
- 4. Dushana

**Correct answer:** Viradha

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Viradha

#### Q3

**Question:** Viradha, who was fatally struck by Rama and Lakshmana, said that in his previous birth he was a Gandharva. By being slain by you, I have been freed from a curse. What was Viradha's name in his previous birth?

**Answer:** Tumburu

**Key entities:** Viradha, Rama, Lakshmana

#### Q4

**Question:** After Rama, along with Sita and Lakshmana, came to Sharabhanga's ashrama, what happened there?

**Answer:** Leaving Atri Maharshi's ashrama, Rama walked quickly and reached Sharabhanga Maharshi's ashrama area by evening. From outside the ashrama, Rama saw a wondrous person beside Sharabhanga Maharshi. Rama realized that divine person was Indra. Then Rama told Lakshmana, 'Brother! You and your sister-in-law stay here; I will go inside and find out who that divine person is,' and entered the ashrama. Seeing this, Indra told Sharabhanga Maharshi, 'O sage! Rama is coming here. I should not be seen by him now; there is still some time for that.' Then Indra left. Then Rama, along with Sita and Lakshmana, met Sharabhanga Maharshi. The sage welcomed them cordially and offered hospitality. Then Sharabhanga Maharshi asked Rama to stay in his ashrama that day. Then Rama said, 'O sage! Please tell us a suitable place for us to live in this forest.' The sage replied, 'O Rama! The greatly radiant sage Sutikshna is nearby. You can meet him and arrange your residence according to his guidance.' Then the sage said, 'O Rama! I knew you would come here. I was waiting to give up this body after your sight. Now I am blessed to have seen you.' Then the sage established the fire, chanted the Brahma Veda mantras, and entered the fire. The fire consumed his body. Rama witnessed that scene.

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Atri, Indra, Brahma

#### Q5

**Question:** From Sharabhanga's ashrama, where did Rama go and in what manner?

**Answer:** After Sharabhanga Maharshi passed away, all the sages in the ashrama came to Rama and said, 'O Rama! We are distressed and beseech you. We are unable to bear the torments of the cruel demons in this region. We seek refuge in you. Protect us from those demons.' Rama replied, 'O great souls! I entered this forest for exile. But it seems I entered this forest under the pretext of fulfilling my father's command, in order to eradicate the harm the demons cause you. My coming here is providential for the accomplishment of your purpose. Therefore, my exile will be greatly fruitful. We consider it our duty to destroy the demons who are enemies of the ascetics. From now on, you will see the valor of us brothers.' Thus Rama gave assurance to the sages and, accompanied by Sita and Lakshmana, set out for the ashrama of Sage Sutikshna.

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Lakshmana

### Chapter 35: Thirty-fifth Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 7-11
- Source PDF pages: 87, 88, 89, 90
- Printed page numbers: 91, 92, 93, 94
- Key entities: Rama, Atri, Agastya, Jatayu, Sita, Lakshmana, Yama
- Places: Dandaka Forest, Panchavati, Chitrakuta

**Summary:** Rama, after receiving hospitality from Sage Sutikshna, asks for a suitable place to stay. Sutikshna advises him to go to Atri's hermitage. Rama then travels through Dandaka forest, encountering various sages and hearing the story of Vatapi and Ilvala from Agastya. He also meets the bird Jatayu.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Rama came to the hermitage of Sage Sutikshna and accepted the hospitality, what did Sage Sutikshna tell him when asked for a suitable place to live?

**Options:**
- 1. He told him to go to Atri's hermitage
- 2. He told him to stay in his own hermitage
- 3. He told him to go to Sharabhanga's hermitage
- 4. He told him to go to Chitrakuta

**Correct answer:** Panchavati

**Key entities:** Rama, Panchavati

#### Q2

**Question:** Who gave Rama some beneficial advice as he left Sutikshna's hermitage and traveled through Dandaka forest?

**Options:**
- 1. Sita
- 2. Lakshmana
- 3. Sages
- 4. Jatayu

**Correct answer:** Chitrakuta

**Key entities:** Rama, Dandaka Forest, Chitrakuta

#### Q3

**Question:** While walking through beautiful forest lands, what did Rama tell Sita that he would not abandon as long as life was in his body?

**Answer:** The question is as per Agastya's instruction, while traveling on the path they had chosen to establish their dwelling, a bird appeared and introduced itself, saying 'I will stay with you.' What is the name of that bird? Answer is in the answer column.

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Agastya

#### Q4

**Question:** After leaving Sutikshna's hermitage, which hermitages did Sita and Rama visit?

**Answer:** During the journey through Dandaka forest, Rama, along with all those following him, walked forward seeing the mountain slopes, rivers, and forest beauty. After traveling some distance, they saw a beautiful lake. Finding the place very charming, Rama heard melodious music there. Seeing no human movement, he asked the sage Dharmabhrita who was following him, 'What is the reason for this music?' The sage replied, 'O Rama! This lake was created by the sage Mandakarni through his penance. To disturb his severe penance, the gods sent apsaras, but the sage, by his power, built a house inside this lake and lives there. Their songs and dances are the sounds we hear now.' Hearing this, Rama looked around the hermitage and thought, 'This place is suitable for our dwelling.' So, along with Sita and Lakshmana, he stayed there happily for some time, receiving the worship of the sages. Thus, Rama spent ten years living comfortably in various hermitages. One day, Rama returned to Sutikshna's hermitage with all his followers. After meeting the sage and receiving his hospitality, he learned the path to Agastya's hermitage from him. On the way, he visited the hermitage of Sudarshana, Agastya's brother, and following the path shown by that sage, they reached Agastya's hermitage.

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Dandaka Forest, Lakshmana, Agastya

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Rama narrate the story of Vatapi and Ilvala to his brother Lakshmana?

**Answer:** While going to Sudarshana's hermitage with all his followers, Rama told his brother on the way: 'Lakshmana! Once upon a time, two brothers named Vatapi and Ilvala used to kill ascetics by their magical arts. Vatapi would become a goat, and after killing it and cooking it appropriately for a shraddha, Ilvala would disguise himself as a Brahmin, invite Brahmins for a shraddha, and serve them the meat of Vatapi. After the ascetics finished eating, Ilvala would call out, 'O Vatapi, come out!' Vatapi would then tear open the stomachs of the ascetics and come out, and both brothers would eat the flesh of the dead Brahmins. Knowing this, Agastya one day went to Vatapi's house for a shraddha meal. After the meal, Ilvala called out, 'O Vatapi, come out!' Then Agastya said, 'Where is Vatapi now? He has been digested and gone to Yama's abode.' Enraged, Ilvala attacked Agastya, but Agastya, with a roar of anger, burned him to ashes. Thus, Sage Agastya saved the ascetics from the torment of Vatapi and Ilvala.' Talking thus about Agastya, Rama and Lakshmana continued their journey.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Agastya, Yama

### Chapter 36: Thirty-Sixth Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 12-17
- Source PDF pages: 90, 91, 92
- Printed page numbers: 94, 95, 96
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Agastya, Jatayu, Surpanakha, Ravana, Indra, Khara, Dushana
- Places: Panchavati, Chitrakuta, Godavari

**Summary:** Rama, Lakshmana, and Sita visit Sage Agastya's hermitage. Agastya advises them to reside in Panchavati. On the way, they meet the vulture Jatayu. Lakshmana builds a beautiful leaf hut (parnashala) in Panchavati. The demoness Shurpanakha enters the hermitage and propositions Rama, threatening to kill Sita and Lakshmana.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Sri Rama came to Agastya's hermitage, through whom did he inform Sage Agastya of their arrival?

**Options:**
- 1. The Dharmabhrita who came with him
- 2. Sita Devi
- 3. That hermitage dweller
- 4. Lakshmana

**Correct answer:** Lakshmana

**Key entities:** Rama, Agastya, Lakshmana

#### Q2

**Question:** What is the name of the place that Agastya indicated as suitable for them to reside, as requested by Sri Rama?

**Options:**
- 1. Panchavati
- 2. Chitrakuta
- 3. Badarikavana
- 4. Siddhashrama

**Correct answer:** Panchavati

**Key entities:** Agastya, Rama, Panchavati

#### Q3

**Question:** As per Agastya's instruction, while Rama and others were traveling on the path they had chosen to establish their residence, a bird appeared in the middle of the way, introduced itself, and said 'I will be with you.' What is the name of that bird?

**Answer:** Jatayu

**Key entities:** Agastya, Rama, Jatayu

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Rama and others set up the leaf hut (parnashala) in Panchavati and reside there?

**Answer:** After entering the Panchavati region, Rama said to Lakshmana, 'We have come to the place suggested by Sage Agastya. This place is very beautiful. Choose a level area where we can get water, fruits, flowers, firewood, and darbha grass without shortage for our fire rituals.' Lakshmana surveyed the entire area and identified a place with all facilities that pleased him. He showed that place to his elder brother and with his permission, on the banks of the Godavari river, he built walls with the mud he dug. He erected beautiful, strong bamboo poles as pillars, placed long bamboo poles on them, spread tender jammi branches, tied them firmly with strong palm fiber, covered them with darbha grass, reeds, and crow-bamboo leaves, and thus built the leaf hut strong and beautiful. Then he leveled the ground nicely. Afterwards, Lakshmana went to the Godavari river, bathed, collected flowers and fruits, and returned. Then he showed the leaf hut to Sita and Rama. Sri Rama was pleased, performed Vastu puja for the hut, and entered it with Sita and Lakshmana. In that Panchavati region, Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana lived peacefully in the leaf hut for some time.

**Key entities:** Rama, Panchavati, Lakshmana, Agastya, Godavari, Sita

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the demoness named Shurpanakha behave when she entered the leaf hut area?

**Answer:** After Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana entered the leaf hut, they were happily performing their daily duties. At that time, by fate, a demoness named Shurpanakha came to that place. She was Ravana's sister. Seeing Sri Ramachandra, who was like a treasure of beauty like Manmatha and shining with the splendor of Indra, she became overcome with lust. Then the repulsive-looking Shurpanakha said, 'O handsome one! You are in the guise of an ascetic. You are accompanied by your wife and carry a bow and arrows. Why have you come to this region, which is the abode of demons?' Then Sri Rama told his story. Later, Rama asked, 'I think you are a demoness. Who are you?' She replied, 'My name is Shurpanakha. Ravana, the lord of demons, is my brother. He is a great hero. Khara, Dushana, and others who roam this region are also my brothers. They are immensely powerful. I possess many powers and abilities. Seeing your wonderful form, I have become lustful. I desire to have you as my husband. What need do you have of Sita? Her form is ugly. I will eat this human woman. I will do the same to your brother. They will not be obstacles for us. O handsome one! Then we two can roam happily in these forests and on mountain peaks.' Thus, with intoxicated eyes, the demoness Shurpanakha behaved after entering the leaf hut area.

**Key entities:** Surpanakha, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Ravana, Indra, Khara, Dushana

### Chapter 37: Thirty-seventh Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 18-23
- Source PDF pages: 92, 93, 94, 95
- Printed page numbers: 96, 97, 98, 99
- Key entities: Surpanakha, Lakshmana, Khara, Rama, Maricha, Subahu, Dushana, Trishira
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** Shurpanakha, after being disfigured by Lakshmana, seeks refuge with Khara. Khara sends fourteen warriors against Rama, who kills them. Shurpanakha returns to Khara, who then prepares for battle with his army, ignoring ominous signs.

#### Q1

**Question:** After Rama stopped Shurpanakha with a roar and told Lakshmana, 'This one is evil-natured. Why jest with her? Disfigure her,' Lakshmana cut off her nose and ears. Bleeding and wailing, whom did she approach?

**Options:**
- 1. Maricha
- 2. Subahu
- 3. Khara
- 4. Sundudunu

**Correct answer:** Khara

**Key entities:** Rama, Surpanakha, Lakshmana, Khara

#### Q2

**Question:** Hearing Shurpanakha's words, how many rakshasa warriors did Khara send against Rama?

**Options:**
- 1. Twelve
- 2. Ten thousand
- 3. Fourteen thousand
- 4. Fourteen

**Correct answer:** Fourteen

**Key entities:** Surpanakha, Khara, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** Seeing that Rama had killed the fourteen warriors sent by Khara, Shurpanakha wept and wailed and went again to whom?

**Answer:** Khara

**Key entities:** Rama, Khara, Surpanakha

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Khara behave upon hearing Shurpanakha's words?

**Answer:** Seeing Shurpanakha return to him as if she were the harbinger of destruction of all rakshasas, Khara said, 'Shurpanakha! Why are you crying? The fourteen warriors I sent with you are equal to me. What happened to those great warriors?' Shurpanakha replied, 'O brother! Rama has killed all the warriors you sent. Moreover, if you do not kill that Rama who cut off my nose and ears today, I will give up my life before you. It is not enough to boast that you are a hero. Kill that mere human Rama.' Fainting and falling, Shurpanakha was consoled by Khara who said, 'Sister! Because of this irreparable insult to you, anger wells up in me. Rama is a mere human and short-lived. Before my prowess, he is nothing. I will kill not only him but also his brother. Calm down and wipe your tears.' Then Khara called his commander Dushana and ordered, 'O Dushana! Prepare my chariot immediately. Gather all weapons. I, skilled in warfare, will be in the front. Command all our troops to be battle-ready and march.' Thus Khara ordered his commander and became battle-ready.

**Key entities:** Khara, Surpanakha, Rama, Dushana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Khara, along with all his men, become battle-ready and advance against Rama?

**Answer:** Fourteen thousand fearsome rakshasa warriors, holding various weapons like iron clubs, broadswords, and tridents, followed Khara. As Khara's chariot horses sped along a smooth royal road, the chariot suddenly seemed to stumble. In the dark blue sky, a halo formed around the sun. On the tall flag atop the chariot, a large vulture circled and perched on it. Many other such inauspicious omens appeared to Khara. But ignoring them, Khara told his men, 'No matter how many great portents occur, I, a courageous one, do not heed them at all. I will surely kill the arrogant Rama and his brother with my fierce arrows. I have never known defeat in my previous battles. May it be so now as well!' Hearing Khara's words, all his followers rejoiced. Around Khara's chariot, twelve commanders followed, including the chief commanders Sthulaksha, Pramadhi, Trishira, and Mahakapala. Thus the rakshasa army, filled with battle fervor, rapidly approached the princes Rama and Lakshmana.

**Key entities:** Khara, Rama, Trishira, Lakshmana

### Chapter 38: Thirty-eighth Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 24-29
- Source PDF pages: 95, 96, 97
- Printed page numbers: 99, 100, 101
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Khara, Dushana, Trishira, Agastya, Dasharatha, Yama
- Places: Godavari, Dandaka Forest

**Summary:** Rama instructs Lakshmana to take Sita to a cave for safety as Khara approaches with his army. Rama fights the rakshasas, using the Gandharva astra to multiply arrows. After killing fourteen thousand rakshasas including Dushana and Trishira, only Khara remains. Rama and Khara engage in a fierce battle, exchanging harsh words. Rama uses the Vaishnava bow given by Agastya.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Rama saw Khara coming with his army, he told Lakshmana to take the responsibility of protecting his sister-in-law and take her to which place?

**Options:**
- 1. To the shade of a tree
- 2. Into the leaf hut
- 3. Into a mountain cave
- 4. To the Godavari region

**Correct answer:** Into a mountain cave

**Key entities:** Rama, Khara, Lakshmana

#### Q2

**Question:** When the rakshasas started the battle and raged with many weapons, Rama released an astra. By its effect, thousands of arrows spread in all directions. What is the name of that astra released by Rama?

**Options:**
- 1. Agneyastra
- 2. Varunastra
- 3. Aindrastra
- 4. Gandharvastra

**Correct answer:** Gandharvastra

**Key entities:** Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** When fourteen thousand soldiers and commanders were killed by the enemy-destroying Rama, who was the last one remaining?

**Answer:** Khara

**Key entities:** Rama, Khara

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the battle between Rama and Khara take place?

**Answer:** Seeing Dushana and Trishira fall on the battlefield, Khara was somewhat frightened by Rama's prowess. Seeing that Rama alone had slain the invincible fourteen thousand rakshasa army before his eyes, including Trishira and Dushana, all his pride was crushed. Regaining courage, Khara rushed at Rama. Khara drew his powerful bow and shot arrows at Rama. Mounted on his chariot, Khara displayed his archery skills in various ways. Then the descendant of Raghu covered the sky with his unerring arrows that showered sparks. The sky became filled with the sharp arrows shot by Rama and Khara. Seeing Rama standing firm with great prowess in battle even after slaying the vast rakshasa army, Khara thought, 'This descendant of Raghu is immensely powerful.' Like a locust that does not realize its own destruction and rushes into fire, Khara rushed at Rama. Then Rama took the Vaishnava bow given by Sage Agastya and rushed at Khara. Thus the battle between Rama and Khara continued.

**Key entities:** Rama, Khara, Dushana, Trishira, Agastya

#### Q5

**Question:** During the battle, how did Rama and Khara speak harshly to each other?

**Answer:** Seeing Khara, who had lost his chariot and held a mace, Rama said, 'O night-roamer! You, who had elephants, horses, chariots, and infantry, committed terrible deeds. All the worlds abhor your evil deeds. One who causes fear to all beings, who torments, who engages in sinful acts, even if he is the lord of the three worlds, cannot escape death. What then of a lowly one like you? Even the most compassionate will not refrain from killing those who are thorns to the world, like a snake that comes at them. What did you gain by killing the ascetics who lived righteously in this Dandaka forest, minding their own business? Sinners who perform evil deeds, even if they obtain wealth, soon perish. O rakshasa! It is to take the lives of those who plot evil against humanity and engage in terrible sinful acts that King Dasharatha sent me to this Dandaka forest.' Hearing this, Khara said, 'O son of Dasharatha! Having killed ordinary soldiers in battle, you boast about yourself like a great hero. Is what you did really a battle? Self-praise is a sign of your pettiness. Do you not see me standing before you in this battlefield, holding a mace, like a motionless mountain? I alone, like Yama who takes away your life, am enough to take your life.' Then Khara hurled the mace from his shoulder at Rama. Rama shattered the weapon with his arrow. Thus Khara and Rama spoke harshly and began to fight.

**Key entities:** Rama, Khara, Dandaka Forest, Dasharatha, Yama

### Chapter 39: Thirty-ninth Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 30-35
- Source PDF pages: 97, 98, 99, 100
- Printed page numbers: 101, 102, 103, 104
- Key entities: Rama, Khara, Dushana, Ravana, Maricha, Surpanakha, Sita, Trishira, Subahu, Lakshmana
- Places: Dandaka Forest, Lanka

**Summary:** Rama kills Khara, Dushana, and fourteen thousand rakshasas. Akampana informs Ravana of their deaths. Ravana seeks Maricha's help. Shurpanakha incites Ravana by describing Sita's beauty and her own disfigurement. Ravana decides to abduct Sita and visits Maricha's hermitage to seek his assistance.

#### Q1

**Question:** In how many ghatikas did Sri Rama slay Khara, Dushana, and the fourteen thousand rakshasas?

**Options:**
- 1. Five ghatikas
- 2. Seven ghatikas
- 3. Two ghatikas
- 4. Three ghatikas

**Correct answer:** Three ghatikas

**Key entities:** Rama, Khara, Dushana

#### Q2

**Question:** Who first informed Ravana of the death of Khara and all their people?

**Options:**
- 1. Akampana
- 2. Dushana
- 3. Trishira
- 4. Subahu

**Correct answer:** Akampana

**Key entities:** Ravana, Khara

#### Q3

**Question:** Enraged by Akampana's words, Ravana came to Dandaka forest and at Janasthana, whose help did he seek to kill Sri Rama?

**Answer:** Maricha

**Key entities:** Ravana, Dandaka Forest, Rama, Maricha

#### Q4

**Question:** Ravana was somewhat pacified by Maricha's advice. How did Shurpanakha again provoke him and send him against Rama?

**Answer:** Ravana went to Maricha to seek his cooperation for abducting Sita. Maricha said, 'O Ravana! War with Sri Rama is not proper for you. The one who sent you after telling you about Sita and Rama is not your well-wisher. Listen to me. Give up this idea and go back to Lanka and live happily.' Ravana agreed and returned to Lanka. In Lanka, Shurpanakha came fearfully to Ravana who was seated in court. She displayed her disfigured form caused by Lakshmana in Dandaka forest and spoke to her brother Ravana: 'O Ravana! Without anyone to oppose you, you are an autocrat, immersed in sensual pleasures and intoxicated. A situation even fearful to hear has arisen. O brother!
