Knowing that countless rakshasa warriors have met a horrible death in Janasthana, how can you be indifferent towards the enemies? Ravana! The truth is that among the beauties of devas, gandharvas, yakshas, kinnaras, and humans, there is none as beautiful as her. She is Rama's wife, Sita Devi. She is worthy of being your wife. Thinking thus, I was trying in that direction when Rama's brother Lakshmana disfigured me like this. For the peace of the souls of Khara, Dushana and other rakshasas, you must slay Rama and Lakshmana. Then you can enjoy the orphaned Sita as you wish.' Hearing Shurpanakha's words, Ravana discussed with his ministers in the court and decided his course of action.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Maricha, Surpanakha, Rama, Sita, Lanka, Lakshmana, Dandaka Forest, Khara, Dushana

#### Q5

**Question:** Having come to a firm decision regarding the abduction of Sita, what did Ravana do?

**Answer:** Ravana went from the court to his inner palace, carefully considered the feasibility of abducting Sita, compared his strength with Rama's, and finally decided on the abduction. Then he went to the stable and told the charioteer to prepare the chariot. As per the king's order, the charioteer prepared a golden chariot yoked with donkeys that had demonic forms. Ravana mounted it, came to the seashore, and traveled through the sky on a chariot that moved at his will. Traveling thus, Ravana saw a beautiful and peaceful hermitage. There he saw a rakshasa named Maricha, who wore a black deer skin, had matted hair, and observed dietary restrictions. Then Maricha offered hospitality to the arriving Ravana and worshipped him with various luxuries. Maricha personally arranged food for Ravana. Then Maricha asked, 'O king of rakshasas! Is everyone in Lanka well? Why have you come here alone and in haste?' Then Ravana explained to him the necessity of abducting Sita.

**Key entities:** Sita, Ravana, Rama, Maricha, Lanka

### Chapter 40: Fortieth Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 36-41
- Source PDF pages: 100, 101, 102
- Printed page numbers: 104, 105, 106
- Key entities: Ravana, Maricha, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** Ravana seeks Maricha's help to abduct Sita. He instructs Maricha to take the form of a golden deer to lure Rama away. Maricha warns Ravana about Rama's prowess and the dangers of the plan, but Ravana threatens him into compliance.

#### Q1

**Question:** Ravana asked Maricha to cooperate in the abduction of Sita. What form did he tell him to assume and wander near Sita?

**Options:**
- 1. Elephant
- 2. Horse
- 3. Deer (stag)
- 4. Dog

**Correct answer:** Deer (stag)

**Key entities:** Ravana, Maricha, Sita

#### Q2

**Question:** Advising Ravana, what did Maricha specifically say about Rama?

**Options:**
- 1. Fickle
- 2. Lowly
- 3. Embodiment of dharma
- 4. Coward

**Correct answer:** Embodiment of dharma

**Key entities:** Ravana, Maricha, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** Maricha told Ravana about his past experience where Rama showed unparalleled valor. Where did that happen?

**Answer:** Siddhashrama

**Key entities:** Maricha, Ravana, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Ravana bring Maricha under his control to make him obey his words?

**Answer:** Despite Maricha's warnings about Rama's strength, Ravana refused to listen. He said, 'O Maricha! I need your help for the task I have planned. I did not ask you whether it is good or bad. Listen to what you must do. O Maricha! Transform into a strange golden deer with white spots like silver and wander near Rama's hermitage. Freely moving thus, tempt Sita. Then Vaidehi, seeing the magical deer, will ask Rama to bring it to her immediately. Rama will come to catch you as per her wish. You lead him far away. Then, imitating Rama's voice, cry out loudly, 'Ha! Sita! Ha! Lakshmana!' Hearing those words, Sita will grieve and urge Lakshmana to go. As soon as Lakshmana leaves, I will easily take Vaidehi away. O Maricha! This is all you need to do for me. After that, you may go as you wish. Thus, without fighting Rama, I will deceive him and go to Lanka with Sita. If you do not do as I say, I will kill you right now. Even if you don't like it, I will make you do this work. If you take the form of an animal, you might survive by fate. But if you oppose me, your life will end now. Consider which of the two you choose.' Thus Ravana threatened Maricha and brought him to his side.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Maricha, Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Lanka

#### Q5

**Question:** In how many ways did Maricha tell Ravana that the task he intended to do was not good?

**Answer:** Maricha, criticizing Ravana's commanding manner with kingly pride, said: 'O night-ranger! If you abduct Sita like this, you will be destroyed along with your main force. Who is the wicked one who gave you this disastrous advice? O king! Who is that sinner who cannot bear your happiness? Who are your weak Rakshasa enemies who, unable to confront you directly, desire your death at the hands of the more powerful Rama? O Ravana! Who is waiting for harm to befall you by planting this evil thought in your head? Even if someone intends to harm you due to your own fault, you alone will suffer the consequences. O Ravana! Soon after Rama kills me, he will kill you too. Dying at Rama's hands, I will give up my life seeing that great soul. You, having abducted Sita, will die along with your relatives, friends, and retinue. If the abduction happens according to your plan, neither you nor I nor the Rakshasas will survive. Lanka will not exist. O Ravana! I speak for your good, yet you do not listen. One whose time has come does not heed a friend's words. You are behaving likewise.' Thus Maricha advised Ravana in many ways.

**Key entities:** Maricha, Ravana, Sita, Rama, Lanka

### Chapter 41: Forty-first Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 42-47
- Source PDF pages: 102, 103, 104, 105
- Printed page numbers: 106, 107, 108, 109
- Key entities: Maricha, Ravana, Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Kabandha, Viradha
- Places: Dandaka Forest

**Summary:** Maricha, under Ravana's orders, goes to Rama's hermitage in Dandaka forest. He takes the form of a golden deer to lure Rama away. Lakshmana suspects it is Maricha's illusion. Rama pursues the deer and shoots it; Maricha cries out in Rama's voice. Sita hears the cry and forces Lakshmana to go to Rama's aid. After Lakshmana leaves, Ravana approaches Sita disguised as a sage. He reveals his identity and tries to seduce her, but Sita rejects him.

#### Q1

**Question:** By which trees did Maricha, who came on Ravana's chariot, identify Rama's hermitage in Dandaka forest?

**Options:**
- 1. Sandalwood trees
- 2. Maddi trees
- 3. Jammi trees
- 4. Banana trees

**Correct answer:** Banana trees

**Key entities:** Maricha, Ravana, Rama, Dandaka Forest

#### Q2

**Question:** Seeing the illusory deer wandering near their hermitage, Lakshmana told his brother that this is not an ordinary deer. Which demon's illusion is this?

**Options:**
- 1. Kabandha
- 2. Viradha
- 3. Maricha
- 4. Akampana

**Correct answer:** Maricha

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Maricha

#### Q3

**Question:** Armed with bow and arrows, Rama followed the illusory deer far away. There, struck by Rama's arrow, Maricha in deer form cried out in what manner?

**Answer:** Ha! Sita! Ha! Lakshmana!

**Key entities:** Rama, Maricha, Sita, Lakshmana

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Ravana get the opportunity to approach Sita?

**Answer:** The cry of Maricha in deer form, struck by Rama's arrow, resembled Rama's voice. Hearing it, Sita concluded that Rama was in danger and told Lakshmana, 'That cry is your brother's. Since hearing it, my mind is not at peace. My life is leaving me. Lakshmana, run immediately to save him.' Despite Sita's words, Lakshmana stayed as per his brother's order. Then Janaki angrily said, 'O Saumitri! You pretend to love your brother, but you don't. You are his enemy. Even in such danger, you don't go to him. Actually, you desire me and are trying to harm Rama. Truly, you have no love for your brother.' Sita spoke unbearable words, thinking her husband was in danger. Lakshmana, though hurt, said, 'Mother! No one—gods, demons, nagas, gandharvas, or humans—can defeat Rama. Do not doubt.' He tried to console her, but due to her stubbornness and harsh words, he bowed to her, steeled his heart, and went to Rama. As soon as Lakshmana left, Ravana, who was waiting for the opportunity, appeared before Sita in the guise of a sage.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sita, Maricha, Rama, Lakshmana

#### Q5

**Question:** When Ravana, disguised as a sage, went to Sita in the leaf hut, what happened there?

**Answer:** Ravana entered the hermitage in the guise of a sage when Rama and Lakshmana were absent. Reciting Vedic mantras appropriately, he saw Vaidehi, Rama's wife. Overcome with desire, he said, 'O woman, who are you? I have never seen such a beauty as you.' Praising her in many ways, he said, 'O young lady, why are you in this place where shape-shifting demons roam? O auspicious one, what is your name? Whose are you? Why are you staying in Dandaka forest?' Though Ravana spoke, Sita, anxious that her husband had not yet returned, listened absent-mindedly. Because of his ascetic guise, she honored him with hospitality. Ravana, however, was planning to abduct her. Then, at Ravana's request, Sita told her entire story. Afterwards, she asked, 'O best of Brahmins, who are you? What is the reason for your wandering in Dandaka forest?' Ravana replied harshly, 'O Sita! I am Ravana, the king of rakshasas. I have brought many beautiful women. If you accept me as your husband, you will be my chief queen. All my wives will serve you. Thousands of maids will serve you.' Sita scorned him. Then Ravana explained about the rakshasa race and his own prowess.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Dandaka Forest

### Chapter 42: Forty-second Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 48-53
- Source PDF pages: 105, 106, 107
- Printed page numbers: 109, 110, 111
- Key entities: Ravana, Sita, Jatayu, Kubera, Sampati, Hanuman, Rama, Lakshmana
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** Ravana abducts Sita after defeating Jatayu. He boasts of his prowess, including having conquered Kubera's Pushpaka Vimana. Sita rebukes him harshly as he carries her through the sky.

#### Q1

**Question:** Ravana, while telling Sita about his heroic exploits, said that he is the brother of Kubera, but after fighting with that Kubera, what did he conquer and take possession of?

**Options:**
- 1. Divine chariot
- 2. Kubera's wife
- 3. Pushpaka Vimana
- 4. Vajra Simhasana

**Correct answer:** Pushpaka Vimana

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sita, Kubera

#### Q2

**Question:** When Ravana was forcibly abducting Sita, who obstructed him?

**Options:**
- 1. Forest deities
- 2. Jatayu
- 3. Sampati
- 4. Anjaneya

**Correct answer:** Jatayu

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sita, Jatayu

#### Q3

**Question:** During the battle between Ravana and Jatayu, Jatayu's blow destroyed Ravana's chariot, charioteer, and the donkeys with distorted faces yoked to the chariot. For what reason did Ravana notice that Jatayu was somewhat fatigued?

**Answer:** Six

**Key entities:** Ravana, Jatayu

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Ravana forcibly take Sita away?

**Answer:** Seeing Jatayu fallen near the hermitage, Ravana approached Sita. She embraced the dying Jatayu and wept. When Ravana came towards her, Sita cried out 'Rama! Lakshmana!' and, terrified, hugged a tree tightly, weeping 'Rama! Protect me! Protect me!' Then Ravana grabbed the weeping Sita by her hair and dragged her. Seeing the insult to Sita at Ravana's hands, nature was plunged into darkness of ignorance. The rakshasa king took Janaki, who was crying 'Rama! Lakshmana! Protect me!' and flew into the sky. The ornaments and anklets worn by the auspicious Sita, struck by the wind, fell one by one here and there. All the flowers from her braid scattered on the ground. Thus Sita, with unbearable grief, wept loudly in a pitiful voice, crying 'Rama! Lakshmana!' and repeatedly looked down at the ground. Seeing Sita thus, the forest deities trembled. Her hair was disheveled. The tilak on her forehead was smeared. Ravana abducted that chaste wife because his death was near.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sita, Jatayu, Rama, Lakshmana

#### Q5

**Question:** While Ravana was abducting her towards the city of Lanka, how did Sita speak harshly?

**Answer:** Sita, angry at Ravana who was carrying her through the sky, wept bitterly and lamented helplessly, saying: 'O vile Ravana! You came when Rama and Lakshmana were absent and are fleeing with me like a thief. Are you not ashamed to do such a deed? O wicked one! Desiring to abduct me, fearing my husband, you sent him away from me in the form of a magical deer and are now abducting me. What hero are you? You killed Jatayu, who was a friend of my father-in-law. Is killing an old bird heroism? O lowest of rakshasas! You did not come by defeating Raghuvira in battle and taking me. From this, your prowess is evident. O lowly one! You abducted the wife of a man when he was absent. Are you not ashamed to do such a despicable act? Though devoid of valor, you boast of being a great hero. By thus harming the great Rama, you will surely die like one who has drunk kalkuta poison. You are abducting the wife of Rama, who alone, without his brother, killed fourteen thousand demons. Will Rama spare the one who abducted his wife? Your death is near.' Thus Janaki, overcome with fear and grief, spoke many harsh words. But Ravana, disregarding her, continued on his way.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Lanka, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Jatayu

### Chapter 43: Forty-third Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 54-58
- Source PDF pages: 107, 108, 109, 110
- Printed page numbers: 111, 112, 113, 114
- Key entities: Rama, Maricha, Sita, Lakshmana, Ravana, Vibhishana
- Places: Lanka, Ashoka Grove

**Summary:** Rama returns to the hermitage after killing Maricha, only to find Sita missing. He laments and questions Lakshmana about leaving her alone. They search the area but find no trace of her.

#### Q1

**Question:** Sita, abducted by Ravana, tore her garment, tied her ornaments in a bundle, and left it on a mountain peak where prominent monkeys saw her. How many prominent monkeys were there?

**Options:**
- 1. Eight
- 2. Seven
- 3. Six
- 4. Five

**Correct answer:** Five

**Key entities:** Sita, Ravana

#### Q2

**Question:** When Ravana brought Sita through the sky to Lanka, where did he first place her?

**Options:**
- 1. In the Ashoka grove
- 2. In the Pushpaka chariot
- 3. In his inner palace
- 4. In Vibhishana's house

**Correct answer:** In his inner palace

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sita, Lanka

#### Q3

**Question:** Ravana showed his wealth and splendor, but Sita refused to accept him as her husband. So he placed her in the Ashoka grove, set a deadline, and threatened to kill her after it expired. How many months was the deadline?

**Answer:** Twelve months

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sita, Ashoka Grove

#### Q4

**Question:** What happened after Sri Rama killed Maricha?

**Answer:** Maricha, in the form of a deer, led Rama far away. Rama killed the shape-shifting Maricha and started back to the hermitage. Then a jackal behind him howled hideously. Hearing it, Rama's body trembled, suspecting some calamity. Maricha had imitated Rama's voice crying 'Ha Sita! Ha Lakshmana!' Thinking of the inauspicious jackal's cry, Rama hurried back. Meanwhile, Lakshmana, with a dejected face, met him. Rama grabbed Lakshmana's left hand and lamented, 'Lakshmana! How could you leave Sita alone in this forest full of demons? You made a great mistake. The demons here might have killed or eaten her. Will we ever see Sita alive? The demon in deer form lured me far away; finally I killed him.' Saying this, Rama walked quickly with Lakshmana.

**Key entities:** Rama, Maricha, Sita, Lakshmana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Rama and Lakshmana reach the hermitage?

**Answer:** Rama, agitated, said to Lakshmana, 'Lakshmana! Where did you leave Sita? I cannot live without her. Is she still alive? Due to your carelessness, has that noble woman fallen into the hands of demons? The wicked demon imitated my voice crying 'Alas Lakshmana!' and you might have been frightened. Because of that fear, Vaidehi might also have been scared and sent you to me.' Thus speaking in various ways, Rama lamented about Sita and walked quickly to the hermitage. Having walked a long distance, Rama was very tired. Due to hunger and thirst, his face was withered and pale. In that state, he scolded Lakshmana with anguish, sighing deeply, and reached the hermitage. Not finding Sita anywhere, they searched inside the leaf hut and the surrounding areas. The result was nothing. Rama, stunned, began to suffer greatly.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Sita

### Chapter 44: Forty-Fourth Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 59-64
- Source PDF pages: 110, 111, 112
- Printed page numbers: 114, 115, 116
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Janaka, Vayu
- Places: Ayodhya, Godavari

**Summary:** Rama and Lakshmana return to the hermitage to find Sita missing. Rama is grief-stricken and searches desperately, recalling her virtues. Lakshmana consoles him and they begin the search, following clues such as scattered flowers, footprints, and signs of a struggle.

#### Q1

**Question:** When asked by his brother, 'Why did you leave Sita alone in the hermitage?', Lakshmana replied, 'Brother! I had to come because my sister-in-law scolded me with words that my ears cannot hear and my mouth cannot utter.' Then Rama said, 'Whatever it is, brother! I see some bad omens. Therefore something terrible must have happened.' What is one of those bad omens?

**Options:**
- 1. My right shoulder twitched
- 2. My right eye twitched
- 2. My left leg twitched
- 4. My left eye twitched

**Correct answer:** My left eye twitched

**Key entities:** Sita, Lakshmana, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** When Rama and Lakshmana came to the hermitage, they could not find any trace of Sita. They looked here and there. Rama's eyes turned red with the weight of grief. Searching for Sita, asking every tree, bush, bank, mountain, valley, and river, 'Where is my Sita? Where is my Sita?', how did Rama appear at that time?

**Options:**
- 1. He was like a madman
- 2. He was like a great hero
- 3. He was like a great king
- 4. He was like a forest-dweller

**Correct answer:** He was like a madman

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Sita

#### Q3

**Question:** Unable to find solace despite Lakshmana's consolations over the pain of Sita's disappearance, Rama lamented to Lakshmana, 'I came to the forests with Sita. If I return to Ayodhya without Sita, and the people there ask where Sita is, what shall I reply?' Specifically, who did he say would confront him and ask about Sita, leaving him at a loss for words?

**Answer:** King Janaka

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Sita, Rama, Ayodhya, Janaka

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Rama suffer as he recalled Sita in various ways?

**Answer:** Rama, overwhelmed with grief and separation from Sita, lamented: 'Lakshmana! There is no one more unfortunate than me on this earth. An endless series of sorrows haunts me, tearing my heart and mind. Brother! The noble Sita is timid. Someone must have forcibly abducted her through the sky. How frightened my Janaki must have been! My virtuous wife, who would not even bear the touch of another man, might have been killed by demons who drank her blood. At that time, she must have looked for my help without blinking. Lakshmana! Your sister-in-law used to sit with me on this stone slab and converse charmingly about many things. She loved this Godavari river, but she never went to the river without me. O Sun god! You are the witness to all actions. You know everything in the world. O Wind god! Nothing happens without your knowledge. Please tell me where my Sita is.' Thus Rama lamented in despair, and though Lakshmana said, 'Brother! Give up grief. Do not lose hope. Be courageous. Let us search with enthusiasm,' Rama lost his courage and sank into endless sorrow.

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Godavari, Vayu

#### Q5

**Question:** What did Rama and Lakshmana discuss as they began the search for Sita?

**Answer:** Rama, grieving and sorrowing for Sita, said, 'Lakshmana! Let us search along this riverbank and in the region of Prashravana Hill. Sita may be found. The strong animals are looking at me as if they want to tell me something.' He asked the animals, 'Where is my Sita?' Then the animals immediately looked towards the southern sky and ran in that direction. Seeing this, Lakshmana said, 'They are showing us the direction Sita went. Brother! Let us travel in the south-westerly direction. Our sister-in-law may be found in that direction, which is the abode of demons.' As the two brothers walked that way, they saw scattered flowers along the path. Rama recognized them as those worn by Sita. Then, after traveling some distance, they saw large footprints of a demon and footprints of Sita. Going further, they saw bloodstains, a broken bow, a chariot, a charioteer, and deformed donkeys. Seeing this, they concluded that two demons must have seen Sita, quarreled over eating her, and fought. Rama said, 'Lakshmana! None of the gods tried to protect my Sita. If they do not return my Sita to me now, they will experience my wrath,' and angrily took up his bow.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Sita

### Chapter 45: Forty-fifth Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 65-70
- Source PDF pages: 112, 113, 114, 115
- Printed page numbers: 116, 117, 118, 119
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Jatayu, Ravana, Kabandha, Sugriva
- Places: Dandaka Forest

**Summary:** Rama and Lakshmana search for Sita, encounter dying Jatayu who tells them Ravana abducted her southward, then meet the demon Kabandha who attacks them; they cut off his arms, and Kabandha reveals his story and advises them to seek Sugriva's help.

#### Q1

**Question:** Lakshmana, consoling Rama who was mentally emaciated due to separation from Sita, said: 'Brother! This entire area is crushed by the pressure of chariot wheel rims. Based on the war signs here, how many people might have fought here?' What did Lakshmana tell Rama?

**Options:**
- 1. Two
- 2. One alone
- 2. A great army
- 4. Three

**Correct answer:** One alone

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Rama, Sita

#### Q2

**Question:** Lakshmana pacified Rama who was grieving and lamenting for Sita, informed him of his duty, and as they walked forward a little, they saw Jatayu in his final moments. Jatayu told Rama that Ravana had abducted Sita and had thrown him down like this when he tried to stop him, and then the king of birds gave up his life. What did Rama and Lakshmana do with Jatayu's body?

**Options:**
- 1. Buried it in the ground
- 2. Left it there and went away
- 3. Performed cremation rites
- 4. Hung it from a tree

**Correct answer:** Performed cremation rites

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Rama, Sita, Jatayu, Ravana

#### Q3

**Question:** How and in which direction did Jatayu tell Rama that Ravana took Janaki?

**Answer:** Through the sky, towards the south.

**Key entities:** Jatayu, Rama, Ravana, Sita

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the demon Kabandha appear to Rama and Lakshmana as they went in search of Sita?

**Answer:** Rama and Lakshmana, both armed with bows and arrows, traveled southwest searching for Sita. They crossed the Dandaka forest, entered the Krauncha forest, and after traveling three yojanas from there, they reached a place between Matanga hermitage and Krauncha forest, where they saw a mountain cave. From there they walked forward and entered a dense forest. Then they heard a great noise that made the forest tremble. Walking in the direction of the sound, they saw a demon of grotesque form. His two arms extended far away, and with those arms he was dragging even cruel animals. That Kabandha stood blocking their path, caught both of them, and pulled them close. Then Rama said, 'Brother! No matter how much we search, Sita is not found. Now our very lives are in danger. For anyone, the influence of time cannot be overcome. Lakshmana! Even the valiant, the strong, and those skilled in archery become subject to time and suffer hardships. It is not difficult for God to control even the greatest.' Thus speaking to Lakshmana, Rama steadied his mind.

**Key entities:** Kabandha, Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Dandaka Forest

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Rama and Lakshmana finish off Kabandha?

**Answer:** Seeing the princes caught in his arms, Kabandha said, 'O princes! Seeing that I am hungry, God himself has sent you as my food. There is no use thinking further.' Hearing the demon speaking thus, Lakshmana said, 'Brother! There is no need for weapons to kill this demon. Cut off that arm with the sword in your hand. I will cut off this arm with my sword.' Then Lakshmana cut off the arm that held him. When both his arms were cut off, Kabandha roared, making the earth and sky tremble. That demon, wallowing in a pool of blood, sorrowfully asked, 'Sirs! Who are you?' Then Lakshmana replied, 'We are of the Ikshvaku dynasty. This one, endowed with divine power, is Sri Rama. I am his younger brother, Lakshmana. Due to some reason, a demon has abducted Sri Rama's wife. Searching for her, we have come here. Now, who are you?' When Saumitri asked, Kabandha said, 'O best of men! My fortune has ripened, and I have obtained your vision. By my good luck, you have cut off my arms. Because I behaved disrespectfully, I was cursed and obtained this grotesque form.' Then Kabandha narrated his entire story to Rama and Lakshmana.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Kabandha

### Chapter 46: Forty-Sixth Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 71-75
- Source PDF pages: 115, 116, 117, 118
- Printed page numbers: 119, 120, 121, 122
- Key entities: Kabandha, Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Shabari, Atri, Vali, Hanuman, Angada, Sita
- Places: Rishyamuka

**Summary:** Kabandha tells his story to Rama and Lakshmana, revealing the sage who cursed him and advising them to seek Sugriva's help. They then travel towards Rishyamuka mountain, meeting the ascetic Shabari at Matanga's hermitage, who is blessed by Rama and attains liberation. Finally, they proceed to the Pampa lake region.

#### Q1

**Question:** While telling his story to Rama and Lakshmana, Kabandha revealed which great sage cursed him to get this deformed form?

**Options:**
- 1. Sharabhaṅga
- 2. Matanga Maharshi
- 3. Sthūlaśiras
- 4. Atri Maharshi

**Correct answer:** Sthūlaśiras

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Kabandha

#### Q2

**Question:** After obtaining a divine body, whom did Kabandha advise Rama and Lakshmana to approach for their mission to succeed?

**Options:**
- 1. Vali
- 2. Hanuman
- 3. Angada
- 4. Sugriva

**Correct answer:** Sugriva

**Key entities:** Kabandha, Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva

#### Q3

**Question:** As instructed by Kabandha, Rama and Lakshmana traveled towards Rishyamuka mountain and on the way saw an old female ascetic at Matanga Maharshi's hermitage. What was her name?

**Answer:** Shabari

**Key entities:** Kabandha, Rama, Lakshmana, Rishyamuka, Shabari

#### Q4

**Question:** While coming to meet Sugriva, whom did Rama and Lakshmana bless in Matanga's hermitage on the way, and how?

**Answer:** Following the path told by Kabandha, Rama and Lakshmana both started walking westwards through that forest. After traveling some distance, they spent the night on a mountain peak there, and the next morning reached the western shore of Lake Pampa. Then they reached the hermitage, which was lush with trees, and met Shabari there. That Shabari, who had attained yogic perfection, seeing Rama and Lakshmana, folded her hands and prostrated at their feet. Then Shabari worshipped both brothers with offerings of arghya, water for washing feet, etc., and presented fruits and flowers. Then Rama said, 'O ascetic rich in penance! Is there any hindrance to your penance? Are you fulfilled in serving your guru?' To Rama's words, Shabari replied, 'O Lord Ramachandra! By seeing you with my own eyes, my penance is fulfilled. All the sages I served, while going to heaven, said that Shri Rama along with Lakshmana will come to this holy hermitage. Honor him. By his sight you will attain the highest worlds. O holy man! If you permit, I will give up this body. My gurus are holy men; I will go to the worlds they went to. Please permit me.' According to Shabari's wish, Rama said, 'O Shabari! I am pleased with your worship. You may go as you wish.' Then, with Rama's permission, Shabari, in a state of yogic meditation, left her body and went to the eternal worlds. Then Rama and Lakshmana performed the fire rites for the devout Shabari's earthly body and continued their journey from there.

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Rama, Lakshmana, Kabandha, Shabari

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Rama and Lakshmana's journey from Shabari's hermitage to the Rishyamuka mountain region proceed?

**Answer:** Near Shabari's hermitage, both Rama and Lakshmana bathed in the Saptasagara Tirtha and offered libations to the ancestors. Then Rama said, 'Brother! With this, all our inauspiciousness has perished. My mind has found some relief. Now I feel that only good things will happen to us. Lakshmana! Let us now go along the shore of Lake Pampa. Rishyamuka mountain is nearby. There Sugriva, afraid of his brother Vali, is living. That foremost of vanaras can help us in the search for Sita.' As Rama was speaking, Lakshmana said, 'Brother! My mind is also eager for that. So we must go quickly.' Thus both brothers started walking along the shore of Lake Pampa. Then Rama said, 'Brother! As Kabandha told us, Rishyamuka mountain is in this region of Lake Pampa. Lakshmana! In this state, without Sita by my side, how can I live?' Remembering Sita and grieving, Rama was consoled by Lakshmana, who walked with his brother along the shore of Lake Pampa.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Shabari, Rishyamuka, Sugriva, Vali, Sita, Kabandha

### Chapter 47: Forty-seventh Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 1-6
- Source PDF pages: 118, 119, 120
- Printed page numbers: 122, 123, 124
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Sugriva, Hanuman, Vali, Ravana
- Places: Rishyamuka

**Summary:** Rama and Lakshmana search for Sita on Rishyamuka mountain. Sugriva sends Hanuman to ascertain their intentions. Hanuman meets them and learns their story, then brings Sugriva. Rama and Sugriva form a friendship with fire as witness. Sugriva shows Rama the bundle of jewels dropped by Sita, confirming her identity.

#### Q1

**Question:** Rama, along with Lakshmana, while searching for Sita, traversing all forests, streams, and mountain caves, walks on Rishyamuka mountain. Among the monkeys who saw those bow-bearing Rama and Lakshmana, who was the first to be afraid?

**Options:**
- 1. Hanuman
- 2. Mainda
- 3. Dvivida
- 4. Sugriva

**Correct answer:** Sugriva

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Rishyamuka, Sugriva

#### Q2

**Question:** Sugriva sent Hanuman to find out who Rama and Lakshmana were and their true intentions, and in what form did he ask him to go?

**Options:**
- 1. Human form
- 2. Monkey form
- 3. Rakshasa form
- 4. As a Gandharva

**Correct answer:** Human form

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Hanuman, Rama, Lakshmana

#### Q3

**Question:** Hanuman met Rama and Lakshmana and spoke to them sweetly, telling them about Sugriva's story: 'Our lord Sugriva was driven from his kingdom by his elder brother Vali. Vali also took Sugriva's wife under his control.' What is the name of that wife of Sugriva?

**Answer:** Ruma

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Vali

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the friendship between Rama and Sugriva take place?

**Answer:** When Hanuman brought Rama and Lakshmana to Rishyamuka mountain, Sugriva had gone to nearby Malaya mountain. Then Hanuman went to Sugriva, brought the monkey king, and on the way told him all he knew about Rama and Lakshmana. He brought him to Rishyamuka mountain and presented him to Rama and Lakshmana. Then Maruti (Hanuman) said to Sugriva: 'Lord, these Rama and Lakshmana are princes of the Ikshvaku dynasty. They are renowned for righteous conduct. While living in exile to fulfill their father's command, Ravana abducted Rama's wife. Therefore, he has come here seeking your help.' Hearing Hanuman's words, Sugriva rejoiced, and with the sight of Rama, all his fear vanished. He said, 'Lord, it is indeed my fortune that a great soul like you seeks the friendship of a monkey like me. Here I extend my hand in friendship.' Then Rama took Sugriva's hand and embraced him, honoring that pure friendship. Then Hanuman brought strong sami branches, kindled a fire, and worshipped it with flowers. Rama and Sugriva, holding each other's hands, circumambulated the fire and became friends with fire as witness. Hanuman arranged suitable seats for Rama and Lakshmana and made them sit.

**Key entities:** Rama, Sugriva, Hanuman, Lakshmana, Rishyamuka, Ravana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Sugriva and others show the bundle of Sita's jewels to Rama and Lakshmana?

**Answer:** Sugriva consoled Rama, saying, 'O mighty-armed one! You will soon be free from the grief of separation from your wife. O Rama! One day I saw a cruel rakshasa carrying a woman. In my opinion, she might be Sita. Because with a choked voice, she was crying loudly, 'Rama! Rama! Lakshmana!' and seeing me, she dropped a bundle tied in her garment. At that time, I was on the mountain with my four ministers. Later, I took that bundle of jewels and kept it safely.' Then Sugriva went into a mountain cave, brought the hidden bundle of jewels, and placed it before Rama. When Rama tried to open the sacred bundle, his eyes filled with tears, and he appeared dim and unclear like the moon covered by frost. Rama lamented, 'Alas! My dear!' and losing courage, fell to the ground. After some time, he regained composure, pressed the ornaments to his heart, and sighed like a snake hissing in an anthill. Then Rama looked at Saumitri (Lakshmana) and wept for a long time. Then Rama asked Lakshmana to look at the ornaments. With a sorrowful face, Lakshmana looked at the ornaments and said, 'Brother! I do not recognize these armlets and earrings, but because I daily bow to our elder sister-in-law's feet, I recognize these anklets as hers.' Thus, seeing the jewels shown by Sugriva, Rama and Lakshmana confirmed that they were Sita's.

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana

### Chapter 48: Forty-Eighth Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 7-12
- Source PDF pages: 120, 121, 122, 123
- Printed page numbers: 124, 125, 126, 127
- Key entities: Sugriva, Rama, Vali, Hanuman, Angada, Tara, Jambavan, Nila, Nala, Indra
- Places: Rishyamuka, Kishkindha

**Summary:** Sugriva narrates his story to Rama, describing Vali's persecution and his own survival with the help of Hanuman and others. He explains Vali's valor, the curse of sage Matanga, and the first battle between Vali and Sugriva where Rama hesitated to shoot due to their resemblance.

#### Q1

**Question:** Sugriva, while telling his story to Sri Rama, said that he has survived till now the torments inflicted by his brother Vali due to whose support?

**Options:**
- 1. Hanuman and others
- 2. Angada and others
- 3. Tara
- 4. Jambavan and others

**Correct answer:** Hanuman and others

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Rama, Vali, Hanuman

#### Q2

**Question:** Sugriva, while telling his story to Sri Rama, said that the father of Vali and Sugriva is who?

**Options:**
- 1. Kesari
- 2. Nila
- 3. Riksharajas
- 4. Nala

**Correct answer:** Riksharajas

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Rama, Vali

#### Q3

**Question:** Sugriva tells Sri Rama: 'Rama! A former enemy of my brother Vali, a rakshasa, challenged us to a fight at midnight; we both went. Seeing us, that rakshasa ran far and entered a mountain cave.' Who was that rakshasa who entered the cave?

**Answer:** Mayavi

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Rama, Vali

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Sugriva describe his brother's valor to Sri Rama?

**Answer:** O Raghuvira! My brother Vali is greatly valorous. Once, a rakshasa named Dundubhi, assuming the form of a buffalo, came to fight Vali. Vali, born from a part of Indra, wore the garland given by Indra, which transfers the opponent's strength to the wearer. Vali fought and killed Dundubhi. He threw the corpse; blood drops from Dundubhi's mouth fell on sage Matanga's hermitage. Seeing the blood stains, sage Matanga learned the matter and cursed: 'Vali, who defiled this hermitage with blood, shall not live in Rishyamuka forest; if he does, death is certain. He and his followers must leave this area within a day, or they will turn to stone for thousands of years.' Since then, Vali and his followers stopped coming to this mountain area. O Rama! That day my brother threw Dundubhi's elephant-like carcass; it lies here. Observe.' Thus Sugriva described his brother Vali's valor to Rama.

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Rama, Vali, Indra, Rishyamuka

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the battle between Vali and Sugriva take place?

**Answer:** Having learned of Vali's valor from Sugriva, to instill confidence in Sugriva, Rama strung his bow and shot a sharp arrow, felling seven madhvi trees that were in a row. Seeing this, Sugriva marveled at Rama's prowess and bowed at his feet, saying, 'Lord! No one can stand against you in battle. Therefore, kill Vali now.' Then Rama said, 'Sugriva! Go to Kishkindha and challenge Vali, who torments you, to battle.' Following Rama's words, Sugriva stood outside Kishkindha city, roared terribly, and challenged Vali to the battlefield. Rama stood hidden behind dense bushes in the forest. The mighty Vali, hearing his brother Sugriva's roar, came out of the city in anger and haste. Then the two struck each other with thunderbolt-like palm blows and diamond-like fist punches. Then Rama, the bow-bearer, seeing the two heroes who resembled each other like the Ashvini deities, could not distinguish Sugriva from Vali and did not release the fatal arrow. Sugriva, severely beaten by Vali, and not seeing his protector Raghava, fled towards Rishyamuka mountain. Thus the battle between Vali and Sugriva took place.

**Key entities:** Vali, Sugriva, Rama, Kishkindha, Rishyamuka

### Chapter 49: Forty-ninth Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 13-18
- Source PDF pages: 123, 124, 125
- Printed page numbers: 127, 128, 129
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Vali, Tara, Nila, Angada
- Places: Kishkindha, Ganga

**Summary:** Rama and Lakshmana help Sugriva in his battle against Vali. Lakshmana adorns Sugriva with a garland to distinguish him from Vali. During the second challenge, Tara tries to stop Vali from fighting. Rama shoots Vali from behind a tree. Vali falls and rebukes Rama for his unfair attack. Rama justifies his action by citing dharma and Vali's sins.

#### Q1

**Question:** Since Vali and Sugriva looked alike, on Rama's suggestion, what did Lakshmana adorn Sugriva with to identify him?

**Options:**
- 1. Helmet
- 2. Tying a cloth around the waist
- 3. Shoulder ornaments
- 4. A garland around the neck

**Correct answer:** A garland around the neck

**Key entities:** Vali, Sugriva, Rama, Lakshmana

#### Q2

**Question:** When Sugriva went to Kishkindha for the second time, roared, and challenged Vali to battle, who tried to stop Vali from going to war?

**Options:**
- 1. Ruma
- 2. Tara
- 3. Nila
- 4. Angada

**Correct answer:** Tara

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Kishkindha, Vali, Tara

#### Q3

**Question:** While Vali and Sugriva were fighting, from where did Rama shoot Vali with an arrow?

**Answer:** From behind a tree

**Key entities:** Vali, Sugriva, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the fallen Vali rebuke Rama on the battlefield?

**Answer:** Vali and Sugriva fought fiercely. Gradually Sugriva's strength waned. Noticing this, Rama released an arrow like a venomous serpent, which struck Vali's chest. Vali fell to the ground, his body drenched in blood. He lay unconscious, then opened his eyes. Rama and Lakshmana approached him with compassion. Vali, seeing the mighty Rama and Lakshmana, humbly said: 'O Lord! You are the son of a great king, learned in all scriptures, born in a noble lineage, truthful and valorous. Yet, while I was fighting with someone else, why did you strike my chest? I came to battle despite Tara's warning because I believed you were of noble birth. I have never seen you before, nor have I done you any harm. I trusted that a righteous one like you would not strike me while I was engaged with another. But your mind seems to have strayed. I have never wronged you or your country. Why do you seek to kill an innocent like me? I am a forest-dwelling monkey who eats fruits and roots. I have never fought against you. My bones, skin, and flesh are of no use to you. I never imagined you would show your might against the innocent like me. If you think this deed of yours is proper, give me an answer.' Thus Vali, wounded and thirsty, with parched mouth, kept looking at Rama.

**Key entities:** Vali, Rama, Sugriva, Lakshmana, Tara

#### Q5

**Question:** What answer did Rama give to Vali's rebuke?

**Answer:** After Vali, struck by Rama's arrow, rebuked the descendant of Raghu, he lay there like a sun without luster. Then Rama said: 'O Vali, not knowing dharma, artha, kama, and worldly customs, you ignorantly blame me. This land with mountains, forests, and groves is part of Jambu Dvipa and is under the rule of the Ikshvaku kings. We, the princes of that lineage, have full authority to punish or reward the animals, birds, and humans here. We punish those who deviate from the path of dharma. You are completely selfish, addicted to pleasures, and have abandoned the code of kings, committing adharma. An elder brother, father, and teacher are all equal to a father. You have cast that dharma into the Ganges. Your younger brother's wife Ruma is like a daughter-in-law to you. A daughter-in-law is like a daughter. While your brother is alive, you, driven by lust, committed the sin of coveting Ruma, who is like your daughter. Therefore, you deserve the death penalty. Your brother Sugriva has agreed to help me. I promised to restore his wife and kingdom. It is my dharma to fulfill that promise. Hence, I had to punish you appropriately. You should understand this well. Kings, while hunting, set traps, spread nets, and shoot from hiding. None of these are adharma. So what I did is also in accordance with dharma.' Thus Rama explained to Vali.

**Key entities:** Rama, Vali, Ganga, Sugriva

### Chapter 50: Fiftieth Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 19-24
- Source PDF pages: 125, 126, 127, 128
- Printed page numbers: 129, 130, 131, 132
- Key entities: Tara, Vali, Rama, Angada, Sugriva, Hanuman
- Places: Kishkindha

**Summary:** Tara, upon learning that Vali has fallen in battle from Rama's arrow, rushes to the battlefield with Angada. Seeing Vali unconscious, she collapses in grief. Sugriva, witnessing this, becomes sorrowful. Vali, in his dying moments, calls Sugriva, entrusts Angada to him, and gives him a divine golden necklace. He advises Sugriva to rule the kingdom, care for Angada, heed Tara's counsel, and fulfill Rama's mission without hesitation. Vali then dies. Rama consoles both Tara and Sugriva, urging them to accept fate and look forward to Angada's future as prince.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Tara, learning that Vali had fallen in battle from Rama's arrow, came to the battlefield with Angada and saw Vali lying unconscious, she fell to the ground in heart-wrenching grief. What was Sugriva's mental state upon seeing this?

**Options:**
- 1. He rejoiced
- 2. He became sorrowful
- 3. He burned with vengeance
- 4. He laughed to himself

**Correct answer:** He became sorrowful

**Key entities:** Tara, Vali, Rama, Angada, Sugriva

#### Q2

**Question:** While Tara was lamenting over her husband Vali, who lay like a felled tree, who tried to console her?

**Options:**
- 1. Sugriva
- 2. Ruma
- 3. Hanuman
- 4. Angada

**Correct answer:** Hanuman

**Key entities:** Tara, Vali, Hanuman

#### Q3

**Question:** Vali, in his final moments, breathing heavily, called Sugriva, entrusted Angada to him, and said, 'Son Sugriva! Take this while I am still alive.' What did he give?

**Answer:** A divine golden necklace

**Key entities:** Vali, Sugriva, Angada

#### Q4

**Question:** What were the final words Vali spoke to Sugriva?

**Answer:** Vali, with his last breath, looked around and called Sugriva close. He said, 'Brother! Do not consider me a wrongdoer for taking your wife and driving you out of Kishkindha. This is all the play of fate. I did so out of pride and ignorance. The gods did not write on our foreheads the fortune to live together happily as brothers. Therefore we acted contrary to that. I am about to leave this body and go to the next world in a moment. So accept this monkey kingdom. Sugriva! Listen to my words in this final hour. Be crowned king of this kingdom. Brother! Consider my son Angada, who is dearer to me than my life, as your own son from now on; embrace and protect him. Brother! My wife Tara is very perceptive; she can foresee dangers and give advice. Whatever Tara says, follow her words without doubt. Brother! Carry out Rama's mission without any hesitation. If you do not, the arrow that killed me will be waiting to punish you. Sugriva! Take this divine golden necklace while I am still alive; otherwise, after my death, its invincible power will be lost.' Hearing Vali's words, Sugriva's enmity vanished and he did as his brother said. Then Vali told Angada, 'Son! Behave as your uncle has instructed,' and gave up his life.

**Key entities:** Vali, Sugriva, Kishkindha, Angada, Tara, Rama

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Rama console Tara and Sugriva?

**Answer:** Seeing Tara immersed in the ocean of grief, unable to bear her husband's death, Sugriva was moved. He came to Rama and said, 'Lord! You have fulfilled your promise. I have obtained the kingdom. But I have no interest in royal pleasures; indeed, I am disillusioned with life itself.' Rama consoled Sugriva. Then Rama noticed Tara repeatedly looking at him. To remove her sorrow, the Lord looked at her with compassion. When Rama approached her, the chief ministers helped her sit up. She looked at Rama with the intention of speaking harsh words, thinking he had killed her husband with a single arrow. But seeing his divine and auspicious form, her intense anger subsided. She said, 'O Rama! You are beyond time and space. You have incarnated to protect dharma. Therefore, kill me with the same arrow that killed my husband. I will go to his side. A wife is half of her husband's body. Without me, my husband cannot be happy even in heaven. Half of my body has gone with that arrow. Now grant release to this remaining half.' As she spoke thus, Rama consoled her, saying, 'O heroic wife! Do not be so despondent. No one can escape fate. Your son Angada will soon become the crown prince. Thus you will attain happiness.' Thus Rama wisely consoled Tara.

**Key entities:** Rama, Tara, Sugriva, Angada

### Chapter 51: Fifty-first Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 25-29
- Source PDF pages: 128, 129, 130
- Printed page numbers: 132, 133, 134
- Key entities: Vali, Rama, Sugriva, Tara, Angada, Lakshmana, Sita, Hanuman, Nila
- Places: Kishkindha

**Summary:** After Vali's death, Rama consoles Sugriva, Tara, and Angada, and instructs them to perform Vali's funeral rites. Rama then crowns Sugriva as king of Kishkindha. During the rainy season, Rama and Lakshmana reside on Prashravana Hill, awaiting autumn to begin the search for Sita. As autumn arrives, Hanuman reminds Sugriva of his promise to Rama, prompting Sugriva to order Nila to assemble the monkey army.

#### Q1

**Question:** While Sugriva, Tara, and Angada were grieving for Vali's death, Rama and Lakshmana consoled them, saying that no matter how much you lament for the dead Vali, his soul will not find peace. Therefore, what kind of rites did Rama ask them to perform for that corpse?

**Options:**
- 1. Perform cremation rites
- 2. Bury it in the ground
- 3. Leave this corpse and go
- 4. Throw it as food for wild animals

**Correct answer:** Hanuman

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Tara, Angada, Vali, Rama, Lakshmana, Hanuman

#### Q2

**Question:** After performing the funeral rites for Vali, whom did Sri Rama order to be crowned as king of Kishkindha?

**Options:**
- 1. Angada
- 2. Tara
- 3. Sugriva
- 4. Hanuman

**Correct answer:** Tara

**Key entities:** Vali, Rama, Kishkindha, Tara

#### Q3

**Question:** After the coronation, Rama said to Sugriva: 'Friend! This is the rainy season starting from the month of Shravana for four months. It is not a suitable time for war. Therefore, in the meantime, you gather the army. During this time, where did Rama say they would reside?

**Answer:** Nila

**Key entities:** Rama, Sugriva, Nila

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Rama and Lakshmana spend their time on Prashravana Hill?

**Answer:** After Sugriva became lord of the monkeys, he came to Sri Rama, took his blessings, and left. Then Rama and Lakshmana reached Prashravana Hill. On that hill, along with wild animals, bears, monkeys, langurs, and wild cats roamed. There, bushes and creepers spread widely, and great trees grew lushly. Pure water reservoirs were abundant. Along with Lakshmana, Sri Rama decided to reside in a spacious cave on the hilltop and began to stay there. Then Rama said, 'Brother! We told Sugriva that we would start the search for Sita in autumn, didn't we? We have to stay here until this rainy season ends. All the monkeys are dancing with great joy, and the sounds of their musical instruments are heard. Sugriva has obtained kingship. He has his wife. He is happy with relatives and wealth.' Thinking thus, Rama and Lakshmana tried to live happily on Prashravana Hill with the fruits and flowers available there. But because Rama's wife Sita was abducted and far away, remembering her, these comforts and beauties could not give him any happiness. Seeing his brother suffering thus, Lakshmana was distressed. In that state, Soumitri tried to console his brother. 'Brother! Suppressing anger and pain, let us wait until autumn. Let us endure these four months until the rainy season ends, not let our enthusiasm diminish, and both of us live in this forest.' Thus both of them spent their time on that Prashravana Hill.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Sita

#### Q5

**Question:** At the onset of autumn, how did Hanuman suggest to Sugriva regarding Rama's task?

**Answer:** Observing the end of the rainy season and the onset of autumn, Hanuman realized that this was the right time for the search for Sita. He immediately approached Sugriva and said, 'O Lord! You have obtained kingship. You have gained fame and prestige. According to the promise given to your friend, you must accomplish their task. For those who act righteously by providing timely help to friends, kingdom, fame, and valor increase. Otherwise, those who delay and neglect will face adverse results. O Lord! According to the promise you made, you must fulfill Sri Rama's task. O Lord! Sri Rama is our supreme friend. It is only by His grace that we are enjoying these pleasures. Therefore, you should immediately try to repay Him. Command the foremost monkeys to search for Sita.' Hearing these gentle words timely and appropriately presented by Hanuman, the valorous Sugriva ordered a commander named Nila to assemble all the monkey armies from all directions.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sugriva, Rama, Sita, Nila

### Chapter 52: Fifty-second Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 30-35
- Source PDF pages: 130, 131, 132, 133
- Printed page numbers: 134, 135, 136, 137
- Key entities: Sugriva, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Angada, Tara, Hanuman, Nila, Ravana
- Places: Kishkindha, Lanka

**Summary:** With the rainy season over and autumn beginning, Sugriva delays the search for Sita. Rama sends Lakshmana to remind him. Lakshmana goes to Kishkindha, and Angada brings him to Sugriva's palace. Tara pacifies Lakshmana's anger, and Lakshmana rebukes Sugriva for his ingratitude. Tara then explains that Sugriva has already sent for the monkey army and is waiting for their arrival.

#### Q1

**Question:** With the rainy season over and autumn beginning, even though a favorable environment for searching for Sita has arisen, Sugriva is not making efforts in that direction. Rama said, 'Lakshmana! Go and remind him.' In what manner did Rama instruct Lakshmana to behave there?

**Options:**
- 1. Speak harshly
- 2. Speak gently
- 3. Beg
- 4. Speak threateningly

**Correct answer:** Speak gently

**Key entities:** Sita, Sugriva, Rama, Lakshmana

#### Q2

**Question:** According to Rama's suggestion, Lakshmana reached Kishkindha and stood at the main gate. Who informed Sugriva of this news?

**Options:**
- 1. Hanuman
- 2. Tara
- 3. Nila
- 4. Angada

**Correct answer:** Angada

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Kishkindha, Sugriva, Angada

#### Q3

**Question:** By Sugriva's order, Angada brought Lakshmana to Sugriva's inner palace in Kishkindha city. There, who recognized the intensity of anger on Lakshmana's face and tried to appease him?

**Answer:** Tara

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Angada, Lakshmana, Kishkindha, Tara

#### Q4

**Question:** After entering Sugriva's palace, how did Lakshmana rebuke Sugriva?

**Answer:** Upon Angada's invitation, Lakshmana approached the inner palace and saw Tara there. Seeing his anger, Tara said, 'O prince! You are greatly valorous. What is the use of being angry with a weak person? Moreover, you are peace personified. I know the valor of Lord Rama. O Lakshmana! Sugriva, the lord of monkeys, is like a brother to you. Therefore, forgive him with compassion. Though Sugriva is now addicted to pleasures, he has already given appropriate orders to accomplish your task.' Saying thus, Tara led Lakshmana to Sugriva. There, Lakshmana saw Sugriva adorned with divine garments and garlands, surrounded by beautiful women, seated on a golden throne. Seeing Lakshmana, Sugriva panicked, quickly rose, and stood near Lakshmana. Then Lakshmana said, 'O king of monkeys! One who receives help from a friend and does not reciprocate is an ingrate and deserves death; moreover, he is as good as dead among all people. Sugriva! Rama can accomplish any task effortlessly. If you forget the favor done by that lord, today his sharp arrows will send you to your brother. Remember that these pleasures you enjoy are obtained by Rama's grace.' Thus Lakshmana severely rebuked Sugriva.

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Lakshmana, Angada, Tara, Rama

#### Q5

**Question:** Seeing Lakshmana's intensity, how did Tara pacify him?

**Answer:** Seeing Lakshmana severely rebuking Sugriva, Tara said, 'O younger brother of Rama! Sugriva is your friend, the king of monkeys. It is not righteous for a great soul like you to utter such harsh words. This Sugriva is not ungrateful, not deceitful, not a liar, nor crooked. Rama has done a task impossible for others on the battlefield. Sugriva has not forgotten that. It is because of Lord Rama that Sugriva has obtained this monkey kingdom and all pleasures. O lord! Food, sleep, fear, and marital pleasure are natural bodily traits of beings. Without knowing the true facts, it is not righteous to hastily become angry like an ordinary person. O my son! Lakshmana! This lord of monkeys can surely kill Ravana in battle and deliver Sita to Rama. Sugriva alone cannot confront Ravana, who is surrounded by countless demon warriors in Lanka. Therefore, to gather countless monkey warriors to help him in war, Sugriva has already sent many monkey chiefs in all directions. This lord of monkeys is not moving from this city, waiting for their arrival. O Saumitri! Crores of monkey, bear, and langur warriors should have already arrived here. Have mercy on us and give up your anger. The red streaks in your eyes are causing us anxiety.' Thus Tara pacified Lakshmana.

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Tara, Sugriva, Rama, Ravana, Sita, Lanka

### Chapter 53: Fifty-Third Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 36-41
- Source PDF pages: 133, 134, 135
- Printed page numbers: 137, 138, 139
- Key entities: Sugriva, Lakshmana, Rama, Sita, Ravana, Tara, Hanuman, Angada, Nila, Sushena, Jambavan
- Places: Kishkindha, Lanka

**Summary:** Sugriva, pacified by Lakshmana, orders the swift assembly of vanara warriors. He and Lakshmana proceed to meet Rama. Rama advises Sugriva on the course of action: first ascertain Sita's whereabouts and Ravana's location. Sugriva then dispatches search parties to the four directions, appointing leaders and setting a one-month deadline.

#### Q1

**Question:** After Tara and Sugriva's words, Lakshmana became calm and happy, and told Sugriva to go see Rama. Sugriva, pleased, had already sent some to quickly bring the vanara warriors from the four corners of the earth to Kishkindha. Whom did he order to send others to hurry them and bring them here?

**Options:**
- 1. Tara
- 2. Hanuman
- 3. Angada
- 4. Nila

**Correct answer:** Hanuman

**Key entities:** Tara, Sugriva, Lakshmana, Rama, Kishkindha, Hanuman

#### Q2

**Question:** Following Lakshmana's suggestion, Sugriva set out with royal honors to meet Rama. What did Lakshmana and Sugriva ride?

**Options:**
- 1. Elephant
- 2. Horse
- 3. Palanquin
- 4. Chariot

**Correct answer:** Palanquin

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Sugriva, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** While Rama was speaking happily with Sugriva who had come to see him, vanara, bear, and other heroes arrived from the four directions in the millions. Among them was Tara's father. What is his name?

**Answer:** Sushena

**Key entities:** Rama, Sugriva, Tara, Sushena

#### Q4

**Question:** When Sugriva showed his entire army to Rama, how did Rama advise Sugriva on the duty to be performed?

**Answer:** While Rama and Sugriva were talking on Prashravana mountain, Sugriva perceived that a vast vanara army had arrived and stood in suitable places. He said to Rama: 'Lord! These powerful vanara chiefs have come and are stationed in appropriate places. They are all immensely strong like rutting elephants, can change form at will, and are equal to demons and titans. All this is your army, under your control. Command them as you wish.' Hearing this, Rama, pleased, said: 'O wise one! Until now, we need to know whether Sita is alive or dead, and the place where Ravana is. First, we must ascertain Sita's whereabouts and Ravana's location. Then we will discuss the course of action and decide appropriately. O king of vanaras! The search for Sita is not possible by me or Lakshmana. You are the one who can accomplish this task. Its success lies in your hands. There is no doubt. Therefore, think properly and command your followers.' After Rama spoke thus wisely, Sugriva called his army commander Vinata and ordered him to go east with a suitable army, search for Sita there, and return within a month. Thus Sugriva sent capable leaders to all four directions for the search of Sita.

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Rama, Sita, Ravana, Lakshmana

#### Q5

**Question:** For the search of Sita, whom did Sugriva send to the south, in what manner, and with what instructions?

**Answer:** For the search of Sita, Sugriva sent thoroughly tested vanaras to the southern direction. Among them were Nila, Hanuman, Jambavan, Suhotra, Sharari, Sharagulma, Gaja, Gavaksha, Gavaya, Sushena, Rishabha, Mainda, Dvivida, Vijaya, Gandhamadana, Ulkamukha, Asanga, and other vanara heroes. He appointed Angada as their leader and sent them south. Notably, in that direction lies Lanka ruled by Ravana. Sugriva described in detail the rivers, mountains, cities, and countries they would encounter. He set a deadline of one month and said: 'Whoever finds Sita and returns within this deadline will be most dear to me, will enjoy pleasures equal to mine, and even if he has many faults, he will be as dear to me as my own life. Therefore, O friends! You possess unparalleled strength and valor. Begin the effort suitable for Rama's task now.' Thus Sugriva spoke to Angada and others and sent them to the south.

**Key entities:** Sita, Sugriva, Nila, Hanuman, Jambavan, Sushena, Angada, Lanka, Ravana, Rama

### Chapter 54: Fifty-fourth Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 42-47
- Source PDF pages: 135, 136, 137, 138
- Printed page numbers: 139, 140, 141, 142
- Key entities: Sugriva, Sita, Rama, Vali, Angada, Hanuman, Sushena, Nala, Jambavan
- Places: Lanka, Kishkindha, Rishyamuka

**Summary:** Sugriva dispatches monkey warriors to the four directions to search for Sita. He describes the geographical features of each direction. Rama asks Sugriva how he knows the entire earth, and Sugriva recounts his exile and travels while fleeing from Vali. The monkeys return from their search without success, except for the southern group led by Angada and Hanuman, who are expected to find Sita in Lanka.

#### Q1

**Question:** Sugriva, describing the mountains, rivers, cities, and janapadas in the western direction for the search of Sita, under whose leadership did he send the monkey warriors?

**Options:**
- 1. Shatavali
- 2. Hanuman
- 3. Nala
- 4. Sushena

**Correct answer:** Sushena

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Sita, Sushena

#### Q2

**Question:** To search for Rama's wife Sita, Sugriva described all the mountains, rivers, forests, forts, janapadas, and cities in the northern direction and made whom the leader to send the monkey warriors?

**Options:**
- 1. Jambavan
- 2. Gavaya
- 3. Shatavali
- 4. Vijaya

**Correct answer:** Shatavali

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Sugriva

#### Q3

**Question:** Among the warriors going to the southern direction, Rama called Hanuman and gave him which object as his token?

**Answer:** ring

**Key entities:** Rama, Hanuman

#### Q4

**Question:** When Rama asked Sugriva, 'How do you know all these details of the earth?', how did Sugriva answer the lord?

**Answer:** After the monkey warriors had departed in all directions as per Sugriva's command, Rama asked Sugriva, 'How do you know about this entire earth?' Then the monkey king said, 'O Lord! My elder brother Vali, chasing a demon named Dundubhi who had the form of a buffalo, entered a cave. I waited outside the cave for my brother. After a long time, my brother did not come out. Then blood started flowing from the cave entrance. Fearing that it was my brother's blood and that the demon might come out and kill me, I closed the cave entrance with a large boulder, gave up hope of my brother's life, and thinking the demon also died in the cave, I returned to Kishkindha. Immediately, the citizens of Kishkindha made me king. Meanwhile, my brother, who had killed Dundubhi, returned to Kishkindha. Seeing Vali, I fearfully and respectfully handed over the kingdom to him. But Vali, being offended and burning with anger, tried to kill me. Then, along with my ministers who followed me, I fled. Thus, I first went eastward. My brother did not leave me; he kept chasing me. In that way, I went in all directions. Finally, I went to Rishyamuka mountain, and knowing that Vali would not come due to a curse, I began to live there. O best of men! Thus, I have traveled and seen the entire earth in all directions.' Thus Sugriva informed Lord Ramachandra.

**Key entities:** Rama, Sugriva, Vali, Kishkindha, Rishyamuka

#### Q5

**Question:** Which monkey chiefs returned after searching for Sita as per Sugriva's command? What information did they convey to Sugriva?

**Answer:** All the monkey troops went to various places as per Sugriva's command to search for Sita. They thoroughly searched lakes, riverbanks, bowers, forests full of trees and creepers, desert places where even grass did not grow, places difficult to cross due to rivers, hills, valleys, cities, villages, mountains, and dense forests. Thus, searching all day, they gathered at designated places at night, eating fruits available there to satisfy their hunger. For a month they searched for mother Janaki, but not finding any trace of her, they returned disappointed to Prashravana hill and met the monkey king Sugriva. Then they all said, 'O monkey king! As you commanded, we searched every inch in the directions we went, even in inaccessible places where one could not step. But our efforts did not bear fruit. We could not find any trace of mother Sita. O great king! Hanuman, who went southward under the leadership of Angada, will surely find Sita's trace. Because in that direction lies the city of Lanka. Therefore, that great soul will bring us the good news of mother's whereabouts.' Thus the monkey warriors informed Sugriva.

**Key entities:** Sita, Sugriva, Hanuman, Angada, Lanka

### Chapter 55: Fifty-fifth Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 48-53
- Source PDF pages: 138, 139, 140
- Printed page numbers: 142, 143, 144
- Key entities: Angada, Sita, Hanuman, Shabari, Simhika, Brahma, Rama, Dasharatha, Ravana, Sugriva
- Places: Ayodhya

**Summary:** The monkey warriors led by Angada begin their search for Sita in the southern direction from the Vindhya mountain region. Suffering from hunger and thirst, they enter a cave called Rikshabila, where they meet the ascetic Svayamprabha. She explains that the cave was created by the demon architect Maya for his pleasure with the apsara Hema. After the monkeys refresh themselves, Svayamprabha uses her ascetic power to transport them to the southern seashore.

#### Q1

**Question:** From which mountain region did the monkey warriors, led by Angada, first begin their search for Sita when they went to the southern direction?

**Options:**
- 1. From the Vindhya mountain region
- 2. From the Gandhamadana region
- 3. From the Himalayan region
- 4. From the Satpura mountain

**Correct answer:** From the Vindhya mountain region

**Key entities:** Angada, Sita

#### Q2

**Question:** While searching for Sita, Hanuman and other prominent monkeys, suffering from great thirst and fatigue, entered a cave called Rikshabila. There they saw a radiant yogini. What is her name?

**Options:**
- 1. Shabari
- 2. Vedavati
- 3. Svayamprabha
- 4. Simhika

**Correct answer:** Svayamprabha

**Key entities:** Sita, Hanuman

#### Q3

**Question:** When Maruti, seeing the splendor in Rikshabila, asked the ascetic there, 'Mother! Who created this forest?', what answer did she give?

**Answer:** The demon architect Maya

**Key entities:** Hanuman

#### Q4

**Question:** In Rikshabila, how did Hanuman respond to the ascetic's questions and the ascetic to his doubts?

**Answer:** Led by Angada, the monkey warriors, suffering from hunger and thirst, saw birds with wet wings emerging from a cave and, thinking there might be water, entered the cave with effort. After going some distance, they saw a vast place with buildings, sweet roots and fruits, and pure water. In that area, an ascetic wearing a deer skin was present. Hanuman humbly asked, 'Mother, who are you? Whose is this extremely radiant place? We have entered this cave unable to bear hunger and thirst.' The ascetic replied, 'Formerly, the demon architect Maya performed penance here for Brahma. Later, by the grace of the Grandfather, he acquired the science of architecture. That Maya created this region for his own enjoyment and, being attached to the apsara Hema, stayed here. That Hema entrusted me with the responsibility of protecting these forests. Without hesitation, partake of these foods and water.' Then all the monkey warriors joyfully satisfied their hunger and thirst. Later, the ascetic revealed her name as Svayamprabha and asked Hanuman to tell his story. Maruti said, 'Mother! Sri Rama, the eldest son of Dasaratha who ruled Ayodhya, was in exile when the demon Ravana abducted his wife, Sita. Searching for Sita, we have all come here.' Thus, Svayamprabha and Hanuman exchanged their details.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Angada, Brahma, Rama, Dasharatha, Ayodhya, Ravana, Sita

#### Q5

**Question:** How did all the monkey warriors reach the seashore from Rikshabila?

**Answer:** Hanuman said to the ascetic Svayamprabha, 'O righteous lady! We all seek refuge in you. The deadline set by our king Sugriva has ended in this cave. We have a great task to accomplish, but circumstances are unfavorable. We are trapped here.' Hearing Hanuman's words, Svayamprabha said, 'O monkeys! It is difficult for those who enter this cave to come out alive. But by the power of my penance performed with discipline, I will deliver you from this cave. All of you close your eyes.' Then all of them covered their eyes with both hands. When they opened their eyes again, they were all near the southern seashore. Then Svayamprabha said, 'May you be blessed! I am going to my abode,' and she left. All the prominent monkeys, hearing the roar of the sea, rested in the shade of the great trees there.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sugriva

### Chapter 56: Fifty-sixth Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 53-57
- Source PDF pages: 140, 141, 142, 143
- Printed page numbers: 144, 145, 146, 147
- Key entities: Angada, Sugriva, Hanuman, Rama, Jatayu, Sita, Sampati, Lakshmana, Tara, Jambavan, Vali, Dasharatha, Ravana
- Places: Ayodhya, Dandaka Forest, Rishyamuka, Kishkindha

**Summary:** The monkeys, having emerged from the cave, sit despondently on the seashore. Angada suggests they perform prayopavesha (fast unto death) rather than face Sugriva empty-handed. Hanuman tries to dissuade him. Angada recounts Rama's exile, Jatayu's death, and Sita's abduction. The vulture Sampati overhears and inquires about his brother Jatayu. Angada narrates the full story of Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Sugriva, and Jatayu's death.

#### Q1

**Question:** Who said, 'If we go before Sugriva empty-handed without finding Sita's trace, he will sentence us to death. Rather than going there and dying, it is better for us to perform prayopavesha here'?

**Options:**
- 1. Tara
- 2. Hanuman
- 3. Angada
- 4. Jambavan

**Correct answer:** Angada

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Sita, Angada

#### Q2

**Question:** Who said to Angada, who was contemplating prayopavesha, 'O young prince! Come with us, complete the search for Sita, and even if the deadline is exceeded, if we go to the king, he will welcome us. Therefore, let us think about the search for Sita'?

**Options:**
- 1. Jambavan
- 2. Suhotra
- 3. Gavaya
- 4. Hanuman

**Correct answer:** Hanuman

**Key entities:** Angada, Sita, Hanuman

#### Q3

**Question:** Despite Maruti's many attempts, Angada did not turn his mind away from prayopavesha. While he was recounting Rama's exile, Jatayu's death, and Sita's abduction, which bird nearby asked for details about Jatayu's death?

**Answer:** Sampati

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Angada, Rama, Jatayu, Sita, Sampati

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Sampati learn the news of his younger brother's death?

**Answer:** Sampati, the king of vultures, was sitting on a mountain peak near the monkeys who were preparing for prayopavesha. He thought that if they died, he could eat them one by one. Then Angada spoke, saying that Jatayu had fought the demon and died trying to protect Sita. Hearing this, Sampati loudly asked who was speaking about his brother Jatayu's death and requested to be brought down from the peak to hear more.

**Key entities:** Sampati, Angada, Jatayu, Sita

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Angada explain the news of Jatayu's death and their search for Sita to Sampati?

**Answer:** Angada went to Sampati and said: 'O king of birds! In the past, the monkey king Rksharajas had two sons, Vali and Sugriva. I am Angada, son of Vali. The eldest son of King Dasaratha of Ayodhya, Sri Rama, came to the forest with his wife Sita and brother Lakshmana to fulfill his father's word. While living in Dandaka forest, they became friends with Jatayu, who was a friend of Dasaratha. When the demon Ravana tried to abduct Sita in the absence of Rama and Lakshmana, Jatayu intervened and was killed by Ravana. Rama and Lakshmana, searching for Sita, befriended Sugriva on Rishyamuka mountain. Sugriva told Rama of the injustice done by my father Vali, and Rama killed Vali, making Sugriva king of Kishkindha. Out of gratitude for Rama's great favor, we, obeying King Sugriva's command, have been searching for Sita and have arrived here.' Thus Angada explained the news of Jatayu's death and the reason for their arrival.

**Key entities:** Angada, Jatayu, Sita, Sampati, Vali, Sugriva, Dasharatha, Ayodhya, Rama, Lakshmana, Dandaka Forest, Ravana, Rishyamuka, Kishkindha

### Chapter 57: Fifty-seventh Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 58-62
- Source PDF pages: 143, 144, 145
- Printed page numbers: 147, 148, 149
- Key entities: Sampati, Ravana, Sita, Jatayu, Rama, Angada, Vayu, Dasharatha, Lakshmana
- Places: Lanka, Dandaka Forest

**Summary:** Sampati tells the monkeys about seeing Ravana abducting Sita, describes Lanka's distance, recounts his own story of losing his wings while protecting Jatayu, and relates the prophecy of sage Nishakara that his wings will regrow after he informs the monkeys about Sita.

#### Q1

**Question:** "I will cooperate in Rama's work. O monkeys! I saw Ravana abducting a beautiful woman and carrying her away. Ravana's residence is the city of Lanka. How far did Sampati say Lanka is from here?"

**Options:**
- 1. 70 yojanas
- 2. 90 yojanas
- 3. 100 yojanas
- 4. 80 yojanas

**Correct answer:** 100 yojanas

**Key entities:** Rama, Ravana, Lanka, Sampati

#### Q2

**Question:** Sampati, while narrating the abduction of Sita, said that one day in those times, when his son had gone in search of food, he saw a wicked man abducting a woman. What is the name of Sampati's son?

**Options:**
- 1. Anuru
- 2. Suparshva
- 3. Vainateya
- 4. Jatayu

**Correct answer:** Suparshva

**Key entities:** Sampati, Sita

#### Q3

**Question:** Sampati, telling Angada and other monkeys about Sita, said: "Once, my wings were burnt by the sun's heat and I fell in the Vindhya mountain region. There I took refuge with a great sage who comforted me." What is the name of that sage?

**Answer:** Nishakara Maharshi

**Key entities:** Sampati, Angada, Sita

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Sampati explain to sage Nishakara the reason for his wings being burnt?

**Answer:** Sampati, whose wings were scorched by the sun's heat, went to the Vindhya mountain region and met the great sage Nishakara. The sage asked: "O Sampati! You two are brothers and can assume any form at will. I have seen you before. How did this happen to you, who are equal to Vayu?" Then Sampati replied: "O sage! We two brothers, proud of our strength and desiring to test our prowess, competed and flew up into the sky. As we flew up and looked down, the cities, mountains, rivers, and oceans on earth appeared very small. Then our bodies sweated from the heat of the sun's rays. We became afraid. Our senses and mind began to fail. We could not discern directions. Then Jatayu, without telling me, began to slip downwards. Seeing the situation, to support my younger brother, I came near him and covered Jatayu with my wings. Thus he was protected from the hot rays of the sun, but my wings were burnt and I fell to the ground. I thought Jatayu would have fallen in the Dandaka forest. I fell in this Vindhya mountain region. My brother became separated." Thus Sampati narrated his story to sage Nishakara.

**Key entities:** Sampati, Vayu, Jatayu, Dandaka Forest

#### Q5

**Question:** How did sage Nishakara console Sampati?

**Answer:** Seeing Sampati weeping before him, sage Nishakara, perceiving with his yogic vision, said: "O Sampati! Do not grieve. Your burnt wings will grow back. Likewise, your vision will also be restored. Your diminished life force, strength, and valor will revive. I have foreseen with my divine sight a great event that will happen in the future. Sri Rama, the eldest son of King Dasharatha of the Ikshvaku dynasty, will come to the Dandaka forest with his wife and brother to fulfill his father's command. A demon named Ravana will abduct Rama's wife. Neither gods nor demons can do anything to Ravana. That same Ravana will be slain by Sri Rama. Good will come to all creatures. Monkeys searching for Sita will come to you. Then you should inform them about Rama's wife. Until then, do not move from this place. Wait for the right time and circumstances. As soon as you tell the monkeys about Sita, your wings will grow back. O Sampati! I wish to see Rama and Lakshmana, but my body will not last until then. Therefore, I must give up this body." Thus Sampati told the monkey chiefs what the sage Nishakara, who had foreseen the future, had told him.

**Key entities:** Sampati, Rama, Dasharatha, Dandaka Forest, Ravana, Sita, Lakshmana

### Chapter 58: Fifty-eighth Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 63-67
- Source PDF pages: 145, 146, 147, 148
- Printed page numbers: 149, 150, 151, 152
- Key entities: Sampati, Angada, Jambavan, Hanuman, Sita, Rama, Nila, Sugriva, Lakshmana, Vayu, Indra
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** Sampati's wings grow back as foretold by sage Nishakara. The monkeys spend the night and in the morning, Angada asks who can leap the hundred-yojana ocean. Jambavan declares his ability to leap ninety yojanas. Jambavan then inspires Hanuman by recounting his divine birth and powers, urging him to undertake the leap. Hanuman resolves to cross the ocean, expands his form, and prepares to leap from Mount Mahendra.

#### Q1

**Question:** While the monkey leaders were watching, Sampati's wings grew back. Then Sampati, looking at his wings with delight, said, 'O monkeys! As the sage Nishakara said, my wings have grown back. In the same way, you will also be able to find the whereabouts of Mother Sita.' What color were Sampati's wings that grew back?

**Options:**
- 1. White
- 2. Green
- 3. Blue
- 4. Red

**Correct answer:** Red

**Key entities:** Sampati, Sita

#### Q2

**Question:** After Sampati encouraged the monkey leaders and left, they all spent the night there. Waking at dawn, who asked, 'O monkey leaders! Whoever can leap this hundred-yojana ocean and accomplish Rama's task, give me your assurance'?

**Options:**
- 1. Angada
- 2. Hanuman
- 3. Jambavan
- 4. Nila

**Correct answer:** Angada

**Key entities:** Sampati, Rama, Angada

#### Q3

**Question:** As part of declaring their abilities for the ocean leap, how many yojanas did Jambavan say he could go?

**Answer:** Ninety yojanas

**Key entities:** Jambavan

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Jambavan inspire Hanuman for the ocean leap?

**Answer:** Observing the many lakhs of monkey army sunk in despair, Jambavan decided to inspire Hanuman: 'O Anjaneya! You are incomparable among all monkeys. You know all the scriptures. O son of Vayu! In your splendor, strength, and valor, you are in no way inferior to Sugriva or Rama and Lakshmana. O Hanuma! The foremost of apsaras, 'Punjakasthala', due to a curse, was born on earth as Anjana Devi. She became the wife of the monkey chief Kesari. Being a shape-shifter, she assumed a human form adorned with all ornaments and was sporting on a mountain peak when Vayu, captivated by her beauty and youth, embraced her. Anjana Devi was frightened by the unexpected turn. Then Vayu said, 'O beautiful one! Though I have embraced you, no stain will come to you. Do not fear.
