A great hero and wise being will be born to you.' So saying, he left. Then your mother gave birth to you. When you, thinking the rising sun to be a fruit, went towards it, Indra stopped you. Angered by this, Vayu caused all the worlds to become still. Then all the gods, pleased, gave you many boons. Therefore, O Hanuma! Among all here, you alone are fit for the ocean leap. So, arise at once.' Thus Jambavan inspired Hanuman.

**Key entities:** Jambavan, Hanuman, Sugriva, Rama, Lakshmana, Vayu, Indra

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Hanuman become determined for the ocean leap?

**Answer:** To immediately cross the ocean of a hundred yojanas, Maruti gathered his valor within and began to expand his wondrous form. Seeing that great hero, the entire monkey army abandoned their sorrow and praised Hanuman. They shouted loudly and were filled with joy and wonder. Then Hanuman, pleased with the monkeys' praise, raised his tail, further increased his strength, and grew. Then the form of that great soul was wonderful. Then Anjaneya said, 'I will leap this ocean, reach Lanka, and see Mother Sita. May you all rejoice! I am confident that I can leap even thousands of yojanas.' As the radiant and powerful monkey chief Hanuman spoke, all the monkeys looked at that lord with joy and wonder. Then Maruti said to Jambavan, 'This ordinary ground cannot bear my foot for leaping. Therefore, I will place my foot on Mount Mahendra and leap the ocean from there.' So he climbed Mount Mahendra and, with concentrated mind, began to think about Lanka.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Lanka, Sita, Jambavan

### Chapter 59: Fifty-ninth Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 1-5
- Source PDF pages: 148, 149, 150
- Printed page numbers: 152, 153, 154
- Key entities: Hanuman, Mainaka, Surasa, Simhika, Sita, Ravana, Garuda, Brahma, Rama
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** Hanuman leaps from Mahendragiri towards Lanka. The ocean asks Mount Mainaka to provide rest. The gods ask Surasa to test Hanuman. A shadow-grabber named Simhika tries to stop him. Hanuman enters Lanka at night, defeats the guardian Lankini, and searches for Sita in Ravana's palace.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Hanuman set out southwards from Mahendragiri, flying like Garuda, the ocean noticed him and, wishing to give some rest to the Maruti going for the sake of the Ikshvaku clan, which mountain inside him did he ask to come out and provide shelter to Hanuman?

**Options:**
- 1. Vidya mountain
- 2. Sheshachala mountain
- 3. Mainaka mountain
- 4. Meru mountain

**Correct answer:** Mainaka mountain

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Garuda, Mainaka

#### Q2

**Question:** The gods, wishing to test Hanuman's strength, ordered whom to obstruct his path?

**Options:**
- 1. Diti
- 2. Atidhi
- 3. Naga-mata Surasa
- 4. Kaliya

**Correct answer:** Naga-mata Surasa

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Surasa

#### Q3

**Question:** As Hanuman was proceeding towards Lanka, a grotesque shadow-catcher in the ocean grabbed his shadow and pulled him back, trying to stop his speed. What is her name?

**Answer:** Simhika

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Lanka, Simhika

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Anjaneya enter Lanka?

**Answer:** The mighty Hanuman, having leaped over the ocean which was impossible for others, fixed his gaze on the city of Lanka situated on Trikuta mountain. While roaming on that mountain, various trees showered flowers on him. Without any fatigue from crossing the ocean, the son of the wind wandered here and there, seeing the forests and groves, and observed the city of Lanka on the mountain. Then Hanuman thought for a moment: first I must know whether Sita is alive or not. In this Lanka guarded by extremely cruel and powerful demons, entering in this form is not advisable; it is better to reduce his form and enter at night. So he waited for some time. When darkness fell and the city of Lanka shone with the light of house lamps and moonlight, Maruti saw it. Then the foremost of monkeys, Maruti, while entering Lanka, was confronted by the guardian deity of Lanka, Lankini, who stood before him and asked, 'Who are you? Why have you come to this city of Lanka? Tell the truth before you lose your life at my hands.' Seeing Lankini standing in a grotesque form, he said, 'I came to see the beautiful city of Lanka.' 'O evil-minded one! You cannot enter Lanka without defeating me,' said Lankini and struck Maruti hard. Immediately Hanuman clenched his fist and struck her with his left fist. Struck down to the ground, Lankini said, 'O foremost of monkeys! As Brahma said long ago, Lanka will be destroyed by the one who strikes me.' And she gave way for Maruti to enter Lanka. Thus Maruti entered Lanka.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Lanka, Sita, Brahma

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Maruti search for Sita in Lanka?

**Answer:** The greatly radiant Hanuman assumed a tiny form and, instead of entering through the main gate, jumped over the rampart and placed his left foot first, as if placing his left foot on the enemy's head, and entered Lanka. That foremost of monkeys proceeded along the royal road adorned with flowering trees on both sides. From the houses there, sounds of various musical instruments were heard. Maruti, skilled in accomplishing his master's task, looked at every house and moved forward. Thousands of demons guarded Ravana's mansion. Hanuman secretly entered Ravana's inner palace, which was in the midst of a very tight security cordon. With the rising of the autumn moon, darkness disappeared and people rejoiced. The night-wanderers delighted in eating flesh. Men and women, having given up quarrels, reveled in the pleasures of love. Some were playing the veena strings. Others, of good conduct, enjoyed the comforts of bed with their husbands. The wise Hanuman examined every house in search of Sita. Though he searched many places, he could not find any trace of Sita, the righteous wife of Rama. Thus Hanuman continued searching for Sita.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Lanka, Ravana, Rama

### Chapter 60: Sixtieth Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 6-11
- Source PDF pages: 150, 151, 152, 153
- Printed page numbers: 154, 155, 156, 157
- Key entities: Hanuman, Ravana, Sita, Mandodari, Brahma, Prahasta, Virupaksha, Kubera, Varuna, Vali, Indra, Rama
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** Hanuman secretly enters Ravana's inner palace in search of Sita. He observes the grandeur of the palace, the guards, and the sleeping women, including Ravana. He briefly mistakes Mandodari for Sita but then reasons that Sita would not be sleeping peacefully or adorned with jewels. He continues his search without finding Sita.

#### Q1

**Question:** Hanuman thought that Ravana had the palaces, built using the diamonds, cat's eye gems, etc., won in battles, constructed by whom?

**Options:**
- 1. Shukracharya
- 2. Maya Brahma
- 3. Prahasta
- 4. Virupaksha

**Correct answer:** Maya Brahma

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Ravana, Brahma

#### Q2

**Question:** After seeing many palaces, Hanuman saw the Pushpaka Vimana, which was like heaven on earth. With whom did Ravana fight and win to bring it?

**Options:**
- 1. Varuna
- 2. Shankara
- 3. Vali
- 4. Kubera

**Correct answer:** Kubera

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Ravana, Kubera

#### Q3

**Question:** While searching very keenly for Sita in Ravana's great mansion, Maruti saw a woman sleeping on a special bed among some divine women sleeping near Ravana on a divine bed. For a moment, he thought she might be Sita. Who was that woman?

**Answer:** Mandodari

**Key entities:** Sita, Ravana, Hanuman, Mandodari

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Hanuman search for Sita in Ravana's inner palace?

**Answer:** Searching for Sita, Hanuman entered Ravana's inner palace without being seen by anyone. That Ravana's mansion was half a yojana wide and one yojana long, vast and spacious. The building was guarded by many armed rakshasas. The great palace was filled with Ravana's wives and also princesses he had forcibly brought by his valor. The wealth and splendor of Kubera, the lord of wealth, and the opulence like Indra's were firmly established in that royal palace. There were many secret chambers there. In those houses on the Pushpaka, Maruti saw people who were exhausted from drinking, eating, and sports until midnight, and were falling asleep. There, while Ravana was sleeping, the lamps burning brightly seemed to stare without blinking at his radiance. Among all the women there, some were abducted by Ravana, while others had come attracted to Ravana. All of them were attracted to Ravana. But Hanuman thought that if Sita, the wife of Rama, were also happily united with her husband like all these women were comfortable, then it would have been well for Ravana. Thus, however much Hanuman searched in Ravana's mansion for Sita, he did not find any trace of her.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Ravana, Kubera, Indra, Rama

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Hanuman rejoice when he mistakenly thought Sita was in Ravana's mansion? What kind of thought did he have afterwards?

**Answer:** Maruti, searching very keenly for Sita in Ravana's mansion, saw a bed. It was inlaid with crystals and gems. That place was filled with various fragrant breezes and incense. Some women were holding fans and waving them. Hanuman saw the great hero Ravana sleeping on that bed. Then Maruti, approaching Ravana, thought, 'Fie! This is a wicked man who has abducted another's wife.' He saw a woman of exceptional beauty among all the sleeping women, sleeping on a specially arranged couch. Her form was charming with pure radiance. Seeing her, Maruti was overjoyed, thinking he had found Sita, and rejoiced greatly. Immediately, that great monkey began to think correctly about Sita. 'Is it possible for Sita, separated from Rama, to sleep like this? In that state, would she have any interest in food and drink? Would she think of wearing ornaments? No matter how great a man, would she allow him near her? Not only humans, are there any gods equal to Rama? Therefore, this is not Sita.' Having decided thus, Hanuman, eager to search for Sita again, began to wander here and there.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Ravana, Rama

### Chapter 61: Sixty-first Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 12-16
- Source PDF pages: 153, 154, 155
- Printed page numbers: 157, 158, 159
- Key entities: Hanuman, Sita, Sampati, Rama, Ravana, Jatayu, Jambavan, Vali, Viradha, Khara
- Places: Lanka, Ashoka Grove, Rishyamuka

**Summary:** Hanuman searches Lanka but cannot find Sita. He recalls Sampati's words that Sita is in Lanka. He enters the Ashoka grove and hides in a flowering tree, waiting for Sita. He sees a woman in soiled silk, surrounded by rakshasis, and identifies her as Sita based on descriptions from Rama and the golden-bordered garment dropped during her abduction. He laments her suffering.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Hanuman searched all of Lanka including Ravana's harem but did not find Sita, he became somewhat disappointed. Nevertheless, whose words did he recall that Sita was indeed in Lanka?

**Options:**
- 1. Jatayu
- 2. Svayamprabha
- 3. Sampati
- 4. Jambavan

**Correct answer:** Sampati

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Lanka, Ravana, Sita, Sampati

#### Q2

**Question:** After searching all over Lanka and not finding any trace of Sita, Hanuman was distressed in various ways and finally entered a grove. What is the name of that grove?

**Options:**
- 1. Ashoka Grove
- 2. Saugandhika Grove
- 3. Chaitraratha Grove
- 4. Nandana Grove

**Correct answer:** Ashoka Grove

**Key entities:** Lanka, Sita, Hanuman, Ashoka Grove

#### Q3

**Question:** Maruti thought that if Sita was alive, she would surely come to this river with sacred waters. Waiting for the sight of Rama's wife in that grove, he hid among the dense leaves of a tree that was in full bloom and looked around. What is the name of the tree that Hanuman climbed?

**Answer:** Ashoka tree

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Hanuman recognize Sita?

**Answer:** Hanuman, perched on an Ashoka tree, waited for a glimpse of Sita and surveyed the entire Ashoka grove. The grove was adorned with wish-fulfilling trees and creepers, and trees bearing fruit and flowers in all seasons bent under their weight. As he gazed at the beauty, he turned his eyes and saw a woman wearing soiled garments, with a suitable figure, seated firmly on the ground, surrounded by rakshasis. She was emaciated from fasting, dejected, and sighing repeatedly. Hanuman reasoned within himself and considered various ways to identify her. She wore a single garment, which though soiled, was silk and still lustrous. With a body wasted by sorrow, as if in meditation, with modesty and grief, she was very dejected. Based on his reasoning, Hanuman concluded that this was the Sita who had been abducted by the lustful Ravana. The features of the woman he had seen on Rishyamuka Mountain were visible in her. All the form, beauty, and splendor that Rama had described were present in her. Therefore, she was indeed Sita. The golden-bordered green garment that had been dropped on Rishyamuka Mountain when Ravana abducted Sita was the same as the one she wore. This was enough to firmly decide that she was Sita. Thus Maruti recognized Sita.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Ashoka Grove, Ravana, Rishyamuka, Rama

#### Q5

**Question:** Seeing Sita in distress, how did Maruti lament?

**Answer:** Seeing Sita seated on the bare ground, Hanuman thought: Praising in his mind the virtuous Sita and Rama, who are worthy of praise by all people, he became absorbed in meditation for a moment and then, seeing Sita's dejected state, began to weep profusely. 'For this embodiment of virtues, Rama killed Vali. Not only Vali, but also Viradha, Khara, and fourteen thousand other rakshasas were destroyed for her sake. Moreover, for this great pativrata, Rama would give up even the lordship of the three worlds. She is holding on to life with the hope that she will one day be reunited with her husband. Seeing her, who is worthy of enjoying divine pleasures with Rama, now suffering among these rakshasis, my mind is disturbed. What need be said of the supremely compassionate Rama?' Thus the great hero Hanuman, after thoroughly considering these matters, firmly concluded 'This is Sita' and remained hidden among the leaves of that tree, grieving.

**Key entities:** Sita, Hanuman, Rama, Vali, Viradha, Khara

### Chapter 62: Sixty-second Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 17-21
- Source PDF pages: 155, 156, 157, 158
- Printed page numbers: 159, 160, 161, 162
- Key entities: Hanuman, Sita, Ravana, Rama, Janaka, Indra, Lakshmana
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** Hanuman, hidden in a tree, observes Sita surrounded by demonesses. He confirms her identity and feels sorrow. Ravana arrives with his harem and tries to seduce Sita, but she rebukes him fiercely, declaring her devotion to Rama and threatening him with Rama's vengeance.

#### Q1

**Question:** Seeing Sita guarded by demonesses of various grotesque forms, Maruti rejoiced thinking 'Whatever happens, I have seen Rama's wife.' But at that time, which constellation did Sita appear to him like, surrounded by inauspicious planets?

**Options:**
- 1. Chitta
- 2. Vishakha
- 3. Swati
- 4. Rohini

**Correct answer:** Rohini

**Key entities:** Sita, Hanuman, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Hanuman, hiding on a branch of a tree near the tree where Sita was sitting, covered by dense leaves and flowers. When did Ravana, lustful and accompanied by many harem women, come to the place where Sita was?

**Options:**
- 1. Noon
- 2. Morning
- 3. Evening
- 4. Midnight

**Correct answer:** Morning

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Ravana

#### Q3

**Question:** As the rakshasa king Ravana approached her, Sita, distressed and afraid, with folded hands, appeared to Hanuman to be praying to whom for Ravana's defeat by Rama?

**Answer:** The answer is in the answer key period.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sita, Hanuman, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** While Hanuman watched from amidst the leaves on the tree, in what manner did Ravana try to tempt Sita?

**Answer:** Ravana, accompanied by harem women, approached Sita and said: 'O beautiful one! Sita! You hide your face seeing me. O large-eyed one, I love you. O beloved! Accept me. O Sita, neither humans, nor rakshasas, nor devas and gandharvas can do anything to me. You need not fear me. Forcibly abducting and enjoying other women is the dharma of rakshasas. Though lust is aroused in me, I will not touch you without your love. Do not fear. Trust me. Love me wholeheartedly. O auspicious one! Look at me once, and behold my wealth, splendor, and fame. Rama, clad in bark garments, exiled to the forest, can give you nothing. He has lost victory and wealth, lives in the forest observing ascetic vows, sleeps on the bare ground. Whether he is alive or dead is unknown. It is impossible for him to regain you from me. In my harem are many virtuous women. If you accept me, they will all serve you. O beautiful one! Rama is in no way equal to me. I will give you my wealth and kingdom. Accept me.' Thus Hanuman saw Ravana tempting Sita in many ways.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Ravana, Sita, Rama

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Sita scornfully speak to Ravana when he tried to tempt her?

**Answer:** Hearing the terrible Ravana's words, the distressed Sita, weeping, meditated on her husband Rama who had used a blade of grass as a Brahmastra against Kakasura, and placing a blade of grass as a barrier, said: 'O Ravana! Turn your mind away from me and towards your own wives. I was born in the noble Janaka dynasty and married into the pure Raghu dynasty. I am the lawful wife of Rama, who is devoted to one wife. Being a pativrata, have proper vision. Follow the disciplined life of virtuous men. Are there no virtuous men in this land? Compare yourself to yourself and enjoy with your wives. If you wish to avoid a terrible death at Rama's hands, reunite me with the righteous Rama. Rama is righteous and compassionate to those who seek refuge. He will surely forgive you. Even if you escape weapons from Indra and other gods, no one can save you from Rama's arrow. My husband, the destroyer of enemies, will soon take me from you. O wretch! Unable to defeat my people in battle, you chose a time when Rama and Lakshmana were absent and abducted me like a thief. In all the fourteen worlds, no one can save you from Rama's arrow.' Thus Hanuman heard Sita scornfully speaking to Ravana.

**Key entities:** Sita, Ravana, Rama, Janaka, Indra, Lakshmana, Hanuman

### Chapter 63: Sixty-third Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 22-26
- Source PDF pages: 158, 159, 160
- Printed page numbers: 162, 163, 164
- Key entities: Ravana, Sita, Rama, Hanuman, Lakshmana
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** Ravana threatens Sita with a deadline to accept him, and demonesses try to persuade her. Unable to bear their harassment, Sita laments and contemplates suicide but decides her life belongs to Rama.

#### Q1

**Question:** Ravana, angered by Sita's words, threatened: 'O Sita! Within this deadline I have set, change your mind and become mine, or I will kill you.' What was the deadline set by Ravana?

**Options:**
- 1. One month
- 2. Two months
- 3. Three months
- 4. Four months

**Correct answer:** Two months

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sita

#### Q2

**Question:** The demonesses around Sita came to her and said: 'O Sita! Ravana is most excellent and great. Becoming his wife is your fortune. So accept Ravana.' To which lineage did they say Ravana belongs?

**Options:**
- 1. Chandra Vamsa (Lunar dynasty)
- 2. Bhrigu Vamsa (Bhrigu dynasty)
- 3. Pulastya Vamsa (Pulastya dynasty)
- 4. Surya Vamsa (Solar dynasty)

**Correct answer:** Pulastya Vamsa

**Key entities:** Sita, Ravana

#### Q3

**Question:** Unable to bear the harassment of the demonesses who said that the mere human Rama can never reach Lanka surrounded by the ocean, and urged her to accept Ravana as husband and enjoy royal pleasures, Sita got up from there and went under which nearby tree?

**Answer:** Shimshapa tree (where Hanuman was)

**Key entities:** Rama, Lanka, Ravana, Sita, Hanuman

#### Q4

**Question:** Unable to bear the words of the demonesses, how did Janaki Devi lament?

**Answer:** Hearing the harsh words of the demonesses around her, Janaki Devi began to lament. Frightened by their words, the great chaste Sita shed tears and with a choked voice and faltering speech, she said: 'No human woman has ever become the wife of a demon. Kill me as you wish.' Like a fawn caught among wolves in the forest, Sita curled up her body and trembled violently. Distressed by grief, she thought of her husband and worried. The words of those demonesses pierced her like spears. 'Separated from my husband Sri Rama, I am like one who has swallowed deadly poison; it is not good to live any longer. What sin did I commit in a previous birth that this terrible sorrow has befallen me? Under the control of these demonesses, I can never reach Sri Rama again. So it is better for me, immersed in endless grief, to end this life. But my life belongs to my husband Sri Rama; therefore I have no right to abandon it at my will.' Thus Janaki Devi pondered in many ways.

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama

#### Q5

**Question:** In her time of distress, how did Sita decide about her survival?

**Answer:** Janaki Devi, continuously shedding tears and lamenting under the tree, fell to the ground like one demented. 'Alas! When Sri Rama went after the wonderful deer, the demon Ravana, who can assume any form, forcibly abducted me and brought me here while I was crying. Later, these demonesses have kept me under their control and are threatening me cruelly. Immersed in such grief, I have no hope in life. Being the righteous wife of the lord of the universe, Sri Rama, why am I suffering such misery? Has my fortune turned? Death is better than living separated from my great lord. Perhaps those two great men, having set aside their weapons, have taken to the life of ascetics in the forest, eating roots and fruits? Or has the wicked Ravana killed the great heroes Rama and Lakshmana by some deceit? In such a time of hardship, whatever I think, death is my only refuge. But even in this grief, death does not come to me. I am far from Rama, who is a knower of the self and the embodiment of love. I am in the clutches of the sinful Ravana. In this state, there is no other way but to die.' Thus Sita decided.

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Ravana, Lakshmana

### Chapter 64: Sixty-fourth Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 27-31
- Source PDF pages: 160, 161, 162, 163
- Printed page numbers: 164, 165, 166, 167
- Key entities: Sita, Trijata, Rama, Hanuman, Ravana, Dasharatha, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Sampati
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** Sita, tormented by the demonesses, decides to end her life. A demoness named Trijata wakes from a dream and rebukes the others, prophesying the destruction of the rakshasas and victory for Rama. Sita, unable to bear the torture, resolves to hang herself with her braid. Later, she feels hopeful due to auspicious signs. Hanuman, perched on a tree, observes everything and plans to console Sita. He softly narrates Rama's story, revealing his identity and mission, which astonishes Sita.

#### Q1

**Question:** While Sita was speaking about sacrificing her life and some demonesses were threatening her, a demoness who had just woken up rebuked the demonesses and said, 'I had a dream just now. In that dream, destruction for the rakshasas and victory for Sri Rama will occur.' What is the name of that demoness?

**Options:**
- 1. Ajāmukhi
- 2. Śūrpaṇakhā
- 3. Pragḥasa
- 4. Trijatā

**Correct answer:** Trijatā

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Unable to bear the torture inflicted by the demonesses, Sita decided to hang herself with which implement?

**Options:**
- 1. With a rope
- 2. With her own braid
- 3. With the end of her saree
- 4. With a banyan root

**Correct answer:** With her own braid

**Key entities:** Sita

#### Q3

**Question:** Janaki, who was distressed and ready to give up her life, after some time felt that something auspicious was about to happen and her mind became calm. For what reason did she feel that way?

**Answer:** Due to some auspicious omens

**Key entities:** Sita

#### Q4

**Question:** Hanuman, perched on the Ashoka tree and calmly observing everything, how did he begin to think?

**Answer:** Hanuman, calmly observing everything from the tree, fully heard Sita's words, Trijata's dream account, and the words of the demonesses threatening Sita. Then Maruti began to think about Sita. 'To find Sita's whereabouts, millions of vanaras have gone in all directions. The fortune of seeing her has come only to me. Like a spy who thoroughly learns the enemy's strengths while awake, I have moved unnoticed and learned everything. I have fully understood the characteristics of these rakshasas. I have seen the entire city of Lanka. I have understood Ravana's power and his ways. Sita's mind is deeply agitated by intense grief. If I leave without consoling her, my journey will be meaningless. If I try to speak to her, the demonesses are all around. For now, I must be patient and when the demonesses are careless, I should speak to her in simple language like an ordinary human. Already Sita is afraid of Ravana; she might mistake me for Ravana's illusion. So, without being seen by her, I should praise Rama's virtues and make her pleased.' Thinking thus, Maruti, staying among the branches on the tree, looking at Sita, decided to speak sweetly in a low voice that only she could hear, and attempted accordingly.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Trijata, Lanka, Ravana, Rama

#### Q5

**Question:** In a low voice that Sita could hear, how did Hanuman describe the story of Rama?

**Answer:** Maruti, speaking from the tree in a low voice that Sita could hear, said: 'In the Ikshvaku dynasty, there was a great king named Dasharatha. Among his four sons, the eldest is Sri Rama. He is the embodiment of wisdom, foremost among bowmen, protector of dependents, all beings, and all dharmas. He is endowed with immense strength and valor, and is truthful. Obeying the command of his aged father, Sri Rama went to the forests with his wife Sita and his brother Lakshmana. In that great forest, he slew many rakshasas who could change form at will. Hearing this news, the rakshasa Ravana came in anger, deceived Sri Rama through a magical deer, and abducted Sita. Then Sri Rama, searching for Sita, befriended the vanara Sugriva in that forest. By the command of the vanara king Sugriva, thousands of vanaras went in all directions to search for Sita. Among them, I, following the indication of Sampati, crossed the ocean of a hundred yojanas and came here for Sita's sake. I had heard from Rama about Sita's form, beauty, special radiance, and some identifying marks. I have seen here Sita endowed with those auspicious marks.' Hearing these words of Hanuman, Janaki was astonished, remembered Sri Rama, and looking carefully at the tree where she was, saw Hanuman.

**Key entities:** Sita, Hanuman, Rama, Dasharatha, Lakshmana, Ravana, Sugriva, Sampati

### Chapter 65: Sixty-fifth Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 32-36
- Source PDF pages: 163, 164, 165, 166
- Printed page numbers: 167, 168, 169, 170
- Key entities: Hanuman, Sita, Rama, Ravana, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Vali
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** Hanuman, hiding in a tree, is seen by Sita who initially suspects him to be a demon. He descends, reassures her by describing Rama's qualities and showing Rama's signet ring, convincing her of his identity as Rama's messenger.

#### Q1

**Question:** Seeing Maruti hidden among the branches and leaves, Sita, after confirming it was not a dream but reality, and seeing the monkey form praising Rama's virtues, who did Janaki consider him to be?

**Options:**
- 1. A demon capable of changing form
- 2. A disguised form of Ravana
- 3. A partisan of Rama
- 4. A monkey who came to deceive her

**Correct answer:** A partisan of Rama

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Hanuman descended from the Shimshapa tree, bowed to Sita, recognized her as Sita, and asked about her plight. At that time, what happened to the demonesses guarding Janaki?

**Options:**
- 1. They went to Ravana.
- 2. All were sleeping.
- 3. They fled seeing Hanuman.
- 4. All went for food.

**Correct answer:** All were sleeping

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita

#### Q3

**Question:** When Hanuman approached the grief-stricken Sita and spoke, she suspected him to be a magical form of Ravana. How did Hanuman dispel her doubt?

**Answer:** He praised Rama's virtues.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Ravana, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Maruti instill confidence in Sita about himself?

**Answer:** Hanuman narrated Rama's story, describing Rama's beauty and virtues from head to toe, told how he met Rama and Lakshmana, how Sugriva became king after Vali's death, and how he was sent to search for Sita. He assured her he was Rama's messenger.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Vali

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Hanuman give Sita the token sent by Rama to convince her?

**Answer:** Hanuman showed Rama's signet ring, saying it was given by Rama to prove his identity. Sita took the ring, rejoiced, and Hanuman comforted her, saying she would soon see Rama on Mount Prashravana.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Rama

### Chapter 66: Sixty-Sixth Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 37-40
- Source PDF pages: 166, 167, 168, 169
- Printed page numbers: 170, 171, 172, 173
- Key entities: Hanuman, Sita, Rama, Sugriva, Ravana, Lakshmana, Indra, Varuna
- Places: Ayodhya, Lanka

**Summary:** Hanuman offers to carry Sita back to Rama, but Sita refuses, insisting that Rama himself must come to rescue her. She gives Hanuman her chudamani (crest-jewel) as a token for Rama. Sita expresses doubts about how the monkey and bear warriors can cross the ocean. Hanuman reassures her of Rama's might and the strength of Sugriva's army. Sita then sends a message to Rama through Hanuman, urging him to come quickly before the deadline set by Ravana.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Hanuman pleaded with Sita to come with him, what did she reply?

**Options:**
- 1. She remained silent without saying anything
- 2. She said it is better that Rama himself comes and takes me
- 3. She became angry with Hanuman
- 4. She suspected Hanuman to be Ravana's illusion

**Correct answer:** She said it is better that Rama himself comes and takes me

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** When Hanuman pleaded with Sita, 'Mother! If you do not wish to come with me, give me some token that Rama can recognize,' what object did Sita give to Anjaneya to send?

**Options:**
- 1. Necklace
- 2. Her anklets
- 3. Crest-jewel (Chudamani)
- 4. Girdle

**Correct answer:** Crest-jewel (Chudamani)

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** Sita said to Hanuman, 'O monkey hero! I have a doubt about the monkey and bear warriors who are your helpers, and about the princes Rama and Lakshmana.' What doubt did she express to Hanuman?

**Answer:** How will all of you cross the ocean?

**Key entities:** Sita, Hanuman, Rama, Lakshmana

#### Q4

**Question:** Knowing that Hanuman was about to depart to Rama, what topics did Sita discuss with him?

**Answer:** Hanuman told Sita that Rama, accompanied by bear and monkey warriors, would soon come, destroy enemies, and end her sorrow. Sita praised Hanuman's words and suggested he rest in a secret place and leave the next day. She expressed uncertainty whether her life would last until he returned. She said that if Rama defeats Ravana and takes her to Ayodhya, it would bring her glory; if he destroys Lanka with arrows and takes her, it would enhance his valor. Hanuman reassured her that Sugriva, king of the monkeys and friend of Rama, has millions of powerful monkey and bear warriors ready to sacrifice their lives for her. He said Rama of the Raghu dynasty will kill Ravana and take her to Ayodhya. He then prepared to depart.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Rama, Sita, Ravana, Ayodhya, Lanka, Sugriva

#### Q5

**Question:** What message did Sita send to Rama through Hanuman?

**Answer:** Sita told Hanuman: 'O best of monkeys! I am very happy to see you, though I am emaciated with grief. I desire to attain my lord, the great soul. Tell Rama as I say: You who have valor equal to Indra and Varuna, how can you bear that your wife Sita was abducted by Ravana and is spending time among demons? I have preserved this divine crest-jewel; whenever I see it, I rejoice as if seeing you. The sorrows caused by the terrible demonesses are unbearable. I have endured them until now with the hope that you will come and rescue me. If you do not come within the deadline set by Ravana, my life will not remain. Tell my Rama thus. Also ask about the welfare of Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva and others.' Hearing this message, Hanuman felt fulfilled and, thinking about the remaining task, resolved to go north.

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Hanuman, Indra, Varuna, Ravana, Lakshmana, Sugriva

### Chapter 67: Sixty-seventh Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 41-44
- Source PDF pages: 169, 170, 171
- Printed page numbers: 173, 174, 175
- Key entities: Hanuman, Sita, Ravana, Vayu, Rama, Sugriva, Prahasta
- Places: Ashoka Grove, Lanka

**Summary:** Hanuman, after meeting Sita, decides to display his prowess to the demons. He destroys the Ashoka grove, fights and kills many demon warriors sent by Ravana, including Jambumali, and burns the Chaitya palace.

#### Q1

**Question:** After leaving Sita, what did Hanuman intend to do to show his prowess to the demons?

**Options:**
- 1. He went to kill Ravana
- 2. He went to kill those guarding Sita
- 3. He went to destroy the city of Lanka
- 4. He set out to destroy the Ashoka grove

**Correct answer:** He set out to destroy the Ashoka grove

**Key entities:** Sita, Hanuman, Ashoka Grove

#### Q2

**Question:** Seeing the destruction of the Ashoka grove, the demons went to Ravana and reported the matter. Enraged, how many demon warriors did Ravana send against Hanuman?

**Options:**
- 1. Sixty thousand
- 2. Seventy thousand
- 3. Eighty thousand
- 4. Ninety thousand

**Correct answer:** Eighty thousand

**Key entities:** Ashoka Grove, Ravana, Hanuman

#### Q3

**Question:** What did the demon women do upon seeing Hanuman destroying the Ashoka grove and the great monkey hero?

**Answer:** They ran in all directions

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Ashoka Grove

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Hanuman destroy the Chaitya palace?

**Answer:** After killing all the demon warriors sent by Ravana in the Ashoka grove, Maruti saw the nearby Chaitya palace. He jumped onto it to destroy it. The guards of the Chaitya palace surrounded Maruti with weapons, various maces, arrows, spears, swords, and axes. Then the son of the wind god, shouting victory to Sri Rama, angrily uprooted the golden pillars of the palace and whirled them around. The fire that arose from them burned the palace. Then, watching the burning palace, Maruti killed hundreds of demons. All-powerful Hanuman flew into the sky and threatened the demons, saying, 'We roam the entire earth under the command of the monkey king Sugriva. They are all more powerful than me. You have enmity with the great Sri Rama. The countless monkey army following Sugriva will destroy all of you. Neither this city of Lanka nor Ravana will remain under our monkey force.' Thus Hanuman, after destroying the Chaitya palace, threatened the demons there.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Ravana, Ashoka Grove, Vayu, Rama, Sugriva, Lanka

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Anjaneya kill Jambumali?

**Answer:** Jambumali, the son of Prahasta, was very powerful. He had large fangs, wore red garments and flower garlands, held a bow, and came on a chariot yoked with donkeys. Seeing Jambumali approaching, Maruti rejoiced and roared. Then Jambumali twanged his bow and struck Hanuman with a crescent-shaped arrow. Then he struck Hanuman with a barbed arrow and ten more arrows, causing pain. Immediately, Maruti sprang up, uprooted a nearby sal tree, and began to whirl it. Jambumali cut that sal tree into pieces with four arrows. Then Hanuman, in anger, crushed Jambumali and his chariot with the trunk of that sal tree. Learning that the mighty eighty thousand Kinkaras and Jambumali had lost their lives, Ravana's eyes turned red with rage.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Prahasta, Ravana

### Chapter 68: Sixty-eighth Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 45-48
- Source PDF pages: 171, 172, 173
- Printed page numbers: 175, 176, 177
- Key entities: Hanuman, Ravana, Indrajit, Brahma, Sugriva
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** After Hanuman kills Jambumali, Ravana sends his minister's sons, then commanders with fourfold army, and finally his son Akshakumara, all of whom are slain. Ravana then sends Indrajit, who uses the Brahmastra to bind Hanuman, but Hanuman feigns capture to meet Ravana.

#### Q1

**Question:** After killing Jambumali, how many minister's sons did Ravana send against Hanuman?

**Options:**
- 1. Seven
- 2. Eight
- 3. Nine
- 4. Ten

**Correct answer:** Four

**Key entities:** Ravana, Hanuman

#### Q2

**Question:** After learning of the minister's sons' destruction, Ravana, thinking carefully, sent how many commanders with the fourfold army against Hanuman?

**Options:**
- 1. Two
- 2. Three
- 3. Four
- 4. Five

**Correct answer:** The question is: Ravana, looking carefully at the monkey standing before him, ordered whom among his ministers to find out who he was and why he came to golden Lanka?

**Key entities:** Ravana, Hanuman, Lanka

#### Q3

**Question:** After learning that all the commanders with the fourfold army were killed by Hanuman, Ravana sent his son Akshakumara against Hanuman. The chariot Akshakumara rode was obtained as a result of great penance and could travel in the sky. How many horses were yoked to that chariot?

**Answer:** Six

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Ravana

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Maruti kill Akshakumara?

**Answer:** With Ravana's permission, Akshakumara, accompanied by the fourfold army, approached Hanuman who was seated at the entrance of the grove. Immediately, he prepared for battle, strung his bow, and shot three arrows at Maruti. When the three arrows struck him at once, Hanuman looked as if he would burn Akshakumara. Then Akshakumara flew into the sky and pursued Hanuman with his chariot, as Hanuman moved about evading his arrows. Hanuman, moving in various ways to avoid the enemy, destroyed Akshakumara's horses and chariot. Leaving the destroyed chariot, Hanuman caught hold of Akshakumara's two legs as he moved in the sky, whirled him around many times, and dashed him to the ground on the battlefield. From that blow, Akshakumara's hands, legs, and bones were crushed, his body soaked in blood, and he died. Thus killing Akshakumara, Maruti instilled fear in Ravana. Then Hanuman returned to the entrance of the grove and waited for the enemies.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Ravana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the battle between Hanuman and Indrajit take place?

**Answer:** Hearing that Akshakumara was killed by Hanuman, Ravana was inwardly agitated but composed himself. Looking at his son Indrajit, he said, 'O son! You are the foremost among archers. You have acquired many divine weapons including the Brahmastra. I have no confidence in anyone as much as in you. Considering the monkey's excellent intelligence, physical strength, and valor, and also considering your own strength and valor, make timely decisions and go, meditating on the Brahmastra. He will not yield to anything except the Brahmastra.' Having circumambulated and bowed to his father, Indrajit, with his army, mounted his chariot and went to the battlefield. Hanuman, hearing the sound of Indrajit's chariot, was delighted to have to fight a worthy opponent and prepared for battle. As Indrajit twanged his bow and released arrows, Hanuman would swiftly dodge aside like playing hide and seek. Indrajit did not know how to defeat Hanuman, nor did Hanuman know how to defeat Indrajit. Then, determined, Indrajit, intending to kill Hanuman, released the Brahmastra. Hanuman, feeling the effect of the Brahmastra, pretended to be bound. But by the boon of Brahma, the power of that weapon vanished in an instant. However, pretending to be bound, he submitted to the rakshasas, wanting to see Ravana. When the rakshasas bound Maruti with jute ropes, the effect of the Brahmastra completely disappeared. Then the rakshasas brought Hanuman before Ravana. At Ravana's command, the ministers asked Hanuman, 'Who are you?' He replied that he was a messenger sent by Sugriva.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Indrajit, Ravana, Brahma, Sugriva

### Chapter 69: Sixty-ninth Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 49-52
- Source PDF pages: 173, 174, 175, 176
- Printed page numbers: 177, 178, 179, 180
- Key entities: Hanuman, Brahma, Ravana, Sugriva, Rama, Vibhishana, Mahaparshva, Prahasta, Nikumbha, Dasharatha, Lakshmana, Sita, Vali
- Places: Lanka, Ayodhya, Dandaka Forest, Rishyamuka, Ashoka Grove

**Summary:** Hanuman, pretending to be bound by Brahma's weapon, is brought before Ravana. Ravana, surrounded by ministers, questions him. Hanuman reveals he is a messenger of Sugriva and describes Rama's glory. When Ravana orders his execution, Vibhishana intervenes, arguing that killing a messenger is against dharma.

#### Q1

**Question:** When the demons brought Hanuman, who was pretending to be bound by the Brahmastra, and stood him before Ravana, how many ministers surrounded Ravana, who was accompanied by his entire retinue?

**Options:**
- 1. Four
- 2. Five
- 3. Six
- 4. Seven

**Correct answer:** Seven

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Ravana

#### Q2

**Question:** Ravana, carefully observing the monkey standing before him, ordered which of his ministers to find out who he was and why he had come to his golden Lanka?

**Options:**
- 1. Durdhara
- 2. Mahaparshva
- 3. Prahasta
- 4. Nikumbha

**Correct answer:** Mahaparshva

**Key entities:** Ravana, Lanka, Mahaparshva

#### Q3

**Question:** When Prahasta asked Maruti, 'Who are you? Why have you come here?', Hanuman replied that he had come on a royal mission. By whose grace did he say he would not be bound by any weapon?

**Answer:** Brahma

**Key entities:** Prahasta, Hanuman, Brahma

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Maruti describe the glory of Sri Rama in Ravana's court?

**Answer:** In the full court, Hanuman said to Ravana: 'O King! I have come to your city of Lanka with Sugriva's message. Sri Rama is the eldest of the four sons of King Dasharatha of Ayodhya, who possesses a fourfold army. He is long-armed, all-capable, and greatly valiant. Following dharma, he came to Dandaka forest with his brother Lakshmana and wife Sita, as per his father's command. That Sita is a great noble lady. She was abducted in Dandaka forest. Searching for her, Rama and Lakshmana came to Rishyamuka mountain, met Sugriva, and made a pact: Sugriva would search for Sita, and Rama would make Sugriva king of the monkey kingdom. As agreed, Rama killed Vali and made Sugriva king. King Sugriva sent his followers in all directions to search for Sita. I am one of those sent. My name is Hanuman, son of Vayu. Searching for Sita, I easily crossed the hundred-yojana ocean and entered Lanka. While searching for Mother Sita, I found her in the Ashoka grove. Such dangerous deeds, contrary to dharma and causing destruction of lineage, should not be done by wise men like you. Therefore, I speak for your good. Listen to my words, return Sita to Rama, and seek refuge in him. You and your relatives can live for ten ages.' Thus Hanuman described Rama's glory to Ravana.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Rama, Ravana, Lanka, Sugriva, Dasharatha, Ayodhya, Dandaka Forest, Lakshmana, Sita, Rishyamuka, Vali, Ashoka Grove

#### Q5

**Question:** When Ravana ordered Hanuman's execution in the court, who told Ravana that it was not dharma, and in what manner?

**Answer:** Considering the words 'Even Brahma cannot save one whom Rama wishes to kill in battle' as displeasing, Ravana became angry, red-eyed, and ordered, 'Kill this monkey!' Hearing this, Ravana's brother Vibhishana did not agree. Desiring his brother's welfare, he thought well and said, 'O Rakshasa king! Forgive me, give up anger. Listen to my words with compassion. No prince who knows what is proper and improper kills a messenger. This is not the custom of the world. You know dharma and what is appropriate. Therefore, O great king! Do not kill the messenger; punish him appropriately.' Thus spoke Vibhishana. He added, 'Brother! Elders have taught us many ways to punish a messenger, but under no circumstances is killing a messenger dharma. Moreover, if you release him, he will go and bring Rama and Lakshmana here. Then it will be easy to destroy your enemies.' Considering Vibhishana's suggestions as excellent, Ravana sincerely gave up his attempt.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Hanuman, Brahma, Rama, Vibhishana, Lakshmana

### Chapter 70: Seventieth Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 53-56
- Source PDF pages: 176, 177, 178
- Printed page numbers: 180, 181, 182
- Key entities: Ravana, Hanuman, Vibhishana, Sita, Prahasta, Mahaparshva, Sugriva, Rama, Lakshmana, Mainaka
- Places: Lanka, Ayodhya

**Summary:** Ravana orders Hanuman's tail to be set on fire. Hanuman burns Lanka but spares Vibhishana's house. He extinguishes his tail in the sea and worries about Sita's safety. After hearing celestial beings praise the miracle of Sita's protection, he regains confidence and decides to return. He climbs Mount Arishta and leaps across the ocean.

#### Q1

**Question:** Ravana, who refrained from killing the messenger, ordered which part of Hanuman's body to be set on fire?

**Options:**
- 1. Feet
- 2. Hands
- 3. Tail
- 4. Head

**Correct answer:** I saw Lanka

**Key entities:** Ravana, Hanuman, Lanka

#### Q2

**Question:** During the burning of Lanka, whose house did Hanuman leave unburnt?

**Options:**
- 1. Prahasta's
- 2. Mahaparshva's
- 3. Vajradamshtra's
- 4. Vibhishana's

**Correct answer:** The question: All who saw Hanuman, with great joy, asked him: 'Maruti! How did you recognize Sita? How is that virtuous lady?' Who asked Hanuman to tell them information about Sita?

**Key entities:** Lanka, Hanuman, Sita

#### Q3

**Question:** After completely burning Lanka, where did Maruti fully extinguish the fire on his tail?

**Answer:** I saw Ravana

**Key entities:** Lanka, Hanuman, Ravana

#### Q4

**Question:** After extinguishing his tail, about whom and in what manner did Maruti grieve?

**Answer:** After extinguishing the fire on his tail in the sea, Anjaneya began to think about Sita. 'Alas! What a great mistake I made by burning this Lanka! If Lanka is completely burnt, will Sita also be burnt in it? Overcome by anger, I have committed such treachery against my master. The entire city of Lanka has turned to ashes. There is no place that is not burnt. Therefore, Sita must have surely died. If due to my perverse intellect, my action has gone awry and endangered the life of Mother Sita, then it is better for me to give up my life. Otherwise, having completely ruined the mission, how can I show my face to Sugriva, the lord of the monkeys, and to the great men Rama and Lakshmana? It is well known that monkey intellect is unstable. Due to my foolish anger, I have displayed the fickleness natural to monkeys.' Thus the son of Vayu lamented to himself. While he was thinking, 'For the success of Rama's mission, the mountain Mainaka in the ocean came forward, but would fire burn the great virtuous Sita?' the celestial beings traveling in the sky said, 'It is a wonder that even though all of Lanka is burnt, fire did not reach the vicinity where Sita is. This is a miracle.' Hearing these words, Maruti was filled with supreme joy. He decided to see Sita once more and then return.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Lanka, Sugriva, Rama, Lakshmana, Mainaka

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Anjaneya cross the ocean again?

**Answer:** Hanuman prostrated at the feet of Sita, who was sitting in the shade of an Ashoka tree, and said, 'Mother! By divine grace, I have been able to see you safe and without any danger.' Then Sita said to Maruti, 'O virtuous one! How can the countless armies of monkeys and bears, or Rama and Lakshmana, cross this vast ocean? This strong doubt does not leave me. What do you, who are capable of accomplishing the task, think about removing this obstacle? What is your answer to this?' Hanuman replied to Sita, 'Mother Sita! Sugriva is the lord of crores of monkey and bear warriors. The mighty Sugriva, along with Rama and Lakshmana, will come here and destroy the city of Lanka. Sri Rama will soon kill Ravana along with his relatives and friends, and will go to his city Ayodhya with you. Mother! Be comforted, good will come to you. Be patient for a short time. Soon you will see Sri Rama kill Ravana.' Then Hanuman bowed to Sita, and eager to see Sri Rama, he decided to go across the ocean. He climbed a great mountain named 'Arishtagiri' nearby. That Arishtagiri, with a width of ten yojanas and a height of thirty yojanas, sank under the pressure of Hanuman's footsteps. Desiring to cross the salt ocean, Maruti leaped into the sky.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Lanka, Ravana, Ayodhya

### Chapter 71: Seventy-first Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 57-60
- Source PDF pages: 178, 179, 180, 181
- Printed page numbers: 182, 183, 184, 185
- Key entities: Hanuman, Angada, Sita, Jambavan, Sugriva, Rama, Ravana, Nila, Nala, Lakshmana
- Places: Lanka, Ashoka Grove

**Summary:** Hanuman returns from Lanka and meets Angada and the other monkeys. He first tells them that he has seen Sita. Then he describes Sita's pitiable condition in the Ashoka grove, guarded by rakshasis. Angada proposes they go to Lanka and rescue Sita, but Jambavan advises they first report to Sugriva and Rama.

#### Q1

**Question:** After crossing the ocean and reaching the northern shore, when Hanuman met Angada and others, what was the first thing he said to them?

**Options:**
- 1. I have seen Lanka
- 2. I have seen Sita
- 3. I have seen Ravana
- 4. I have burnt Lanka

**Correct answer:** I have seen Sita

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Angada, Sita

#### Q2

**Question:** Who, upon seeing Hanuman, asked him with great joy: 'O Maruti! How did you recognize Sita? How is that virtuous lady? Tell us the news about Sita'?

**Options:**
- 1. Jambavan
- 2. Angada
- 3. Nila
- 4. Nala

**Correct answer:** Jambavan

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Jambavan

#### Q3

**Question:** While telling Angada and others about his search for Sita, at what time did Hanuman say he reached Lanka?

**Answer:** At sunset time

**Key entities:** Angada, Sita, Hanuman, Lanka

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Hanuman describe Sita's pitiable condition to Angada and others?

**Answer:** Hanuman told Angada and others about seeing Sita and her pitiable condition: 'O foremost of monkeys! Sri Rama's effort has succeeded. Sugriva's vow has been fulfilled. My mind is overwhelmed with devotion and reverence for Sita's virtuous influence. In her devotion to her husband, she has no equal. Ravana, the rakshasa king, is powerful with his asceticism. Though he touched her, he did not perish by his own ascetic power. I have learned all the details of Lanka. We can all go together, destroy Lanka, kill the rakshasas, and deliver the virtuous Sita to Sri Rama. In Ravana's Ashoka grove, under the shade of a Shimshapa tree, the great virtuous Sita is in distress. Around her, rakshasa women are guarding. Though she has the beauty of the full moon, she is dim like a moon covered by clouds. Though the arrogant Ravana tormented her, the beautiful and chaste Janaki did not care for him at all. Sita, endowed with auspicious signs, is wholly devoted to Sri Rama in thought, word, and deed. She still wears the same garment she wore on the day she was abducted. Her body is covered with dust and dirt, and she is emaciated with grief and sorrow.' Thus Maruti described Sita's pitiable story to all his companions.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Angada, Rama, Sugriva, Ravana, Lanka, Ashoka Grove

#### Q5

**Question:** After hearing Hanuman's words, how did Angada and Jambavan express their opinions?

**Answer:** Hearing Maruti's words, Angada said: 'O monkey heroes! Even after knowing Sita's whereabouts, it is not proper for us to go to Sri Rama's presence without her. In flying and valor, no one can equal us. My opinion is that we should go to Lanka, conquer the rakshasas, and bring Janaki back.' To Angada, Jambavan replied: 'O wise Angada! Your words do not seem appropriate. Sugriva, the lord of monkeys, and the great Sri Rama sent us to the southern direction to search for Sita, but they did not ask us to bring her back. In any case, taking Sita with us may not please Sri Rama. Sri Rama will bring Sita back by his own valor; he does not depend on others. That lord has vowed in the presence of all monkeys that he will conquer the enemy and bring Sita back. How would he like his vow to be broken? Then all our efforts would be futile. Therefore, let us all go and inform Sugriva and Rama and Lakshmana of what has happened so far.' Thus Jambavan expressed his opinion.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Angada, Jambavan, Sita, Rama, Lanka, Sugriva, Lakshmana

### Chapter 72: Seventy-second Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 61-64
- Source PDF pages: 181, 182, 183
- Printed page numbers: 185, 186, 187
- Key entities: Angada, Hanuman, Jambavan, Sugriva, Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Sushena
- Places: Kishkindha, Dandaka Forest

**Summary:** Angada, Hanuman, and others, following Jambavan's advice, enter the Madhuvana forest on their return journey. They indulge in fruits and honey, causing destruction. The forest guard Dadhimukha reports to Sugriva, who interprets the act as a sign of success in their mission. Sugriva sends Dadhimukha to bring the monkeys. The monkeys arrive at Kishkindha, and Hanuman informs Rama that he has seen Sita, bringing great joy.

#### Q1

**Question:** Angada, Anjaneya and others, heeding Jambavan's advice, intending to see Sugriva, Rama, and Lakshmana, entered which forest on their return journey with joy and shouts?

**Options:**
- 1. Ashoka forest
- 2. Dandaka forest
- 3. Saugandhikavana
- 4. Madhuvana

**Correct answer:** Madhuvana

**Key entities:** Angada, Hanuman, Jambavan, Sugriva, Rama, Lakshmana

#### Q2

**Question:** The forest that Hanuman and others entered was under Sugriva's control, yet unable to bear the troubles caused by those monkeys, who was the forest guard that went to Sugriva?

**Options:**
- 1. Tarudu
- 2. Dadhimukha
- 3. Sushena
- 4. Shatavali

**Correct answer:** Dadhimukha

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sugriva

#### Q3

**Question:** What did Angada and others do after entering Madhuvana?

**Answer:** They drank honey and ate fruits.

**Key entities:** Angada

#### Q4

**Question:** When Dadhimukha reported the news that Hanuman and others had destroyed Madhuvana, what did Sugriva do?

**Answer:** The mighty Dadhimukha came to Sugriva, bowed at his feet, and said that Hanuman and others had destroyed Madhuvana. Then Lakshmana asked why this forest guard had come and why he was grieving. Sugriva said, 'O Lakshmana! Dadhimukha says that the heroes led by Angada, who went to the southern direction in search of Sita, entered Madhuvana, ate fruits, drank honey, and are destroying the forest. This is joyful news, because without success in their mission, they would not engage in such acts. Even though the deadline I set has passed, they have boldly entered Madhuvana and are happily sporting, meaning their mission must have succeeded. Sita must have been seen by them. There is no doubt. The achiever of this task may be Hanuman himself.' Hearing these delightful words from Sugriva, the righteous Rama and Lakshmana were filled with great joy. Then Sugriva ordered Dadhimukha, 'Uncle! What you have told us is good news. So go and quickly send Hanuman and others here. Rama, Lakshmana, and I are very eager to hear the details of the search for Sita from their mouths.'

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sugriva, Lakshmana, Angada, Sita, Rama

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Angada and others, upon arriving at Kishkindha, convey the news of seeing Sita?

**Answer:** Receiving Sugriva's command, Dadhimukha immediately went to Madhuvana and told Angada, 'O prince! Forgive our faults. I went to your uncle Sugriva and told him what happened here. They all rejoiced and ordered me to send all of you quickly to Kishkindha.' Hearing Dadhimukha's words, Angada said to his companions, 'O monkey warriors! After the mission is accomplished, we should not stay here even for a moment. Our fatigue is also relieved. Only going to Sugriva remains.' According to Angada's words, all the monkeys said, 'Alright, let us go that way,' and they flew into the sky, traveled some distance, and came to the place where Sugriva, Rama, and Lakshmana were. They came with the desire to see Rama, placing Angada and Hanuman in front. Seeing their approach, Sugriva rejoiced, thinking they must have accomplished Rama's task. Then the mighty-armed Hanuman prostrated before Rama and said the nectar-like words, 'I have seen Sita.' Hearing from Hanuman's mouth, Rama and Lakshmana were filled with supreme joy. Sugriva, Rama, and Lakshmana, who had faith that Hanuman alone could accomplish the task, looked at Maruti with respect.

**Key entities:** Angada, Kishkindha, Sita, Sugriva, Rama, Lakshmana, Hanuman

### Chapter 73: Seventy-third Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 65-68
- Source PDF pages: 183, 184, 185, 186
- Printed page numbers: 187, 188, 189, 190
- Key entities: Hanuman, Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Janaka, Ravana, Sugriva
- Places: Lanka, Chitrakuta, Ayodhya

**Summary:** Hanuman returns to Rama and Lakshmana, reports that he has seen Sita, and delivers her message and token. He recounts Sita's doubts and his reassurances, and describes the state of Lanka.

#### Q1

**Question:** What object did Hanuman tell Rama that Sita gave him as a token?

**Options:**
- 1. A necklace
- 2. The crest-jewel
- 3. A gem bracelet
- 4. Anklets

**Correct answer:** The crest-jewel

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Rama, Sita

#### Q2

**Question:** While telling Rama about Sita's situation, Hanuman said that she told him she would live for how long?

**Options:**
- 1. One year
- 2. Six months
- 3. Three months
- 4. One month

**Correct answer:** One month

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Hanuman

#### Q3

**Question:** When Rama saw the divine crest-jewel sent by Sita through Hanuman, he pressed it to his heart and recalled who had given it to Sita as a gift?

**Answer:** Her father-in-law, King Janaka

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Hanuman, Janaka

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Hanuman explain Sita's message to Rama?

**Answer:** Hanuman said to the noble Rama: 'Lord! Janaki told me exactly the incident that happened earlier in Chitrakuta to remind you. O Ramachandra! While sleeping happily with you, Janaki woke up first. At that time, a crow injured her chest. Knowing this, you woke up and, chanting a Brahmastra on a blade of darbha grass, released it. Due to the intensity of that astra, the crow wandered through all the worlds and finally sought refuge in you. Though the crow deserved to be killed, you, being compassionate to those who seek refuge, removed the crow's right eye to pacify the Brahmastra. O Rama! Rama and Lakshmana, the best of men, are immensely strong and radiant like fire. They are invincible even to the gods. Why do such great heroes neglect me? Is there any fault on my part?' Saying thus, Vaidehi shed tears and spoke pitiful words. Hearing them, I said, 'Mother Janaki! I swear to you. Rama is grieving for you and is in a state of confusion. Because he is immersed in sorrow, Lakshmana is also distressed. At last, I was able to see you. This is not a time to grieve. Mother! Soon all your troubles will disappear. Rama will kill Ravana and take you to Ayodhya. This is true.' Thus she conveyed her message to you in many ways. Therefore, Lord! Knowing these words I have spoken, believe that she is safe.' Thus Hanuman conveyed Sita's message to Lord Ramachandra.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Rama, Chitrakuta, Lakshmana, Ravana, Ayodhya

#### Q5

**Question:** What words did Hanuman tell Rama that he used to resolve Janaki's doubts in Lanka?

**Answer:** Anjaneya told Rama the words he spoke to resolve Sita's doubts: 'O best of men! Janaki spoke to me saying, 'Maruti! You are fully capable. Setting aside your ability, how will the other vanara and bear warriors, Rama and Lakshmana, cross this great ocean that is impossible to cross? What are you planning for them to cross this great ocean? Tell me. My son! Hanuman! You alone are sufficient to accomplish this task. But if Rama comes with all his forces, kills Ravana in battle, and takes me to Ayodhya as a victor, that would be glorious for both the lord and me. Rama is a great hero. I am a hero's wife. You devise a method so that Rama destroys Lanka with his own arm strength and takes me away.' Thus Janaki spoke to me. O Rama! To her meaningful and logical words, I replied, 'Mother! Sugriva is the lord of the vanara and bear warriors. As soon as he wills, they will all come here. Mother! You will soon see Rama and Lakshmana, who have the prowess of lions, standing at the gates of Lanka.' Thus I gave courage to Sita in many ways. Lord! I consoled my mother Maithili with many words of courage and auspicious words, making her cheerful. Then that mother attained peace in my presence.' Thus Hanuman told Rama how he resolved Sita's doubts.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Rama, Sita, Lanka, Lakshmana, Ravana, Ayodhya, Sugriva

### Chapter 74: Seventy-fourth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 1-4
- Source PDF pages: 186, 187, 188
- Printed page numbers: 190, 191, 192
- Key entities: Rama, Hanuman, Sita, Sugriva, Jambavan, Angada, Ravana, Lakshmana
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** Rama rejoices upon hearing Hanuman's account of meeting Sita. Sugriva advises Rama to channel his distress into anger. Hanuman describes Lanka's defenses in detail. Rama then orders the monkey army to march to the seashore, and they proceed under Sugriva's command.

#### Q1

**Question:** After hearing Hanuman's entire account of seeing Sita, Rama was overjoyed and thrilled. What did Rama give to Hanuman for doing such a great favor?

**Options:**
- 1. Praised him
- 2. Presented a garland
- 3. Gave the joy of an embrace
- 4. Blessed him

**Correct answer:** Gave the joy of an embrace

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Sri Rama, thinking deeply about crossing the ocean, began to suffer. Who first told him that they could build a bridge over the ocean and enter Lanka?

**Options:**
- 1. Sugriva
- 2. Hanuman
- 3. Jambavan
- 4. Angada

**Correct answer:** Sugriva

**Key entities:** Rama, Lanka, Sugriva

#### Q3

**Question:** While Sri Rama was in a state of agitation that spoiled all purposes, what did Sugriva advise him to abandon the agitation and adopt?

**Answer:** Anger (fire of anger)

**Key entities:** Rama, Sugriva

#### Q4

**Question:** At Sri Rama's request, how did Hanuman describe the defense system of Lanka city?

**Answer:** When Sri Rama asked about the defense system of Lanka city, Hanuman said: 'O Lord! All the residents of Lanka are happy and comfortable. That city is filled with mad elephants, countless chariots, and a Rakshasa army. Therefore it is impenetrable to enemies. The city has four gates on four sides, built wide and high. Around them are moats. On the gates are powerful machines that can rain arrows and stones, stopping enemy armies attacking the city. At those gates, many Rakshasa warriors have placed hundreds of catapults made of metal. The rampart around the city is built of gold. In the moats around the rampart, water-dwelling animals like crocodiles roam. O Lord! Ravana is always eager for war. He is always vigilant in overseeing his armies. Attacking Lanka is an impossible task; even the gods cannot enter it. Countless Rakshasa armies guard the gates on all four sides. O Lord! I have filled the bridges over the moats and the moats themselves with stones and bricks. I have leveled most of the ramparts. I destroyed a quarter of the Rakshasa army. I set that Lanka city ablaze. If we can enter Lanka city with our army by some means, victory will be ours. Therefore, O Lord! Being fully prepared, decide on an auspicious moment for our departure and command Sugriva, Angada, and others.' Sri Rama listened attentively to what Hanuman said.

**Key entities:** Rama, Hanuman, Lanka, Ravana, Sugriva, Angada

#### Q5

**Question:** According to Sri Rama's command, how did the monkey army reach the seashore?

**Answer:** After hearing the details of Lanka city from Hanuman, Sri Rama said to Sugriva: 'O best of monkeys! We have heard about Lanka ruled by the wicked Ravana. Let us now destroy it immediately. The sun has reached the middle of the sky. This is the victorious moment. Today is the auspicious Uttara Phalguni nakshatra. This is a suitable day for travel and victory. So it is better to depart now.' Hearing Rama's words, Lakshmana and Sugriva rejoiced, prepared for the journey, appointed suitable leaders for the various army divisions, and Sugriva commanded the monkey army leaders to proceed on the correct path as directed by Rama, avoiding cities and other settlements, passing through places with good tasty fruits and sweet waters. As they proceeded, they saw the Sahyadri mountain. On the way, they saw lakes, ponds, and forests blooming with flowers. Thus, all of them traveled happily, following Rama in the southern direction, and reached the seashore filled with all kinds of aquatic creatures.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lanka, Hanuman, Sugriva, Ravana, Lakshmana

### Chapter 75: Seventy-fifth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 5-8
- Source PDF pages: 188, 189, 190, 191
- Printed page numbers: 192, 193, 194, 195
- Key entities: Rama, Sita, Hanuman, Ravana, Lakshmana, Indrajit, Vibhishana, Kumbhakarna, Mandodari, Prahasta, Nikumbha, Sugriva
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** Rama reaches the seashore with the monkey army and expresses his grief over separation from Sita. In Lanka, after Hanuman's destruction, Ravana holds a council with his ministers and generals, who boast of their strength and vow to destroy Rama and the monkeys.

#### Q1

**Question:** Rama, having reached the seashore with the monkey army, told Lakshmana: 'Brother! What kind of fire, caused by separation from Sita, is burning me completely?'

**Options:**
- 1. Submarine fire
- 2. Fire of separation
- 3. Fire of anger
- 4. Fire of jealousy

**Correct answer:** Fire of separation

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Sita

#### Q2

**Question:** After Hanuman caused destruction in Lanka city, who addressed the demon assembly saying 'What would be good to do?'

**Options:**
- 1. Indrajit
- 2. Vibhishana
- 3. Kumbhakarna
- 4. Ravana

**Correct answer:** Ravana

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Lanka, Ravana

#### Q3

**Question:** Seeing Ravana's valor, which prominent demon gave his daughter Mandodari in marriage to him?

**Answer:** Maya

**Key entities:** Ravana, Mandodari

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Ravana's ministers speak words of courage to him?

**Answer:** After Hanuman destroyed Lanka city, Ravana convened a council with his ministers and addressed them: 'O prominent demons! In such a critical situation, to protect ourselves and our city Lanka, all of you think well and give appropriate suggestions.' Then all of them, one after another, saluted the lord and said: 'Lord! We have immense military strength. Our weaponry is also adequate. In such a state, why are you worried? Have you forgotten the occasions when you defeated Yakshas, Nagas, and Danavas in battle and subjected them to various tortures? Moreover, you have conquered many mighty kings on this earth. Before those kings, this Rama is nothing. For you who conquered such kings, is this Rama any account? O great king! You need not exert yourself. Your mighty son Indrajit alone is enough to destroy the entire monkey army. This Indrajit has performed many sacrifices to please the Supreme Lord and obtained boons unattainable by others. Lord! The strength of Hanuman is far less than the splendor of those we conquered earlier. Do not overestimate him and his prowess. O king! You can certainly kill Rama and achieve victory over them.' Thus Ravana's ministers submitted to him.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Hanuman, Lanka, Rama, Indrajit

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Ravana's army commanders boast before him?

**Answer:** After the ministers spoke words of courage to king Ravana in the assembly, his army commanders Prahasta, Durmukha, Vajradamshtra, Nikumbha, and Vajrahanu, one after another, said: 'O great king! Devas, Danavas, Gandharvas, Pishachas, Nagas, and kings of birds could not do anything to you. What can monkeys do to you? We were complacent thinking there was no enemy threat. Hence Hanuman struck us. Otherwise, that monkey would not have left Lanka alive.' Then another commander said: 'Lord! Entering the inner apartments without our permission and burning Lanka city are all insults to the great king. Therefore, I alone will go and kill all those monkeys.' Then another commander, gnashing his teeth and seizing a terrible club, said: 'Lord! Rama along with Sugriva and Lakshmana is our enemy. I alone will go and destroy them.' Immediately another commander said: 'O great king! Let you and this demon army be as they are. I alone can destroy Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Hanuman, and the entire monkey army.' Then another commander, trembling with anger, said: 'O sovereign of demons! All of you stay calm and happily drink sweet wine. I alone will go and destroy all our enemies Rama and others.' Thus all of Ravana's commanders boasted in various ways.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Prahasta, Nikumbha, Hanuman, Lanka, Rama, Sugriva, Lakshmana

### Chapter 76: Seventy-sixth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 9-12
- Source PDF pages: 191, 192, 193
- Printed page numbers: 195, 196, 197
- Key entities: Vibhishana, Ravana, Rama, Kumbhakarna, Lakshmana, Indrajit, Sita, Indra, Sugriva, Brahma
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** After Vibhishana warns Ravana about Rama's valor, Ravana leaves the assembly and goes to his palace. He then summons his important ministers and friends to a council. Kumbhakarna, awakened from his long sleep, arrives and speaks to Ravana, offering to kill Rama and Lakshmana.

#### Q1

**Question:** After Vibhishana told Ravana about Sri Rama's valor, where did Ravana go after leaving the assembly?

**Options:**
- 1. To the Ashoka garden
- 2. To the anger chamber
- 3. To his own palace
- 4. To Indrajit's palace

**Correct answer:** To his own palace

**Key entities:** Vibhishana, Ravana, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** When Vibhishana, wishing Ravana's welfare, advised him to return Sita to Rama, Ravana said that even if Rama came with whom, he cannot stand before me?

**Options:**
- 1. With Indra and other gods
- 2. With Sugriva and others
- 3. With Brahma and others
- 4. With all the people of the world

**Correct answer:** With Indra and other gods

**Key entities:** Vibhishana, Ravana, Sita, Rama, Indra

#### Q3

**Question:** Thinking that the time had come to consult with his important ministers and friends, where did Ravana go?

**Answer:** To the council chamber

**Key entities:** Ravana

#### Q4

**Question:** In what manner did Ravana summon all his important people?

**Answer:** Ravana, the evil-doer who committed the sinful act of abducting Sita, despite the good advice of Vibhishana and other relatives and friends, rejected their words due to his desire for Sita. He was distressed and weakened, not knowing what to do. War seemed inevitable, and danger was approaching. Therefore, Ravana thought that the time had come to deeply consult with his important ministers and friends. Immediately, he mounted a wonderful chariot and went to the council chamber. Then he ordered the messengers there, 'The time has come to show our strength and capabilities. So, depart at once and bring all the prominent rakshasas in our city.' Immediately, the rakshasa soldiers went throughout the city of Lanka, entered without hesitation into pleasure houses, bed chambers, and gardens, and announced the lord's command to all the prominent rakshasas. Upon hearing the king's order, they all came quickly on their respective chariots, elephants, horses, or on foot. They parked their vehicles at a distance from the palace where the great king resided, entered the palace on foot, and had an audience with Ravana. The king welcomed all who came. Thus, they all waited for the king's command.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sita, Vibhishana, Lanka

#### Q5

**Question:** Among all those assembled in Ravana's court, how did Kumbhakarna converse with Ravana?

**Answer:** Ravana addressed all those who had come to the court: 'O courtiers! It seems war is inevitable. Enchanted by the beauty of Sita, Rama's wife, I abducted her. Keeping these two things in mind, give me advice that will ensure my victory. My brother Kumbhakarna has awakened from sleep and has just arrived at the court. But since Kumbhakarna was immersed in sleep until now, I could not discuss these matters with him.' Hearing the lamentation of the lustful Ravana, Kumbhakarna said angrily: 'O lord! It would have been better if you had consulted us and taken a decision before deceiving Rama and Lakshmana and abducting Sita from their hermitage. O brother! If one performs actions contrary to dharma through improper means, they bring about disasters. The faults of a fickle-minded person who boasts 'I am strong' and acts hastily are noticed by the enemy, who easily strikes him. Because of your thoughtless action, we now have to deliberate. But do not grieve. I will kill them and protect you from that danger. Why should you fear while I am alive? I will kill Rama and Lakshmana and devour the vanaras. With Rama slain by my hand, Sita will be permanently yours.' Thus Kumbhakarna spoke to his elder brother.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Kumbhakarna, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana

### Chapter 77: Seventy-seventh Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 13-16
- Source PDF pages: 193, 194, 195
- Printed page numbers: 197, 198, 199
- Key entities: Ravana, Vibhishana, Indrajit, Rama, Brahma, Indra, Sita, Mahaparshva, Angada
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** In the council hall, Ravana's ministers discuss strategies. Vibhishana advises peace, but Indrajit and Ravana reject his counsel. Ravana insults Vibhishana, who then leaves the assembly with his four ministers and flies to Rama's side.

#### Q1

**Question:** Who cursed that if Ravana forcibly enjoys another's wife, his head will split and he will die?

**Options:**
- 1. Indra
- 2. Punjakasthala
- 3. Sita Devi
- 4. Brahma

**Correct answer:** Brahma

**Key entities:** Ravana, Brahma

#### Q2

**Question:** Observing Ravana's anger, Mahaparshva told his king which of the four upayas (strategies) should we follow?

**Options:**
- 1. Sama (conciliation)
- 2. Dana (gift)
- 3. Bheda (division)
- 4. Danda (punishment)

**Correct answer:** Danda (punishment)

**Key entities:** Ravana, Mahaparshva

#### Q3

**Question:** Who told Ravana's curse story and words that would benefit him?

**Answer:** Angada

**Key entities:** Ravana, Angada

#### Q4

**Question:** In the council hall, how did Indrajit respond to Vibhishana's words?

**Answer:** Indrajit, unwillingly hearing the words of Vibhishana who spoke for Ravana's welfare like a second Brihaspati, said in the council hall: 'O uncle! You speak useless words like a coward. In our Pulastya lineage, no one like you was born before. O coward Vibhishana! What are those mere human princes before us? One ordinary rakshasa among us is enough to kill them. Not only are you afraid, but why do you frighten us? I have deposed Indra, the lord of the three worlds. To a great hero like me, what is a mere human prince?' Hearing this, Vibhishana replied: 'My son! Indrajit! You are still a child. You do not have the ability to decide what is to be done and what is not. By speaking such meaningless words, you will bring destruction to Ravana.' While Vibhishana was thus answering Indrajit, all those present heard.

**Key entities:** Indrajit, Vibhishana, Ravana, Indra

#### Q5

**Question:** Why did Vibhishana leave the council hall?

**Answer:** Not heeding Vibhishana's words spoken for his welfare, Ravana, impelled by death, said harshly: 'O rakshasa! One may live with a deadly venomous serpent, but never with a relative like you who behaves like a friend but has a biased mind. I know well the nature of kinsmen in all worlds. All these relatives rejoice when their kinsmen fall into sorrow. In the world, kinsmen insult those who are superior, efficient, learned, virtuous, and heroic. Moreover, whenever they get an opportunity, they humiliate them. These wicked ones not only do not help but also contemplate treachery. In that way, you, being my kinsman, are trying to harm us in our difficult situation. O Vibhishana! I am honored and respected in all worlds. I am wealthy, born in a noble lineage, and have trampled my enemies. Seeing this greatness, you, my kinsman, are envious. O traitor to your clan! You were born evil in the rakshasa lineage. If anyone else had spoken like this, I would have taken his life. You survive only because you are my brother.' Hearing Ravana's rude words, the righteous Vibhishana thought he should not stay there any longer, took his mace, and flew into the sky. His four ministers also followed him.

**Key entities:** Vibhishana, Ravana

### Chapter 78: Seventy-eighth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 17-20
- Source PDF pages: 195, 196, 197, 198
- Printed page numbers: 199, 200, 201, 202
- Key entities: Vibhishana, Rama, Sugriva, Ravana, Hanuman, Angada, Jambavan, Nala, Nila, Brahma, Kumbhakarna, Indra, Indrajit, Agni, Vali, Sita
- Places: Lanka, Kishkindha

**Summary:** Vibhishana seeks refuge in Rama, and after initial suspicion by Sugriva, Rama accepts him. Vibhishana reveals the strengths of Ravana's forces. Later, Ravana's messenger Shuka comes to Sugriva with a message, but is captured and then released by Rama's order.

#### Q1

**Question:** Who first told Rama that Vibhishana, who came to seek refuge, should not be given shelter, as he is an enemy partisan?

**Options:**
- 1. Hanuman
- 2. Sugriva
- 3. Angada
- 4. Jambavan

**Correct answer:** Sugriva

**Key entities:** Rama, Vibhishana, Sugriva

#### Q2

**Question:** Who informed Rama that Vibhishana is worthy of refuge and trustworthy?

**Options:**
- 1. Jambavan
- 2. Nala
- 3. Nila
- 4. Hanuman

**Correct answer:** Hanuman

**Key entities:** Rama, Vibhishana, Hanuman

#### Q3

**Question:** Quoting the instructive words of which great sage did Rama tell Sugriva that granting refuge to Vibhishana is righteous?

**Answer:** Kandu Maharshi

**Key entities:** Rama, Sugriva, Vibhishana

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Rama learn about the strengths and weaknesses of the demons through Vibhishana, who sought refuge at his feet?
