**Answer:** As soon as Vibhishana learned that Rama had granted him safety, he approached Rama's feet and bowed. Then Rama said, 'Vibhishana! Tell me the strengths and weaknesses of the demons in Lanka.' Then Vibhishana said, 'O prince! Ravana has obtained extraordinary boons from Brahma. By their power, he cannot be slain by any of the gods, Gandharvas, Yakshas, or demons. My elder brother Kumbhakarna is a great warrior, equal to Indra in battle. Ravana's son Indrajit, wearing an impenetrable armor in battle, is a bowman who fights invisibly. He performed a sacrifice, satisfied Agni, and gained immense power. Moreover, O Rama! Ravana's ministers and commanders fight on earth like the guardians of the directions. The countless demon army living in Lanka eats flesh and blood. Some of them are shape-shifters.' Hearing this, Rama said, 'Vibhishana! You have told the truth. I have understood everything. I will sacrifice Ravana and his relatives and friends on the battlefield and make you king of Lanka.' Then Vibhishana bowed his head and saluted Rama.

**Key entities:** Rama, Vibhishana, Lanka, Ravana, Brahma, Kumbhakarna, Indra, Indrajit, Agni

#### Q5

**Question:** As Ravana's messenger, Shuka came to the place where Sugriva and others were. What topics did he discuss?

**Answer:** By Ravana's order, the demon Shuka, being a shape-shifter, took the form of a parrot and reached Rama's army on the far shore of the ocean. Remaining in the sky, he wished to convey Ravana's message to Sugriva. He said, 'O king of monkeys! You are the brother of the mighty Vali. Therefore you are like a brother to our great king. So abandon Rama's side and join my side. What benefit will you get by fighting on Rama's side? It is true that I abducted Sita, Rama's wife. But what loss is that to you? Think. You are a monkey. He is a human. There is no relationship between you two. So go back to Kishkindha. Even if you all try, crossing the ocean and reaching Lanka is impossible.' As Shuka spoke, some monkey warriors flew into the sky, caught the demon Shuka, brought him down, and began to punch him and pluck the feathers of the parrot-formed Shuka. Then the demon Shuka, frightened, sought refuge in Rama, saying, 'Lord! Protect me. Killing a messenger is not righteous.' Then Rama, showing compassion, ordered them to release him. They obeyed Rama's command and did so.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sugriva, Rama, Vali, Sita, Kishkindha, Lanka

### Chapter 79: Seventy-ninth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 21-24
- Source PDF pages: 198, 199, 200
- Printed page numbers: 202, 203, 204
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Garuda, Angada, Nila, Jambavan, Sushena, Sugriva
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** Rama, having reached the ocean with his army, lies on a bed of darbha grass for three days to propitiate the ocean god. Angered by the ocean's lack of response, Rama prepares to use the Brahmastra, which prompts the ocean to appear and advise him to build a bridge. Rama then describes ominous portents to Lakshmana and arranges his army in the Garuda formation for the attack on Lanka.

#### Q1

**Question:** To propitiate the ocean and reach Lanka with his army, on which bed did Sri Rama lie for three days after taking a vow?

**Options:**
- 1. On a bed of darbha grass
- 2. On a bed of grass
- 3. On a bed of leaves
- 4. On a stone platform

**Correct answer:** On a bed of darbha grass

**Key entities:** Lanka, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Knowing the power of which weapon that Rama, enraged at the ocean, was about to discharge, did the ocean become propitiated?

**Options:**
- 1. Varunastra
- 2. Agnayastra
- 3. Brahmastra
- 4. Aindrastra

**Correct answer:** Brahmastra

**Key entities:** Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** By what means did the ocean tell Sri Rama that he could cross the ocean and go to Lanka?

**Answer:** By building a bridge

**Key entities:** Rama, Lanka

#### Q4

**Question:** What kind of ominous portents did Sri Rama describe to Lakshmana that he saw?

**Answer:** Rama, having built a bridge over the ocean and reached Lanka with all his people, set up camp there. He told Lakshmana: 'Brother! This place, with abundant cool waters and full of fruit trees, is very favorable for our army. From here, let us proceed with proper battle strategy. I think that based on the portents we see, a terrible fearful situation may arise. Especially for the prominent rakshasas, this will be the cause of destruction. Meanwhile, I feel that danger also lurks for our vanara and bear warriors. Suddenly, winds mixed with dust particles and polluted are blowing. The earth is trembling. Mountains are also slightly shaking. Clouds are roaring harshly, causing fear. The twilight time is extremely terrifying, as if smeared with red sandalwood. Cruel animals and birds, with dejected faces, looking towards the sun, are screaming cruelly. All this is an indication of a fearful situation.' Thus Sri Rama told his brother that they should immediately be ready to attack Lanka city.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Lanka

#### Q5

**Question:** Following military strategy, how did Sri Rama divide his army?

**Answer:** Following military strategy, Sri Rama divided his army and commanded thus: 'Let the valiant Angada, along with Nila, stand at the chest part of the army. Let the foremost of vanaras, Rishabha, with his troops, be on the right flank. Let the mighty Gandhamadana be on the left flank of the army. I and Lakshmana, with our forces, will be at the head of the army, alert. Let Jambavan, Sushena, and Vegadarshi, the vanara and bear warriors skilled in warfare, stand at the belly part of the army and protect it. Let Sugriva, the lord of vanaras, be at the rear of the army and protect it.' Then, following the Garuda formation, that army, well divided and protected by prominent vanara and bear warriors, appeared like the sky covered with clouds. The warriors in that vanara army, eager to crush the enemies on the battlefield, holding mountain peaks and great trees, besieged Lanka. They were all firmly determined to grind Lanka to dust.

**Key entities:** Rama, Angada, Nila, Lakshmana, Jambavan, Sushena, Sugriva, Garuda, Lanka

### Chapter 80: Eightieth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 25-29
- Source PDF pages: 200, 201, 202
- Printed page numbers: 204, 205, 206
- Key entities: Rama, Ravana, Hanuman, Lakshmana, Vibhishana, Sugriva, Prahasta, Nikumbha, Jambavan
- Places: Lanka, Ashoka Grove

**Summary:** Rama and his army reach Lanka. Ravana sends spies Shuka and Sarana to assess the enemy forces. They report back, and Ravana goes to his palace roof to view the army. Shuka describes the vanara warriors, including Hanuman, Rama, Lakshmana, Vibhishana, and Sugriva. Ravana rebukes Shuka and Sarana for praising the enemy, but spares them due to past services.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Sri Rama reached Lanka with his army, whom did Ravana send to ascertain the strengths and weaknesses of the enemy army?

**Options:**
- 1. Prahasta
- 2. Vajradamshtra
- 3. Nikumbha
- 4. Shuka and Sarana

**Correct answer:** Shuka and Sarana

**Key entities:** Rama, Lanka, Ravana

#### Q2

**Question:** After hearing the words of his returning messengers, Ravana, desiring to see Rama's army along with Shuka and Sarana, where did he go?

**Options:**
- 1. On a mountain peak
- 2. Onto his palace
- 3. Outside the city of Lanka
- 4. Into the Ashoka grove

**Correct answer:** Onto his palace

**Key entities:** Ravana, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** While showing Rama's army, Sarana among Shuka and Sarana, while telling Ravana about the bear warriors, especially praised whom?

**Answer:** Jambavan

**Key entities:** Rama, Ravana, Jambavan

#### Q4

**Question:** While informing Ravana about the vanara army, in what manner did Shuka describe the strength and valor of Hanuman and others?

**Answer:** While Ravana was viewing the vanara army from his palace, Shuka, having gone in a disguised form and gathered information, told the rakshasa lord: 'O lord! Look at the great warriors on the enemy side. They are as mighty as mad elephants. They can fight like gods in battle. Therefore, it is impossible to face them. All these are followers of Sugriva. They are born from the aspects of gods and gandharvas. Behold, O lord! The two youths standing there are Mainda and Dvivida. They have divine forms. O king! After careful inquiry, I have learned that there is no one superior to Hanuman in strength, physique, or eloquence. He is intent on destroying the city of Lanka without anyone's help. O lord! Near Hanuman, the great hero of dark complexion is Sri Rama himself. He never transgresses dharma. He is skilled in the use and withdrawal of the Brahmastra. He is learned in the Vedas. On his right side is his brother Lakshmana. He is like Rama's right arm. On his left side is your brother Vibhishana. Between Vibhishana and Sri Rama stands Sugriva. All of them are eager and enthusiastic to fight against Lanka.' Thus Shuka informed his lord Ravana.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Hanuman, Sugriva, Lanka, Rama, Lakshmana, Vibhishana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Ravana rebuke Shuka and Sarana?

**Answer:** After hearing what Shuka and Sarana said, Ravana saw the vanara army chiefs and Rama etc. facing Lanka and felt a little fear in his heart. He became angry because Shuka and Sarana praised the enemies and rebuked them. They bowed their heads in fear and stood with folded hands. 'O Shuka and Sarana! A king is capable of restraint and favor. Ministers or anyone else who are recipients of his grace should not speak words displeasing to him. Is it proper for you to praise the enemy party that is coming to fight against us? You know the principles of statecraft. Yet you speak thus; it is due to your ignorance. That I rule the kingdom with such foolish ministers is my greatness. A king is capable of restraint and favor. I am now letting you go without punishment because your past services have cooled my anger.' Thus Ravana spoke, and Shuka and Sarana, ashamed, bowed their heads and said 'Victory to Ravana' and left from there.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Rama, Lanka

### Chapter 81: Eighty-first Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 30-34
- Source PDF pages: 202, 203, 204
- Printed page numbers: 206, 207, 208
- Key entities: Ravana, Rama, Sita, Vibhishana, Indrajit, Prahasta, Lakshmana, Hanuman
- Places: Ayodhya

**Summary:** After Shuka and Sarana, Ravana sends spies to learn about Rama's forces. He orders Vidyujjihva to create a magical head of Rama to deceive Sita. When Ravana shows the head to Sita, a doorkeeper announces someone's arrival. Sarama, Vibhishana's wife, consoles Sita and later reports Ravana's secret plans.

#### Q1

**Question:** After Shuka and Sarana, whom did Ravana send as spies to learn about Sri Rama's forces?

**Options:**
- 1. Vajradamshtra
- 2. Indrajit
- 3. Shardula and others
- 4. Prahasta

**Correct answer:** Vidyujjihva

**Key entities:** Ravana, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** To frighten and deceive Sita, whom did Ravana order to create the head of Sri Rama?

**Options:**
- 1. Vidyujjihva
- 2. Shardula
- 3. Prahasta
- 4. Akshakumara

**Correct answer:** Indrajit

**Key entities:** Sita, Ravana, Rama, Indrajit

#### Q3

**Question:** When Ravana showed the magical head of Sri Rama to Sita and asked her to surrender, who did the doorkeeper announce had come to see him?

**Answer:** Prahasta

**Key entities:** Ravana, Rama, Sita, Prahasta

#### Q4

**Question:** Who consoled Sita when she was grieving after seeing the magical head of Sri Rama, and how?

**Answer:** Sarama, the wife of Vibhishana, a kind rakshasi among those appointed by Ravana to guard Sita, came to Sita and consoled her. She said, 'Mother Sita! Calm down and be courageous. I heard Ravana's words while hiding behind a tree. The head shown to you is Ravana's illusion. Sri Rama has crossed the sea with the monkey army and is protected by powerful monkeys, Vibhishana, and Lakshmana. No one can even look at Rama. If Ravana had truly killed Rama, why would he prepare for war? Soon you will hear good news.'

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Vibhishana, Ravana, Lakshmana

#### Q5

**Question:** At Sita's request, what details did Sarama reveal to Janaki?

**Answer:** Sarama went to Ravana's court, hid behind a pillar, and overheard his secret discussions. She then told Sita: 'Vaidehi! Ravana's mother Kaikesi and the aged minister Aviddha advised Ravana to return you to Rama, citing Rama's prowess and Hanuman's feats. But greedy Ravana refuses to release you. Only when Ravana falls in battle to Rama's arrows will Rama safely take you to Ayodhya.'

**Key entities:** Sita, Ravana, Rama, Hanuman, Ayodhya

### Chapter 82: Eighty-second Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 35-39
- Source PDF pages: 204, 205, 206
- Printed page numbers: 208, 209, 210
- Key entities: Ravana, Rama, Vibhishana, Prahasta, Indrajit, Nila, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Indra
- Places: Lanka, Kailasa

**Summary:** Ravana, seated in court with his ministers, is advised by his relative Malyavan to make peace with Rama. Ignoring this advice, Ravana prepares for war and assigns guards to the gates. Meanwhile, Rama, following Vibhishana's counsel, lays siege to Lanka and stations forces at the eastern gate. The army spends the night on Suvela mountain, and from there they observe the beauty of Lanka.

#### Q1

**Question:** O king! When Ravana was seated in court with his ministers, who among Ravana's close relatives advised him that making peace with the mighty Rama would be better?

**Options:**
- 1. Prahasta
- 2. Malyavan
- 3. Indrajit
- 4. Vajradamshtra

**Correct answer:** Malyavan

**Key entities:** Ravana, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Disregarding whose words, spoken for his welfare, did Ravana prepare for war and first appoint whom for protection at the eastern gate?

**Options:**
- 1. Vidyujjihva
- 2. Indrajit
- 3. Prahasta
- 4. Malyavan

**Correct answer:** Prahasta

**Key entities:** Ravana, Prahasta

#### Q3

**Question:** According to Vibhishana's advice, whom did Rama tell to stand at the eastern gate and confront those there, in order to besiege Lanka?

**Answer:** Nila

**Key entities:** Vibhishana, Rama, Lanka, Nila

#### Q4

**Question:** On the night when Rama made battle plans to conquer Lanka, where and how did they all spend the night?

**Answer:** To conquer Lanka, Rama decided who should confront at which gate, and told Vibhishana that the vanaras are shape-shifters, but during battle they should not assume human forms. In the war, the vanara forces alone would be our mark to identify our side. During battle, only I, Lakshmana, you my friend, and your four followers—seven of us in total—will remain in human form. Then Rama, along with Sugriva, Vibhishana, Lakshmana, and all his followers, said: 'Friends! Let us all go to this beautiful Suvela mountain, which is full of various minerals like red ochre. Let us all ascend this mountain and spend the night there.' Thus Rama and his followers went to Suvela mountain and spent the night comfortably.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lanka, Vibhishana, Lakshmana, Sugriva

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Rama and others view Lanka from Suvela mountain?

**Answer:** The entire vanara army with Rama spent the night comfortably on Suvela mountain. Afterwards, they all enjoyed the beauties of Lanka city on Trikuta mountain. They saw its gardens, groves, and level grounds without hills or valleys. The many beautiful places between Trikuta and Suvela mountains, with various trees, flowering trees, divine trees, and creepers entwined around them, and flowers blooming on the treetops, were delightful to see. Seeing Lanka shining like Indra's Amaravati, they were all amazed. The royal palace in Lanka, built with a thousand pillars, touching the sky like the peak of Kailasa, was an ornament to the city. That Lanka city, with wonderful forests, was the abode of various-shaped rakshasas. The greatly radiant Rama, along with his followers, viewed that Ravana's Lanka city, abounding in all wealth like grains and riches, and was amazed.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lanka, Indra, Kailasa, Ravana

### Chapter 83: Eighty-third Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 40-44
- Source PDF pages: 206, 207, 208
- Printed page numbers: 210, 211, 212
- Key entities: Ravana, Sugriva, Rama, Angada, Indrajit, Lakshmana, Jambavan, Vibhishana, Brahma
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** The battle between the vanaras and rakshasas begins. Ravana and Sugriva fight, and Sugriva retreats after Ravana uses a magical weapon. Rama besieges Lanka and sends Angada as an envoy to Ravana. Ravana observes the siege from his palace. The initial daytime battle is fierce, with both sides using various weapons. At night, the battle continues; Indrajit uses the Nagastra to bind Rama and Lakshmana, causing them to fall unconscious.

#### Q1

**Question:** In the battle between Ravana and Sugriva, which weapon did Ravana use that made Sugriva retreat?

**Options:**
- 1. Brahmastra
- 2. Varunastra
- 3. Maya Shakti
- 4. Agneyastra

**Correct answer:** Maya Shakti

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sugriva

#### Q2

**Question:** After besieging Lanka on all sides, whom did Sri Rama send as an envoy to Ravana according to war policy?

**Options:**
- 1. Jambavan
- 2. Angada
- 3. Sugriva
- 4. Vibhishana

**Correct answer:** Angada

**Key entities:** Lanka, Rama, Ravana, Angada

#### Q3

**Question:** When Ravana learned from his soldiers that Sri Rama had besieged Lanka on all sides, where did he go to observe the scene?

**Answer:** From atop his palace

**Key entities:** Ravana, Rama, Lanka

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the initial battle between the vanaras and rakshasas take place?

**Answer:** The vanara and rakshasa warriors engaged in a fierce battle. Both sides were filled with rage. The cruel rakshasas, desiring victory for Ravana, shouted battle cries that shook the directions, adorned with gold ornaments, horses, elephants, chariots, banners, and armor. The vast vanara army, eager for victory, rushed towards the shape-shifting rakshasas. Then a duel broke out between the vanaras and rakshasas. Each warrior fought with a suitable opponent. The rakshasas used their weapons, while the vanaras fought with sharp nails, teeth, and trees. In this duel, like the battle between devas and danavas, the rakshasas bit the dust from the blows of the vanaras. In that terrible battle, swords, maces, spears, iron clubs, and axes fell on the battlefield. Broken chariots, dead horses, elephants, and the corpses of vanaras and rakshasas, along with chariot wheels, axles, and poles, were scattered everywhere. Jackals gathered in packs to devour the corpses. After sunset, the rakshasas waited for that time, hoping their strength would increase.

**Key entities:** Ravana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the night battle between the vanara and rakshasa warriors take place?

**Answer:** While the vanaras and rakshasas were fighting, the sun set and darkness enveloped them. Yet the battle did not stop; both sides were determined to win. In the darkness, the rakshasas attacked the vanaras, killing and devouring them. The vanaras, not yielding, tore the rakshasas with their teeth and agitated them with fury. Then Rama and Lakshmana killed both visible and invisible rakshasas with their arrows. In that terrible battlefield, rivers of blood flowed horribly. The cries of severely wounded rakshasas and the lamentations of blood-soaked vanaras were heard dreadfully. Angada, seeking to kill his rival Indrajit, performed heroic feats on the battlefield. Indrajit was wounded by his attack; his chariot and horses died, and his charioteer fell. Then Indrajit, helpless, abandoned his chariot and disappeared. Rama and Lakshmana praised Angada's battle skill. Defeated by Angada, Indrajit, using the boon from Brahma, fought invisibly with the art of disappearing. In anger, Indrajit released the Nagastra on Rama and Lakshmana. Due to that, their bodies were wounded, bound by the Nagastra, and they fell unconscious. The leading vanaras saw Rama and Lakshmana in that state. Thus the night's battle took place.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Angada, Indrajit, Brahma

### Chapter 84: Eighty-fourth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 45-49
- Source PDF pages: 208, 209, 210, 211
- Printed page numbers: 212, 213, 214, 215
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Indrajit, Sugriva, Vibhishana, Ravana, Sita, Trijata, Angada, Jambavan, Hanuman, Prahasta, Mandodari
- Places: Lanka, Kishkindha, Ashoka Grove

**Summary:** Rama and Lakshmana are bound by the Nagastra (serpent weapon) of Indrajit. Sugriva is terrified, but Vibhishana consoles him. Indrajit returns to Lanka and boasts to Ravana that he has killed Rama and Lakshmana. Ravana orders demonesses to show Sita the bound brothers, causing her immense grief. The demoness Trijata consoles Sita, assuring her that Rama and Lakshmana are alive. Rama regains consciousness and, seeing Lakshmana wounded, laments and tells Sugriva to return to Kishkindha, but the monkeys weep. Vibhishana arrives with a mace.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Sugriva was afraid seeing Rama and Lakshmana bound by the Nagastra, who consoled him?

**Options:**
- 1. Angada
- 2. Jambavan
- 3. Hanuman
- 4. Vibhishana

**Correct answer:** Vibhishana

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Rama, Lakshmana, Vibhishana

#### Q2

**Question:** When Indrajit, overjoyed that Rama and Lakshmana were killed by him, reached Lanka, to whom did he first tell this?

**Options:**
- 1. Prahasta
- 2. Ravana
- 3. Vajradamshtra
- 4. Mandodari

**Correct answer:** Ravana

**Key entities:** Indrajit, Rama, Lakshmana, Lanka, Ravana

#### Q3

**Question:** When demonesses showed Sita the Nagastra-bound Rama and Lakshmana by Ravana's order, who consoled her who was suffering from endless grief?

**Answer:** Trijata

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Ravana, Trijata

#### Q4

**Question:** Who among the demonesses guarding Sita consoled her when she saw Rama and Lakshmana bound by the Nagastra? In what way did she console her?

**Answer:** In the battlefield, by Ravana's order, demonesses took Sita on the Pushpaka Vimana and showed her Rama and Lakshmana bound by the Nagastra. Seeing that sight, Sita, thinking Rama and Lakshmana had died, began to lament endlessly. Then Trijata, one of the demonesses guarding her, consoled Sita, saying, 'Devi! You need not grieve. Your husband is alive. Both Rama and Lakshmana are alive. Otherwise, O Vaidehi, this divine vimana would not have brought a woman who has lost her husband. Devi! Moreover, based on my dream, it is impossible for Rama and Lakshmana to have died. So stop grieving and thinking wildly.' Hearing these nectar-like words of Trijata, Sita folded her hands in gratitude and said, 'Trijata! May your words come true!' Then the distressed Janaki, along with Trijata and other demonesses, reached Ashoka Vana in the Pushpaka Vimana. Thereafter, she thought only of Rama and Lakshmana and fell into deep sorrow.

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Ravana, Trijata, Ashoka Grove

#### Q5

**Question:** After regaining consciousness, what did Sri Rama, who was bound by the Nagastra, think?

**Answer:** Rama and Lakshmana, bound by terrible serpent nooses, were sighing. Sugriva and other foremost monkeys surrounded them, grieving. Though bound by serpent nooses, the greatly valiant Sri Rama, being courageous, strong, and of firm bodily strength, regained consciousness after some time and opened his eyes. Then he saw Lakshmana, wounded and bleeding. Seeing him, Sri Rama thought, 'Alas! Lakshmana, who is my life's life, has been defeated in battle and lies on the ground. While I am alive, I have to see my brother in this state! For whom should I live? What is Sita to me now? Why should I live? My desire to live is waning. It is better to give up my body here. Because of me, he has come to this state.' Thinking thus, Sri Rama called Sugriva and said, 'O best of monkeys! Sugriva! I will give up my life. When I am gone, Ravana, considering you weak, will drive you away. So you should immediately return to Kishkindha from here. You and your followers risked your lives and fought for me. I am pleased with that. Sugriva! No human can overcome destiny. You have done all that you had to do for me. All these monkey warriors, out of affection for me, have fought wonderfully until now. Now you may go to your respective places as you wish.' Hearing Sri Rama's words, all the monkeys shed tears from their eyes red with grief. Then Vibhishana, mace in hand, came there and saw Sri Rama.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Sita, Ravana, Kishkindha, Vibhishana

### Chapter 85: Eighty-fifth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 50-54
- Source PDF pages: 211, 212, 213
- Printed page numbers: 215, 216, 217
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Garuda, Ravana, Hanuman, Angada, Jambavan, Vibhishana, Indrajit, Nikumbha, Sugriva
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** After Rama and Lakshmana are freed from the Nagastra bonds by Garuda, Ravana sends demon warriors to battle. Dhumraksha is killed by Hanuman, then Vajradamstra is sent and is slain by Angada after a fierce fight.

#### Q1

**Question:** Who is the reason for Rama and Lakshmana being freed from the Nagastra bonds?

**Options:**
- 1. Jambavan
- 2. Hanuman
- 3. Vibhishana
- 4. Garuda

**Correct answer:** Garuda

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Garuda

#### Q2

**Question:** After learning that Rama and Lakshmana, freed from the Nagastra bonds, became more radiant than before, whom did Ravana first send to the battlefield?

**Options:**
- 1. Indrajit
- 2. Dhumraksha
- 3. Nikumbha
- 4. Prajangha

**Correct answer:** Dhumraksha

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Ravana

#### Q3

**Question:** By whose hand did the demon Dhumraksha die?

**Answer:** Hanuman

**Key entities:** Hanuman

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Angada confront Vajradamstra who came to the battlefield?

**Answer:** Learning that Dhumraksha had fallen in battle, Ravana summoned the mighty, heroic, and magical Vajradamstra and said, 'O hero! Go to the battlefield with a sufficient demon army and destroy Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, and other vanara warriors,' and sent him to the battlefield. Foot soldiers carrying various weapons like sticks, small spears, strange tridents, pestles, lances, nooses, axes, swords, discs, maces, and large axes followed their commander Vajradamstra and came to the southern gate where Angada was stationed. At that time, some ill omens appeared to the demons. But ignoring them, they all advanced with battle enthusiasm. A fierce battle began between the terrifying and courageous vanara warriors and the demon warriors. The battle was so fierce that the battlefield was filled with broken chariots, fallen horses, strangely lying banners, and the corpses of vanaras and demons. The ground was soaked with the blood of fallen heroes. The battlefield, with the cries of warriors, resembled an autumn night. Angada, with his unparalleled valor, terrified the demon forces.

**Key entities:** Angada, Ravana, Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the slaying of Vajradamstra take place?

**Answer:** The mighty Vajradamstra was skilled in archery. Immediately he strung his bow and rained arrows on the vanara army. The heroic demon warriors also continued fighting with various weapons. The best among the vanaras, holding huge rocks, fought from all sides. At that time, the demon warriors hurled thousands of weapons at the monkey warriors. The vanara warriors also attacked the demons with tree branches and stones. All bodies were covered with streams of blood. There, vanaras and demons fell unable to bear the blows of battle. Vultures, eagles, crows, and jackals gathered in flocks to eat the corpses. Seeing all this, Vajradamstra's anger burst forth, and he shot sharp arrows at the vanaras. Then the invincible and valiant Angada picked up a tree and hurled it at Vajradamstra. Vajradamstra cut the approaching tree with his arrows. Seeing that, Angada picked up a huge rock and threw it at Vajradamstra. To avoid the oncoming rock, the demon jumped down from his chariot holding a mace. The chariot was destroyed by the rock. Then Angada threw another stone. Hit by it, Vajradamstra lost consciousness. After a while, the demon recovered and came at Angada, engaging in fistfight. In that fight, they kicked each other with knees, and both fell to the ground exhausted. Quickly recovering, Angada snatched the sword from Vajradamstra's hand and struck the demon's head, splitting it in two. Thus Vajradamstra died at the hands of Angada.

**Key entities:** Angada

### Chapter 86: Eighty-sixth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 55-59
- Source PDF pages: 213, 214, 215, 216
- Printed page numbers: 217, 218, 219, 220
- Key entities: Angada, Ravana, Prahasta, Hanuman, Nila, Sugriva, Lakshmana, Rama, Indrajit, Kumbhakarna, Vibhishana, Jambavan, Tara
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** After Vajradamshtra is killed by Angada, Ravana sends Prahasta to lead the demon army. Hanuman kills Akampana, and then the demons advance under Prahasta. Prahasta is confronted by the vanara Nila, who kills him with a boulder. Ravana then enters the battlefield, fights with Sugriva, Lakshmana, and Hanuman, and finally engages Rama. Rama, seeing Ravana exhausted, tells him to return to the city and come back the next day.

#### Q1

**Question:** After Vajradamshtra was killed by Angada, under whose leadership did Ravana lead the demon army?

**Options:**
- 1. Prahasta
- 2. Akampana
- 3. Dhumraksha
- 4. Indrajit

**Correct answer:** Prahasta

**Key entities:** Angada, Ravana, Prahasta

#### Q2

**Question:** After Akampana was killed by Hanuman, under whose leadership did the demon warriors enter the battlefield?

**Options:**
- 1. Vajradamshtra
- 2. Ravana
- 3. Prahasta
- 4. Kumbhakarna

**Correct answer:** Prahasta

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Prahasta

#### Q3

**Question:** Who stopped Ravana's commander Prahasta on the battlefield?

**Answer:** Nila

**Key entities:** Ravana, Prahasta, Nila

#### Q4

**Question:** How and by whom was the demon commander Prahasta killed?

**Answer:** Seeing Prahasta arrive on the battlefield, Sri Rama smiled and asked Vibhishana, 'O mighty-armed one! Who is this coming with a great army and in anger?' Vibhishana replied, 'Lord! This is Prahasta, the commander-in-chief of all the armies of Ravana, the lord of Lanka. He is immensely strong and valorous.' While he was speaking, Prahasta roared and advanced towards the vanara army. The demon army came bearing various weapons. Seeing the demon army approaching, the vanara army also stood ready, holding trees, branches, and large boulders. A fierce battle began between the two sides. Many demon warriors killed vanara warriors. The prominent vanaras, using trees and huge boulders, crushed the demons all over the battlefield. Then Prahasta's ministers—Narantaka, Kumbhahanu, Mahanada, and Samunnata—four demon warriors, began killing vanaras. Seeing this, the vanara warriors Dvivida, Jambavan, Tara, and Durmukha came and killed those four demon warriors. Enraged, Prahasta, from his chariot, killed vanara warriors with a shower of arrows. Seeing this, the vanara warrior Nila confronted Prahasta. Uprooting a nearby maddi tree, Nila destroyed Prahasta's chariot, horses, and charioteer. Then Nila forcefully snatched the bow from Prahasta's hand and broke it into pieces. Prahasta jumped to the ground. As Prahasta rushed towards him, Nila killed him by smashing his head with a large boulder. Thus Prahasta died at the hands of Nila.

**Key entities:** Prahasta, Rama, Vibhishana, Ravana, Jambavan, Tara, Nila

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the first battle between Rama and Ravana take place?

**Answer:** Learning that Prahasta, the commander-in-chief of the demons, had been killed by the vanara warrior Nila, Ravana mounted a chariot yoked with excellent horses and went to the battlefield. He sent back some of the prominent demons who were following him to guard the city. Sugriva hurled a mountain peak at Ravana as he approached the vanara army. Ravana avoided it with his arrows. Then, in anger, Ravana shot an arrow that struck Sugriva, who lost consciousness and fell on the battlefield. The vanara warriors then sought refuge in Sri Rama. Immediately, Rama took up his bow and started forth, but Lakshmana said he would go and finish Ravana. With Rama's permission, Lakshmana fought with Ravana for a while, but lost consciousness when struck by Ravana's Shakti weapon. Then Hanuman, enraged, rushed at Ravana. The son of the wind clenched his fist and struck Ravana on the chest, causing Ravana to lose consciousness. At that time, Hanuman picked up the unconscious Lakshmana and brought him to Sri Rama. Then Rama mounted Hanuman's shoulders and went to battle. After fighting with Ravana for some time, Rama saw that Ravana was very tired and his energy was diminished. Rama said, 'Ravana! You are very tired now. Therefore, go back to the city and return tomorrow. Then you will know how great my strength is.' Ravana, following Sri Rama's words, stopped the battle and went to the city.

**Key entities:** Rama, Ravana, Prahasta, Nila, Sugriva, Lakshmana, Hanuman

### Chapter 87: Eighty-seventh Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 60-64
- Source PDF pages: 216, 217, 218
- Printed page numbers: 220, 221, 222
- Key entities: Ravana, Rama, Prahasta, Kumbhakarna, Mahodara, Sita, Lakshmana, Vibhishana, Indrajit, Trishira, Hanuman, Sugriva, Jambavan
- Places: Lanka, Ashoka Grove

**Summary:** Ravana, recalling his humiliation by Rama and the death of Prahasta, considers whom to send next into battle. Kumbhakarna is awakened and after a conversation with Ravana, prepares for war. Mahodara proposes a deceptive plan to trick Sita into believing Rama and Lakshmana are dead.

#### Q1

**Question:** Recalling his humiliation at the hands of Sri Rama and the death of Prahasta, whom did Ravana think of introducing next into the battle?

**Options:**
- 1. Indrajit
- 2. Kumbhakarna
- 3. Trishira
- 4. Mahodara

**Correct answer:** Vibhishana

**Key entities:** Rama, Prahasta, Ravana, Vibhishana

#### Q2

**Question:** Seeing Kumbhakarna's entry into battle, whom did Sri Rama ask about his story?

**Options:**
- 1. Anjaneya
- 2. Sugriva
- 3. Vibhishana
- 4. Jambavan

**Correct answer:** The question is: Seeing the form and roars of Kumbhakarna who entered the battlefield, who stopped the frightened fleeing vanaras with conciliatory words?

**Key entities:** Kumbhakarna, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** When Kumbhakarna, awakened with great difficulty, asked his elder brother Ravana 'From whom do you have fear?', whose name did Ravana mention?

**Answer:** Sri Rama

**Key entities:** Kumbhakarna, Ravana, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** Before entering the battlefield, how did Kumbhakarna converse with his elder brother Ravana?

**Answer:** Having awakened from a long sleep, Kumbhakarna entered Ravana's inner palace and said laughingly, 'O King! Earlier, some of us pointed out the flaw in your decision and spoke for your good, but you turned a deaf ear. This war is the result of that; the fruit of your sin has come to you quickly. O great king! Before abducting Sita, you should have considered the pros and cons of this act. But due to your pride in your strength, you could not think about it. However strong and proud one may be, one should think about the consequences of the action one is about to perform. When one does not do so, one must suffer the result.' Having spoken thus, Ravana said to Kumbhakarna, 'O Kumbhakarna! There is no use thinking about the past now. Think about what needs to be done now. Tell me what would be beneficial for us now. What is done is done. Correct my mistake with your ability.' Then Kumbhakarna said to Ravana, 'O great king! You do not wish to return Sita to Rama as our brother Vibhishana advised. Therefore, be carefree now. Give up your anger and steady your mind. As long as there is life in my body, you need not worry. It is about Sri Rama that you are thinking. I will surely kill him. Now in the battlefield, I will display valor against the enemy, kill Sri Rama, and bring his head from the battlefield. Seeing that, you will rejoice.' Thus Kumbhakarna prepared for battle.

**Key entities:** Kumbhakarna, Ravana, Sita, Rama, Vibhishana

#### Q5

**Question:** What kind of deceptive plan did Mahodara reveal to Ravana?

**Answer:** After Kumbhakarna said 'I alone will go and kill Rama', Mahodara, who was present there, said to Ravana, 'O lord! I will tell you a stratagem that I know, better than conquering Rama in battle. If it seems best to you, follow it. O great king! You brought Sita here because you desired her. If you desire, she will come under your control. My plan is this: I, Kumbhakarna, Vidvijjihva, Samhradi, and Vitardhana – we five will go to the battlefield to kill Rama. If we conquer Rama, no stratagem is needed. If Rama conquers us, then we, struck by Rama's arrows and with blood-smeared bodies, will fall at your feet and say that we have killed and devoured Rama and Lakshmana. Then you should proclaim in the city of Lanka that Rama and Lakshmana have died in the battlefield. This news will spread throughout Lanka and also reach Sita. Thereafter, you may enter the Ashoka grove and, with conciliatory words, tempt Sita and win her over. Upon learning this, Rama will stop the war. You will no longer need to fight. Therefore, O great king! I have told you the plan that occurred to me. If you think it will bring you benefit, you may try it.' Thus Mahodara revealed his plan to Ravana.

**Key entities:** Mahodara, Ravana, Kumbhakarna, Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Lanka, Ashoka Grove

### Chapter 88: Eighty-eighth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 65-70
- Source PDF pages: 218, 219, 220, 221
- Printed page numbers: 222, 223, 224, 225
- Key entities: Kumbhakarna, Ravana, Rama, Vibhishana, Sugriva, Hanuman, Angada, Nila, Trishira, Atikaya, Indra, Mahodara, Mahaparshva, Brahma
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** Kumbhakarna, with Ravana's permission, goes to the battlefield and boasts about whom he will kill first. The monkeys flee in fear upon seeing Kumbhakarna, but are stopped by someone. Kumbhakarna is eventually slain. Ravana laments upon hearing the news, and his sons and brothers go to battle, where they are killed by various monkey warriors.

#### Q1

**Question:** With Ravana's permission, going to the battlefield, Kumbhakarna told the demon army accompanying him whom he would kill first?

**Options:**
- 1. Vibhishana
- 2. Sugriva
- 3. Sri Rama
- 4. Hanuman

**Correct answer:** Sri Rama

**Key entities:** Ravana, Kumbhakarna, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Who stopped the monkeys fleeing in fear upon seeing Kumbhakarna's form and roars on the battlefield with conciliatory words?

**Options:**
- 1. Sri Rama
- 2. Nila
- 3. Vibhishana
- 4. Angada

**Correct answer:** Angada

**Key entities:** Kumbhakarna, Angada

#### Q3

**Question:** Who killed Kumbhakarna, who was valiantly roaming the battlefield and terrifying the monkeys?

**Answer:** Sri Rama

**Key entities:** Kumbhakarna, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Ravana lament upon hearing the news of Kumbhakarna's death?

**Answer:** Upon hearing the news of Kumbhakarna's death at the hands of Sri Rama, Ravana fell into boundless grief and lost consciousness. His sons Devantaka, Narantaka, Trishira, and Atikaya also mourned for a while. Ravana cried out, 'Alas, Kumbhakarna! You were immensely strong, having killed many enemies. You left me alone before helping me in my time of need. Brother! You were like my right arm. As long as you were my support, I feared neither gods nor demons. Now that you have fallen, I am as good as dead. You, a great hero, did not fear even Indra's thunderbolt. How were you killed by Rama? All the sages and gods will rejoice at your fall. Brother Kumbhakarna! I ignored Vibhishana's good advice due to my stubbornness, and now I see the result.' Thus Ravana lamented in various ways, falling to the ground.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Kumbhakarna, Rama, Trishira, Atikaya, Indra, Vibhishana

#### Q5

**Question:** How were Ravana's sons Trishira, Devantaka, Mahodara, and Mahaparshva killed in battle, and by whom?

**Answer:** Seeing Ravana grieving, his four sons consoled him, saying, 'O king, our uncle's death is fate. You should not lament. You are capable of ruling the three worlds. With Brahma's boon, you are endowed with various weapons. You can easily conquer Rama. With your permission, we will go to war.' Ravana, somewhat comforted, blessed them and sent his brothers Mahaparshva and Mahodara with them. Driven by fate, the six great warriors—Ravana's sons Trishira, Devantaka, Narantaka, Atikaya, and his brothers Mahaparshva and Mahodara—went to the battlefield. They were skilled in aerial combat and magic. In battle, they fought appropriate monkey warriors. Narantaka was killed by Angada's fist. Devantaka's head was crushed by Hanuman's fist. Mahodara was struck by a rock thrown by Nila and fell dead. Hanuman seized Trishira's sword and cut off his head. Mahaparshva was felled by the monkey chief Rishabha. Thus, Ravana's sons and brothers were killed by the monkey chiefs.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Trishira, Mahodara, Mahaparshva, Brahma, Rama, Atikaya, Angada, Hanuman, Nila

### Chapter 89: Eighty-ninth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 71-75
- Source PDF pages: 221, 222, 223
- Printed page numbers: 225, 226, 227
- Key entities: Ravana, Rama, Indrajit, Lakshmana, Hanuman, Sugriva, Kumbha, Nikumbha, Atikaya, Kumbhakarna, Narayana, Brahma, Shiva, Indra, Jambavan, Vibhishana
- Places: Lanka, Kailasa

**Summary:** Ravana mourns his fallen sons and brothers, realizing Rama is no ordinary being. Indrajit uses the Brahmastra to render Rama and Lakshmana unconscious, but Hanuman brings the Sanjivani mountain with healing herbs to revive them. Sugriva then orders the vanaras to set Lanka on fire, and Ravana sends Kumbha, Nikumbha, and other rakshasas to counterattack.

#### Q1

**Question:** By which weapon, launched by Lakshmana, did Ravana's son Atikaya fall to the ground?

**Options:**
- 1. Brahmastra
- 2. Varunastra
- 3. Agnayastra
- 4. Pashupatastra

**Correct answer:** Brahmastra

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Ravana, Atikaya

#### Q2

**Question:** Unable to bear that his sons and brothers like Kumbhakarna had become sacrifices on the battlefield, Ravana thought Rama was not ordinary. As whose incarnation did he consider Rama?

**Options:**
- 1. As Brahma
- 2. As Parama Shiva
- 3. As Indra
- 4. As Sriman Narayana

**Correct answer:** As Sriman Narayana

**Key entities:** Kumbhakarna, Ravana, Rama, Narayana

#### Q3

**Question:** While Ravana was grieving thinking of all his people becoming sacrifices on the battlefield, who consoled him and, as Indrajit went to the battlefield, which animals did he yoke to his chariot?

**Answer:** High-bred donkeys

**Key entities:** Ravana, Indrajit

#### Q4

**Question:** Why did Rama and Lakshmana lose consciousness? In what manner did Hanuman bring the Sanjivani mountain?

**Answer:** Indrajit, who had received boons from Brahma, remained invisible and attacked from the sky, injuring all the prominent vanaras. Then he released the Brahmastra on Rama and Lakshmana. Seeing this, Rama told Lakshmana, 'Brother, this rakshasa hero has released the Brahmastra on us. Its power is unimaginable. So let us lie down as if we have withdrawn from battle,' and they did so. Seeing this, Indrajit rejoiced that Rama, Lakshmana, and all the vanara heroes had fallen on the battlefield, went to Lanka city, and told his father everything, rejoicing. Then on the battlefield, Jambavan summoned Hanuman with Vibhishana and said, 'Maruti! This is the time for you to exert yourself. Go immediately across the ocean to the Himalayan region, near a place called Vrishabha Hill, in the mountain region called Kailasa Hill, and bring the four herbs named Mritasanjivani, Vishalyakarani, Sandhanakarani, and Savarnyakarani, and return quickly.' Thus he sent Hanuman. According to Jambavan's words, Maruti saw Kailasa Hill in the Himalayan region. But unable to identify the herbs, he lifted that herb mountain and descended among the vanara army. As soon as the fragrance of those herbs touched them, all the vanaras who were barely alive, along with Rama and Lakshmana, rose as if from sleep and became radiant.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Hanuman, Indrajit, Brahma, Lanka, Jambavan, Vibhishana, Kailasa

#### Q5

**Question:** With the vanara army invigorated by the Sanjivani herbs, how did Sugriva besiege Lanka?

**Answer:** Sugriva informed Rama of the events that had happened and what was to come, and told Hanuman, 'Maruti! Kumbhakarna, Ravana's sons, and relatives have died; that rakshasa king is dejected and will not come to battle now. Therefore, let our vanara warriors take torches and burn Lanka!' According to Sugriva's command, the prominent vanaras took torches and set fire to Lanka's gates, royal palaces, and rakshasa houses during the first watch of that night. The fire consumed the lofty mansions, priceless objects, and wealth and grains there. Then Ravana sent Kumbha and Nikumbha, sons of Kumbhakarna, to battle, along with Yupaksha, Shonitaksha, Prajangha, and Kampana as their companions, and sent them to the battlefield to conquer the vanaras. All of them, accompanied by the rakshasa army, went to the battlefield and continued a fierce battle with the vanara heroes.

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Lanka, Rama, Hanuman, Kumbhakarna, Ravana, Kumbha, Nikumbha

### Chapter 90: Ninety-ninth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 76-81
- Source PDF pages: 223, 224, 225
- Printed page numbers: 227, 228, 229
- Key entities: Kumbha, Nikumbha, Sugriva, Hanuman, Ravana, Indrajit, Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Angada, Nila, Jambavan, Khara
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** After the burning of Lanka, battles continue. Kumbha and Nikumbha are killed by Sugriva and Hanuman respectively. Ravana sends Indrajit to the battlefield. Indrajit performs a sacrifice to gain invisibility, then attacks Rama and Lakshmana with arrows. He creates a magical Sita and beheads her in front of Hanuman, causing grief.

#### Q1

**Question:** After the vanara warriors set Lanka ablaze on Sugriva's orders, in the ensuing battle, by whom was the prominent rakshasa named Kampana killed?

**Options:**
- 1. Hanuman
- 2. Mainda
- 3. Dvivida
- 4. Angada

**Correct answer:** Angada

**Key entities:** Lanka, Sugriva, Angada

#### Q2

**Question:** Seeing his brother Kumbha killed by Sugriva, Nikumbha raged and fought. By whom was Nikumbha killed?

**Options:**
- 1. Sugriva
- 2. Nila
- 3. Hanuman
- 4. Jambavan

**Correct answer:** Hanuman

**Key entities:** Kumbha, Sugriva, Nikumbha, Hanuman

#### Q3

**Question:** Hearing the news that Kumbha and Nikumbha were slain on the battlefield, whom did Ravana send to the battlefield?

**Answer:** Indrajit

**Key entities:** Kumbha, Nikumbha, Ravana, Indrajit

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Sri Rama slay Makaraksha?

**Answer:** Makaraksha, son of Khara, came to the battlefield with a rakshasa army and attacked the vanara army. He wounded many vanara warriors with his arrows, causing them to flee in confusion. Seeing the vanaras scattered, Sri Rama stopped the rakshasas with his arrows. Unable to withstand Rama's assault, the rakshasas halted. Enraged, Makaraksha challenged Rama, boasting that he would kill him. Rama replied that victory is not achieved by boasting but by prowess in battle. Makaraksha then shot arrows at Rama, but Rama shattered them. After a brief duel, Rama destroyed Makaraksha's bow, charioteer, and chariot. Makaraksha, standing on the ground, hurled a trident at Rama. Rama cut it into three pieces with three arrows and then felled Makaraksha with the Agneyastra. The vanaras rejoiced.

**Key entities:** Rama, Khara

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Indrajit, obedient to his father's command, display his magical tactics after going to the battlefield?

**Answer:** Hearing that Makaraksha was slain, Ravana sent Indrajit to the battlefield. Indrajit went to a sacrificial ground, kindled a fire, offered a black goat as oblation, propitiated the gods, and gained the power of invisibility. Then mounting a chariot equipped with all weapons, he went to the battlefield. Becoming invisible, he rained a torrent of arrows from the sky, wounding Rama and Lakshmana. Rama and Lakshmana shot divine arrows, but they had no effect on Indrajit. Many prominent vanaras fell to Indrajit's arrows. Lakshmana then suggested using the Brahmastra, but Rama said that would destroy the entire rakshasa race, so they should use other weapons to kill only Indrajit. Meanwhile, Indrajit created a magical Sita, brought her before Hanuman, grabbed her hair, and beheaded her with a sharp sword. Seeing this, Hanuman grieved, thinking that Indrajit had killed the real Sita.

**Key entities:** Indrajit, Ravana, Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Hanuman

### Chapter 91: Ninety-first Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 82-87
- Source PDF pages: 225, 226, 227, 228
- Printed page numbers: 229, 230, 231, 232
- Key entities: Indrajit, Sita, Hanuman, Vibhishana, Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Jambavan, Ravana
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** Indrajit creates a magical illusion of Sita and kills her in front of Hanuman, causing grief. He then goes to perform the Nikumbila homa. Vibhishana consoles Rama, revealing the illusion, and urges Lakshmana to go with him to stop Indrajit's ritual. Lakshmana, accompanied by Vibhishana and the monkey army, confronts Indrajit's forces. Indrajit abandons his homa and engages in battle. A dispute arises between Indrajit and Vibhishana about loyalty and dharma.

#### Q1

**Question:** After showing Hanuman and others that he killed Sita through his magical power, which homa did Indrajit go to perform?

**Options:**
- 1. Vishvajit sacrifice
- 2. Ashvamedha
- 3. Ishti homa
- 4. Nikumbila homa

**Correct answer:** Nikumbila homa

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Indrajit

#### Q2

**Question:** When Maruti told Rama that Indrajit had killed Sita in front of him, and Rama was grieving in various ways, who consoled Rama?

**Options:**
- 1. Lakshmana
- 2. Sugriva
- 3. Jambavan
- 4. Hanuman

**Correct answer:** Vibhishana

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Rama, Indrajit, Sita, Vibhishana

#### Q3

**Question:** Who told Rama that what Indrajit killed was not the real Sita but a Maya Sita?

**Answer:** Vibhishana

**Key entities:** Rama, Indrajit, Sita, Vibhishana

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Vibhishana inspire Lakshmana with war enthusiasm to kill Indrajit?

**Answer:** When Rama was immersed in grief upon hearing from Maruti that Indrajit had killed Sita, Vibhishana came to Rama and said, 'Lord! Indrajit killing Sita is not true. It is merely an illusion. Having plunged us into sorrow, Indrajit has gone to perform the Nikumbila homa. If Indrajit completes the Nikumbila homa, he will become invincible. Therefore, send Lakshmana with me now to kill him. Lakshmana will surely slay him.' Hearing Vibhishana's words, Rama was pleased and turning to Lakshmana said, 'Lakshmana! Take Sugriva, some more monkey forces, bear forces, and also Jambavan, follow Vibhishana, and conquer that deceitful Indrajit. Vibhishana knows all the ins and outs of that area. He will accompany you with his ministers.' Following his elder brother's command, Lakshmana, together with Vibhishana, holding his excellent bow, wearing armor, and wielding a sword, bowed to Rama's feet and said, 'Brother! May the arrows I release today tear apart that son of Ravana!' Then, following Vibhishana, he went and saw Indrajit's forces.

**Key entities:** Vibhishana, Lakshmana, Indrajit, Rama, Hanuman, Sita, Sugriva, Jambavan, Ravana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the battle between Lakshmana and Indrajit take place? Describe the dispute between Indrajit and Vibhishana.

**Answer:** Following Vibhishana, Lakshmana reached the Nikumbila chaitya. Vibhishana said, 'O younger brother of Rama! Without destroying this visible rakshasa army, Indrajit, who is performing the abhicara homa, will not come out. So first, we must scatter this rakshasa army.' Immediately, Lakshmana rained arrows on the rakshasa army. Taking trees and mountain peaks, the monkey army fiercely confronted the rakshasa army. Then the rakshasa army, with weapons in their hands, faced the monkey and bear warriors. Seeing his army scattered and frightened by the onslaught of the monkey warriors, Indrajit stopped the abhicara homa, mounted his chariot, and prepared for battle. Then Hanuman uprooted a great tree and hurled it at the rakshasas. Noticing that Indrajit was determined to kill Hanuman, Vibhishana informed Lakshmana. Lakshmana came forward to confront Indrajit. Seeing this, Indrajit said to Vibhishana, 'O rakshasa! You were born and raised on this land. You are the real brother of my father. You are my uncle. Having such a relationship, you are committing such treachery against me. O evil-minded one! You have forgotten that you belong to the Pulastya lineage.' To these words of Indrajit, Vibhishana replied, 'O son of Ravana! It is true that I was born in the cruel rakshasa clan as you say. But I do not relish unrighteous deeds. However, just because a younger brother's nature is opposed to his elder, can the elder drive the younger out of his house? For this reason, I have had to behave in this manner.' Thus Vibhishana answered Indrajit.

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Indrajit, Vibhishana, Rama, Hanuman, Ravana

### Chapter 92: Ninety-second Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 88-93
- Source PDF pages: 228, 229, 230
- Printed page numbers: 232, 233, 234
- Key entities: Lakshmana, Indrajit, Hanuman, Ravana, Sita, Sugriva, Vibhishana, Jambavan, Rama
- Places: Lanka, Ashoka Grove

**Summary:** Lakshmana and Indrajit engage in a fierce battle. Indrajit fights from a chariot while Lakshmana fights from Hanuman's shoulders. After a prolonged fight, Lakshmana kills Indrajit with the Aindra astra. Ravana, upon hearing the news, loses consciousness and in grief decides to kill Sita, but is dissuaded by his minister Suparshva.

#### Q1

**Question:** While a fierce battle was raging between Lakshmana and Indrajit, Indrajit was riding a chariot. Where was Lakshmana fighting from?

**Options:**
- 1. Standing on the ground
- 2. From Hanuman's shoulders
- 3. From Sugriva's shoulders
- 4. From a chariot

**Correct answer:** From Hanuman's shoulders

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Indrajit, Hanuman

#### Q2

**Question:** During the fierce battle between Indrajit and Lakshmana, both were wounded and exhausted. Who came forward to help Lakshmana?

**Options:**
- 1. Sugriva
- 2. Vibhishana
- 3. Hanuman
- 4. Jambavan

**Correct answer:** Vibhishana

**Key entities:** Indrajit, Lakshmana, Vibhishana

#### Q3

**Question:** All of Ravana's forces were destroyed. Only Indrajit remained. Who encouraged the Vanara army saying that victory would be theirs if they killed him?

**Answer:** Vibhishana

**Key entities:** Ravana, Indrajit, Vibhishana

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Lakshmana kill Indrajit?

**Answer:** The great warriors Lakshmana and Indrajit fought on the battlefield, raining arrows on each other. During the fierce combat, it was impossible to tell who was striking whom. Then Lakshmana severely struck the four horses yoked to Indrajit's chariot with arrows. Next, the younger brother of Rama cut off the head of the demon charioteer with a very powerful arrow. Then Indrajit himself drove the chariot and continued fighting. Then, with overflowing enthusiasm, four Vanara warriors named Pramadi, Sharabha, Rabhasa, and Gandhamadana killed Indrajit's horses. Left with no choice, Indrajit fought from the ground. Both Lakshmana and Indrajit, skilled archers, sought to kill each other. At that time, Indrajit told the demons, 'I will go to Lanka now and return with another chariot. Until then, fight with courage.' Indrajit went to Lanka and returned on another chariot. Thus arriving, Indrajit confronted Lakshmana and Vibhishana. In his battle fury, Indrajit shot arrows at his uncle Vibhishana and tormented him. Vibhishana, with the mace in his hand, struck and killed Indrajit's chariot horses and charioteer. Then Indrajit descended to the ground and fought a most terrible battle with Lakshmana. In that combat, where both warriors used various missiles and weapons, finally Lakshmana killed Indrajit with the Aindra astra.

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Indrajit, Rama, Lanka, Vibhishana

#### Q5

**Question:** After Indrajit's death, what did Rama and Ravana do?

**Answer:** Lakshmana, wounded and covered with blood, along with Vibhishana, Hanuman and others, approached his elder brother and humbly informed him of Indrajit's death. Then Vibhishana told Rama that it was Lakshmana who had cut off Indrajit's head. Rama was greatly pleased, praised Lakshmana, and rejoiced that they had conquered the demons. Meanwhile, in Lanka, Ravana's ministers heard the news of Indrajit's death, went to the battlefield, saw the lifeless Indrajit, and wept for a long time. Then they informed Ravana of Indrajit's death. Hearing the news, Ravana lost consciousness. Grieving for his son, Ravana thought that it would be better to kill Sita. Immediately, ignoring the pleas of his well-wishers, Ravana, sword in hand, went to the Ashoka grove. Then Suparshva, the wisest of Ravana's ministers, said, 'O king! It is not good for a valiant man like you to kill a woman. Direct your anger at Rama on the battlefield. If you defeat him, Sita will surely come under your control.' With many conciliatory words, he made Ravana desist from his attempt to kill Sita.

**Key entities:** Indrajit, Rama, Ravana, Lakshmana, Vibhishana, Hanuman, Lanka, Sita, Ashoka Grove

### Chapter 93: Ninety-third Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 94-99
- Source PDF pages: 230, 231, 232, 233
- Printed page numbers: 234, 235, 236, 237
- Key entities: Ravana, Indrajit, Rama, Surpanakha, Sugriva, Virupaksha, Mahodara, Angada, Mahaparshva, Hanuman, Indra, Vishvamitra, Dasharatha, Sita, Khara, Sushena, Jambavan, Vali
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** Ravana, grieving Indrajit's death, sends all his warriors to battle. Rama defeats them all by evening and mentions that only he and one other possess divine astra power. The demon women lament the destruction of their army, blaming Surpanakha. Ravana then proceeds to the battlefield. Sugriva kills Virupaksha and Mahodara. Angada kills Mahaparshva.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Ravana, grief-stricken upon hearing of Indrajit's death, sent all the demon warriors with him to the battlefield saying 'Go and kill Rama', on that day Rama performed heroic feats and felled all the demons by evening. Then Rama told Hanuman and others, 'This divine astra power belongs to me and only one other.' Who is that other person Rama mentioned?

**Options:**
- 1. Parashiva
- 2. Deva Indra
- 3. Vishvamitra
- 4. Dasharatha

**Correct answer:** Parashiva

**Key entities:** Ravana, Indrajit, Rama, Hanuman

#### Q2

**Question:** Knowing that all the four-fold army sent by Ravana had died at Rama's hands, the demon women lamented and pondered who was the root cause of all this?

**Options:**
- 1. Sita Devi
- 2. Khara
- 3. Surpanakha
- 4. Ravana

**Correct answer:** Surpanakha

**Key entities:** Ravana, Rama, Surpanakha

#### Q3

**Question:** While the demon women were lamenting that all their men had fallen on the battlefield, who set out for the battlefield?

**Answer:** Ravana

**Key entities:** Ravana

#### Q4

**Question:** By whom and in what manner did Virupaksha and Mahodara die?

**Answer:** When Ravana set out for the battlefield, all the remaining demon warriors in Lanka followed him. Among them were Virupaksha, Mahodara, and Mahaparshva. On the battlefield, due to Ravana's heroic feats, some vanaras lost their heads, some had their chests broken, and others had their limbs severed. Seeing this, Sugriva entrusted the protection of the army camp to Sushena and resolved to fight Ravana, picking up a great tree. Seeing this, the demon Virupaksha descended from his chariot, mounted an elephant, and roaring fearsomely, shot arrows at Sugriva. Sugriva was wounded by those arrows. Quickly recovering, Sugriva roared in anger, picked up a great tree, and struck with it. The elephant Virupaksha was riding collapsed. Immediately, Virupaksha took a sword and shield and advanced on Sugriva. In the ensuing close combat, Sugriva's blow caused Virupaksha to fall to the ground with a blood-soaked body, blood flowing from his nine orifices like streams, and he died. Seeing Virupaksha fall, Ravana sent Mahodara against Sugriva. Mahodara also fought with Sugriva for a while and finally had his head severed by Sugriva and died.

**Key entities:** Virupaksha, Mahodara, Ravana, Lanka, Mahaparshva, Sugriva, Sushena

#### Q5

**Question:** By whom and in what manner did Mahaparshva die?

**Answer:** Seeing Mahodara and Virupaksha die at Sugriva's hands, the extremely powerful Mahaparshva, his eyes red with anger, began to torment Angada and his army, who were with the fearsome vanara army, with his arrows. Due to the force of that night-ranger's arrows, the heads of prominent vanaras in the vanara army began to fall. Seeing his forces thus diminishing, Angada picked up an iron mace lying nearby and struck Mahaparshva severely. That blow caused the demon, along with his charioteer, to lose consciousness and fall from the chariot to the ground. Then Jambavan and Gavaksha picked up large boulders and destroyed Mahaparshva's chariot horses and chariot. Then Mahaparshva regained consciousness and struck Angada with arrows. Next, Angada picked up a parigha weapon and hurled it at Mahaparshva. Due to the blow of that parigha weapon, Mahaparshva's bow and arrows and helmet fell to the ground. Then Mahaparshva hurled a large axe at Angada. That son of Vali dodged the blow and with his fist, which was like a thunderbolt, broke Mahaparshva's chest and killed him. Thus Mahaparshva died at Angada's hands.

**Key entities:** Mahaparshva, Mahodara, Virupaksha, Sugriva, Angada, Jambavan, Vali

### Chapter 94: Ninety-fourth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 100-106
- Source PDF pages: 233, 234, 235
- Printed page numbers: 237, 238, 239
- Key entities: Ravana, Rama, Lakshmana, Hanuman, Indra
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** Ravana, after his forces are destroyed, comes to fight Rama. He first uses the Tamasastra against the monkeys. During the battle, Ravana strikes Lakshmana unconscious with a Shakti weapon. Lakshmana is revived by Hanuman with Sanjivini herb. Indra sends his chariot and weapons to aid Rama. Ravana's charioteer briefly diverts the chariot, citing tired horses and Ravana's need for rest.

#### Q1

**Question:** When all his men perished on the battlefield, Ravana came to fight Rama. Which astra did he first use against the monkeys?

**Options:**
- 1. Tamasastra
- 2. Agnayastra
- 3. Varunastra
- 4. Brahmastra

**Correct answer:** Tamasastra

**Key entities:** Ravana, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** In the Rama-Ravana battle, with which weapon did Ravana strike Lakshmana unconscious?

**Options:**
- 1. Modaki weapon
- 2. Musala weapon
- 3. Tamasastra
- 4. Shakti weapon

**Correct answer:** Shakti weapon

**Key entities:** Rama, Ravana, Lakshmana

#### Q3

**Question:** How did Lakshmana, who lost consciousness due to Ravana's weapon, regain consciousness?

**Answer:** Through the Sanjivini herb brought by Hanuman

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Ravana, Hanuman

#### Q4

**Question:** When the battle between Rama and Ravana became intense, how did Indra help Rama?

**Answer:** During the fierce battle, Rama fought from the ground while Ravana fought from a golden chariot. Then Indra, lord of the gods, ordered his charioteer Matali to take his chariot and give it to Rama. Matali brought the chariot before Rama, bowed, and said, 'Rama, Indra has sent this chariot for your victory. He also gave a divine great bow, armor, arrows, and a sharp Shakti weapon. O mighty lord, ascend this chariot; I will be your charioteer.' Rama circumambulated the chariot, bowed, and ascended. Then an amazing battle ensued. When Ravana launched a fierce trident weapon, Rama tried to stop it with arrows, but they were neutralized. Then Rama used the Shakti weapon sent by Indra, which neutralized Ravana's trident. Thus Indra helped Rama appropriately.

**Key entities:** Rama, Ravana, Indra

#### Q5

**Question:** When the battle between Rama and Ravana became intense, why did Ravana's charioteer turn the chariot aside? What explanation did he give to Ravana?

**Answer:** Ravana, wounded by Rama, became furious and struck Rama severely. Then Rama rained arrows on Ravana. Rama's skill and valor doubled. Noticing this, Rama struck Ravana fiercely. Ravana, battered by the monkeys' stone attacks and Rama's arrows, became mentally disturbed and could not counter effectively. Even when he tried to shoot arrows patiently, they were useless as his end neared. Seeing Ravana's plight, his charioteer cautiously and slowly turned the chariot aside. When Ravana became angry, the charioteer said, 'Lord, the horses are thirsty. I noticed you need some rest, so I turned the chariot aside. That is all. Now, as you command, I will place the chariot before Rama.' And he did so.

**Key entities:** Rama, Ravana

### Chapter 95: Ninety-fifth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 107-111
- Source PDF pages: 235, 236, 237, 238
- Printed page numbers: 239, 240, 241, 242
- Key entities: Rama, Ravana, Agastya, Shiva, Narayana, Kausalya, Sugriva, Vibhishana, Lakshmana
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** The chapter describes the intense battle between Rama and Ravana. Sage Agastya advises Rama to worship the Aditya Hridaya mantra. Matali positions the chariot to the right of Ravana's chariot. Rama beheads Ravana multiple times, but heads regrow. Matali reminds Rama of the Brahmastra, which Rama then uses to kill Ravana. The gods and allies rejoice.

#### Q1

**Question:** Seeing Sri Rama, who was tired from fighting, along with the gods in the sky, Sage Agastya, desiring Rama's victory, taught him which mantra and told him to worship it?

**Options:**
- 1. Shiva mantra
- 2. Narayana mantra
- 3. Aditya Hridaya mantra
- 4. Narasimha mantra

**Correct answer:** Aditya Hridaya mantra

**Key entities:** Rama, Agastya

#### Q2

**Question:** Seeing Ravana returning ready for battle, Matali, as per Sri Rama's instruction, moved his chariot to which side of Ravana's chariot and stopped?

**Options:**
- 1. Right side
- 2. Left side
- 3. Rear side
- 4. Far away

**Correct answer:** Right side

**Key entities:** Ravana, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** During the intense phase of the Rama-Ravana battle, was the series of weapons they were using physical or illusory?

**Answer:** Illusory

**Key entities:** Rama, Ravana

#### Q4

**Question:** Why did Sri Rama fall into deep thought regarding the destruction of Ravana?

**Answer:** Both Rama and Ravana, from their chariots, were provoking each other with anger on the battlefield, intending to kill each other, and their forms were extremely fierce. The monkeys and demons stopped fighting and watched with wide eyes. Thus the Rama-Ravana battle continued incessantly for a day and night. Then Sri Rama, with immense rage, strung a sharp arrow like a great venomous serpent and severed Ravana's head. All the worlds saw Ravana's head, adorned with glittering earrings, fall to the ground. Immediately, another head like that sprouted from Ravana's body. Rama swiftly cut off that head too with another arrow. Immediately, as before, Ravana's head grew back. Then many heads cut by Sri Rama's arrows grew back with equal splendor, so Ravana was not killed. Rama, the joy of Kausalya, was a great hero who knew all weapon applications and possessed many weapons. Yet such Sri Rama fell into deep thought about how to kill that demon king. Charioteer Matali noticed this.

**Key entities:** Rama, Ravana, Kausalya

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the destruction of Ravana take place?

**Answer:** In that Rama-Ravana battle, Rama was only countering Ravana's arrows but not attempting to kill him. Matali thought, 'O descendant of Raghu! Why are you following him like an ignorant person? This one will die at the hands of a human. Therefore, kill him with the Brahmastra that resides in you.' Hearing the charioteer's words, Sri Rama remembered the Brahmastra. Immediately, that great hero took an arrow that hissed like a great serpent and shone with light. Sri Rama, endowed with great strength and valor, duly consecrated it with Vedic mantras, placed that Brahmastra on his bow, drew it to his ear, and released that Brahmastra, capable of severing the vital points, at Ravana. Immediately, that weapon struck Ravana's chest and pierced his heart. The next moment, that weapon, having taken Ravana's life, struck the ground and then, like a humble servant who has completed his duty, returned to Sri Rama's quiver. Then Ravana's bow, along with the arrows in his hand, fell to the ground along with his life. That mighty and radiant demon king, losing his life, fell from his chariot onto the battlefield like Vritrasura killed by the thunderbolt. Then all beings rejoiced. Sugriva, Vibhishana, and Lakshmana, along with their followers, duly worshipped and praised Sri Rama on that battlefield.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Rama, Sugriva, Vibhishana, Lakshmana

### Chapter 96: Ninety-sixth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 112-116
- Source PDF pages: 238, 239, 240
- Printed page numbers: 242, 243, 244
- Key entities: Ravana, Vibhishana, Rama, Mandodari, Hanuman, Sita, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Indra
- Places: Lanka, Ashoka Grove

**Summary:** After Ravana's death, Vibhishana grieves over his brother's body and is consoled by Rama. The women of the harem mourn and rush to the battlefield through the northern gate. Mandodari, Ravana's chief queen, laments. Rama arranges Vibhishana's coronation as king of Lanka. Hanuman visits Sita in Ashoka Vana and conveys Rama's message; Sita expresses her desire to see Rama.

#### Q1

**Question:** Who consoled Vibhishana when he was grieving over his brother Ravana, who was killed by Sri Rama and lying on the ground?

**Options:**
- 1. Lakshmana
- 2. Sugriva
- 3. Hanuman
- 4. Sri Rama

**Correct answer:** Sri Rama

**Key entities:** Vibhishana, Ravana, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Through which gate did all the women of the harem come out, grieving upon hearing the news of Ravana's death, ignoring the people who tried to stop them, to go to the battlefield?

**Options:**
- 1. Southern gate
- 2. Northern gate
- 3. Eastern gate
- 4. Western gate

**Correct answer:** Northern gate

**Key entities:** Ravana

#### Q3

**Question:** Mandodari, who was among the women lamenting upon seeing Ravana's body on the battlefield, was which number wife of Ravana?

**Answer:** First wife

**Key entities:** Mandodari, Ravana

#### Q4

**Question:** In what manner did Sri Rama conduct the coronation of Vibhishana as king of Lanka?

**Answer:** After the war ended, Rama respectfully allowed Matali to take back the chariot sent by Indra. Then Sri Rama embraced Sugriva and granted him the joy of a deep hug. Then, following Soumitri's suggestion, the Lord went with everyone to the military camps. Thereafter, Sri Rama, looking at Lakshmana who was near him, said, 'Brother! Vibhishana is affectionate towards me, a supreme devotee. He greatly helped us in this war. Crown such a virtuous man as king of Lanka.' Thus commanded by Ramachandra, Lakshmana happily entered the city of Lanka with Sugriva and other prominent vanaras, along with Vibhishana. Then Lakshmana selected swift messengers, gave them a golden vessel, and had them bring waters from the oceans. Afterwards, Lakshmana seated Vibhishana on the throne. That royal assembly was filled with Vibhishana's friends and prominent vanaras. Then all the elders, according to Vedic rites, anointed Vibhishana, who was on the throne, with the waters of the seven seas. Then they offered unbroken rice, fried grains, sweetmeats, flowers, and fragrant substances to that lord of rakshasas. By Rama's grace, as per the promise made by Sri Rama, Vibhishana became king of Lanka.

**Key entities:** Rama, Vibhishana, Lanka, Indra, Sugriva, Lakshmana

#### Q5

**Question:** After the war, when Hanuman visited Sita, what kind of message did she send to Sri Rama through Maruti?

**Answer:** As per Sri Rama's command, Maruti entered Lanka and, with Vibhishana's permission, visited Sita in Ashoka Vana. Seeing Hanuman approaching, Sita recognized him as Maruti and was so overjoyed that she could not speak. Then Hanuman, seeing her face radiant with happiness at his arrival, began to convey Rama's message: 'Mother! Vaidehi! Rama and Lakshmana are well. Sugriva, Vibhishana, and all who helped in the war are well. Lord Ramachandra, who killed the tormentor of the world Ravana, asked about your welfare. Mother! I have told you these pleasing words that will give you immense joy. O virtuous lady! It is my fortune that you have preserved your life until now; otherwise this victory of mine would be meaningless. Mother! Why are you still worrying? Why don't you speak to me?' Hearing Hanuman's words, the goddess, with great joy and a choked voice, said, 'Maruti! Hearing the news that my lord and god has achieved victory, I was unable to speak for a moment due to joy.' Then Janaki, standing before Maruti who stood with folded hands, said, 'O venerable one! I will now go to that Lord. Please grant me your message.' Then Janaki said, 'O foremost of vanaras! I wish to see my lord.' Then Hanuman, with her permission, quickly went and stood before Sri Rama.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Rama, Lanka, Vibhishana, Ashoka Grove, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Ravana

### Chapter 97: Ninety-seventh Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 117-121
- Source PDF pages: 240, 241, 242
- Printed page numbers: 244, 245, 246
- Key entities: Vibhishana, Sita, Rama, Brahma, Narayana, Agni, Ravana, Sugriva, Hanuman, Dasharatha
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** Vibhishana brings Sita to Rama in a palanquin. Rama, fearing public opinion, speaks harshly to Sita, who then decides to enter fire. Brahma and other gods appear, revealing Rama's divine nature as Narayana and Sita as Lakshmi. Agni returns Sita unharmed, and Rama accepts her after explaining his actions.

#### Q1

**Question:** How did Vibhishana bring Sita to Rama according to Rama's command?

**Options:**
- 1. Seated on an elephant
- 2. On a chariot
- 3. In a palanquin
- 4. In the Pushpaka Vimana

**Correct answer:** In a palanquin

**Key entities:** Vibhishana, Sita, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** When Rama told Sita, 'You have been seen by Ravana's sinful glances, so I must doubt you. Henceforth you may go anywhere in the ten directions,' what decision did she make?

**Options:**
- 1. To enter fire
- 2. To seek refuge with Vibhishana
- 3. To seek refuge with Sugriva
- 4. To seek refuge with Hanuman

**Correct answer:** To enter fire

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Ravana

#### Q3

**Question:** Out of what fear did Rama speak harsh words to Sita?

**Answer:** Fear of public censure

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita

#### Q4

**Question:** When Sita entered the fire, Brahma appeared and spoke what words?

**Answer:** When Sita entered the fire, hearing the cries of the monkeys and rakshasas, the righteous Rama was very sorrowful, distressed, shedding tears, and fell into thought for a moment. Meanwhile, Brahma and other gods appeared and said, 'Rama! You are the supreme one, foremost among the wise. How can you be indifferent while Sita enters the fire? You are the supreme among all gods, Shri Narayana. You do not realize that.' Then Rama bowed to Brahma and the gods and said, 'As the son of King Dasharatha, as an ordinary human, I think of myself. But who am I? Whose am I? Why have I come? I pray that Brahma explain to me.' Then Brahma said, 'O Rama of true valor! I will tell you the truth, listen. You are Narayana, the cause of the world, endowed with six divine qualities. This Sita is Lakshmi. To slay the tormentor of the worlds, Ravana, you have incarnated as a human on earth. You have established dharma and fulfilled the gods' purpose. By praising you, desired wishes are fulfilled.' Thus Brahma himself told Rama.

**Key entities:** Sita, Brahma, Rama, Narayana, Dasharatha, Ravana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Agni deliver Sita, who had entered the fire, to Rama?

**Answer:** As soon as he heard Brahma's auspicious words, Agni, like a father, brought Sita with him, came up from the fire pit, pushed aside the burning kindling, came out, and stood. Agni handed over that Sita, who had unparalleled beauty and splendor, to Rama. Then Agni, the witness of the world, said, 'O Lord Ramachandra! There is no fault whatsoever in this Vaidehi, your lawful wife. She, with purity in thought, word, and deed, always meditates on you alone. There is no fault in her.' Hearing Agni's words, Rama thought, 'Alas! I have unjustly hurt this noble woman with harsh words,' and shed tears in distress. After thinking for a moment, he said to that best of gods, 'O Havyavahana! There is no fault in Sita. She is pure, but because she stayed for a long time in the shade of the Ashoka tree in Ravana's city, I had to conduct this test so that the three worlds would not doubt her. If I had accepted her without any test to reveal the purity of this Ayonija, people would blame me, saying Dasharatha's Rama is lustful and foolish. I, who am always devoted to truth, remained indifferent while she entered the fire so that all three worlds would believe in Sita's chastity.' Thus Rama took Sita near him and lived happily.

**Key entities:** Agni, Sita, Rama, Brahma, Ravana, Dasharatha

### Chapter 98: Ninety-eighth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 122-126
- Source PDF pages: 242, 243, 244, 245
- Printed page numbers: 246, 247, 248, 249
- Key entities: Rama, Sita, Shiva, Bharata, Vibhishana, Indra, Sugriva, Dasharatha, Narayana, Brahma, Hanuman, Jambavan, Mandodari, Jatayu
- Places: Ayodhya, Lanka, Kishkindha, Rishyamuka, Ganga

**Summary:** After the fire ordeal, Rama accepts Sita. The gods appear, and Shiva shows Rama the divine being in the sky. Rama explains Bharata's vow to Vibhishana. At Rama's request, Indra revives the fallen monkeys. Rama prepares to return to Ayodhya, and Vibhishana offers the Pushpaka Vimana. Rama bids farewell to Sugriva and others, but they insist on accompanying him. They all board the Pushpaka Vimana and depart for Ayodhya. During the journey, Rama points out various landmarks to Sita.

#### Q1

**Question:** Shiva, appearing with all the gods, said, 'Rama! Look at this great person seated in the divine aerial chariot in the sky.' Who is that great person?

**Options:**
- 1. Narayana
- 2. Dasaratha
- 3. Brahma
- 4. Indra

**Correct answer:** Dasaratha

**Key entities:** Shiva, Rama, Dasharatha

#### Q2

**Question:** To whom did Lord Ramachandra explain Bharata's vow?

**Options:**
- 1. Hanuman
- 2. Sugriva
- 3. Vibhishana
- 4. Jambavan

**Correct answer:** Vibhishana

**Key entities:** Bharata, Vibhishana

#### Q3

**Question:** At Sri Rama's request, what did Lord Indra do to the dead monkeys lying on the battlefield?

**Answer:** He revived them (made them alive)

**Key entities:** Rama, Indra

#### Q4
